1201 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Shealy v. Policy Studies, Inc.


No. E2005-01124-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 567


July 17, 2006, Session  
August 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected September 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Bradley County. No. 01-389. Jerri S. Bryant, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of human services (DHS) challenged an order of the Chancery Court for Bradley County holding that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-501 and the pre-January 1, 2005, version of § 36-5-103(f) were unconstitutional in appellee child support child support obligors' action challenging the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-5-103(f) and 36-5-501 on the basis that they violated due process and the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were each paying child support to their respective former spouses, and under §§ 36-5-103(f) and 36-5-501, DHS summarily increased the amount of appellees' child support obligations. Appellees maintained that DHS's ability to summarily issue wage assignments without a hearing violated due process and the separation of powers doctrine. The trial court issued an order restraining DHS from acting on any administrative orders and from collecting any child support payments in excess of the amount appellees had previously been ordered to pay. However prior to the trial court declaring Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(f) unconstitutional, substantial changes to § 36-5-103(f) became effective. As amended, the statute provided for notice and a hearing prior to the issuance of an order increasing or decreasing a child support obligation under § 36-5-103(f)(4) and (f)(5). Therefore, the only relief available to appellees would be a declaration that § 36-5-103(f) as it existed prior to January 1, 2005 was unconstitutional. And such an order would serve no useful purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated, and the cause was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter an order dismissing this case.

 

1202 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mosby v. Colson


No. W2006-00490-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 544


June 6, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
August 14, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 6012. Joseph Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, prison officials and Tennessee Department of Corrections (TDOC) personnel, and denied the inmate leave to amend his complaint. The inmate filed his action pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging that prison officials terminated his prison job in retaliation for his filing grievances against them.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court first held that the inmate's complaint failed to state a claim for violations of the First or Fourteenth Amendments and that the trial court therefore properly dismissed those aspects of his complaint. The court decided that the trial court correctly dismissed the complaint as to a deputy warden and the TDOC's assistant commissioner of operations because the inmate nowhere alleged that they directly participated in the job termination decisions of their subordinates. The court then agreed with the trial court's decision to reject the inmate's amended complaints. The court's independent review of the amended complaints showed that they either suffered from the same deficiencies as the original complaint or constituted actions for which he initially had to seek administrative redress. The court then found that the inmate's alleged need for a preliminary injunction had been abrogated since the inmate's complaint failed to state a claim for which relief could be granted. Finally, the court held that the inmate's action should have been dismissed at the trial level pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-801 et seq., which governed lawsuits filed by inmates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the case to the trial court for the assessment of all costs, expenses, and fees associated with the lawsuit against the inmate in accordance with Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-801 et seq. Thereafter, the trial court was directed to enter an order assessing that amount to the inmate for filing a frivolous lawsuit and appeal.

 

1203 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mills v. Shelby County Election Comm'n


No. W2005-02883-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


218 S.W.3d 33; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 589


June 28, 2006, On-Brief  
August 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mills v. Shelby County Election Comm'n, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1184 (Tenn., Dec. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-05-1565-3. The Honorable D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant voter filed suit against appellee Shelby County, Tennessee, Election Commission (the Commission), under the Tennessee Declaratory Judgment Act asserting that the legislation authorizing the use of electronic voting machines in some jurisdictions violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 5 and Tenn. Const. art. IV, § 1. The Shelby County Chancery Court, Tennessee, dismissed the complaint pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6). The voter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The voter sought to have the trial court declare that the Commission must use a system of voter verified, tangible paper ballots that were capable of being placed by the voters into an appropriate ballot box for later tabulation. The voter's primary concern was that, without a paper ballot or paper record of his vote, there could be no meaningful recount in a questionable election outcome, nor could there be a meaningful election contest if one became necessary, and that consequently, his voting rights were diminished when compared with other citizens of Tennessee who received a paper ballot of record. The appellate court ruled that even if it were to concede that paperless voting could disenfranchise voters under certain circumstances, there was no indication in the complaint that voters were presently being disenfranchised by the current voting system. In short, the voter's allegations appeared to be based on conjecture and not upon actual events. The voter presented a theoretical question of what could happen in future elections, which did not rise to the level of a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1204 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re S.M.N.


No. E2005-01974-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 445


May 22, 2006, Session  
June 30, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. No. 62153. Cynthia Chapman, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Knox County, Tennessee, terminated the parental rights of appellant father to his minor child upon finding, by clear and convincing evidence, that the father abandoned his child and that termination of the father's parental rights was in the child's best interest. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(f)(3) was unconstitutional in that it gave trial courts the discretion to determine whether a prisoner was entitled to be physically present in the courtroom during a proceeding involving the termination of the prisoner's parental rights. The appellate court noted that the father failed to give proper notice to the attorney general that he planned to challenge the constitutionality of a state statute. Thus, the appellate court could not address the constitutional issue on appeal. The father had meaningful access to court by way of his participation in the trial via telephone and there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's decision to proceed with the trial. Appellee relatives alleged an applicable ground of abandonment and the parties proceeded to try the case with the implicit understanding that the relatives were attempting to prove that the father had abandoned the child in the four months preceding his incarceration. The evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that the father's visitation and support of the child did not even rise to the level of token visitation or support.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1205 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Marceaux v. Thompson


NO. E2004-01390-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


212 S.W.3d 263; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 426


May 23, 2006, Session  
June 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Marceaux v. Thompson, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1068 (Tenn., Nov. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] TENN. R. APP. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Cause Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Cumberland county. No. 9053-1-04. Vernon Neal, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Cumberland County, Tennessee, dismissed appellant citizen's complaint against appellees, various Cumberland County officials and local media, upon motions to dismiss and motion for summary judgment. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen had complained of the conduct of routine traffic stops by the officials and that the media had failed to inform the public of the occurrence of these stops and of the alleged illegality of same. The citizen argued that the trial court erred in dismissing his complaint against the county officials and local media for failure to state a claim upon which relief may be granted. The appellate court found that there was no authority that supported the citizen's argument that the media was legally obligated to publish or broadcast news chosen by the citizen, and decisions regarding the decision as to what information would be published or broadcast was left to the media owners and editors. The citizen's complaint against various county officials consisted of a series of rambling criticisms - none of which set forth a cause of action against the officials or the government that they served.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1206 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Interstate Mktg. Corp. v. Equip. Servs.


No. M2005-00208-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 383


March 29, 2006, Session  
June 6, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-1252-III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee manufacturer contracted with appellant sales representative company in 1980. In 1994 they entered a new contract. Modifications were made in 2001. In 2002 the manufacturer terminated the contract. The company filed suit. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed the company's action upon determining the contract was governed by former Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1301 et seq., as it existed in 1991. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company prayed for damages of $ 5,000,000, costs, and attorney's fees under Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1311(a). The trial court found that the 1991 version of the statute did not provide redress for the damages allegedly suffered by the company. The issue on appeal was whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-1301 et seq., as amended in 1999, applied to the contract originally executed by the parties in 1994. The appellate court disagreed with the trial court that the additional modifications of sales quota in the contract in 2001 were not material. The 2001 modification established a probationary period and the curative policy modified the termination provisions of the 1994 agreement. The 2001 modification altered the termination rights provision of the contract and significantly and materially affected the parties' rights under the contract. In light of the parties' rights and obligations under the contract, and in light of the intervening amendments to § 47-25-1301 et seq., in 1999, which, inter alia, prohibited termination without cause, the instant modification of termination rights was material. That modification was sufficiently material to have resulted in a new contract.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the manufacturer.

 

1207 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Rodgers v. Rodgers


No. M2004-02046-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 328


July 15, 2005, Session  
May 17, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County. No. 02-5326DR. Royce Taylor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father was ordered to pay $ 375 per month in child support. Appellant department of human services issued an ex parte order attempting to require the father's employer to deduct child support from his salary. The father filed a petition requesting the Chancery Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee) to vacate the department's orders and to enjoin the department from issuing further orders or to otherwise modify the final divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued a temporary restraining order and, following a hearing, vacated the department's orders with regard to the father's child support and enjoined the mother from further attempts to collect child support without first seeking relief from the court. The court also dismissed the department on the ground that it was not a proper party, and then denied the motion of the attorney general to intervene to defend the constitutionality of the department's administrative child support enforcement procedures. The department and the attorney general appealed. The substantive dispute in the instant case involved the payment of child support. The mother claimed that the father had not paid any of the child support ordered by the court, while the father asserted that he had provided support of the parties' child in excess of the amount the mother claimed was past due. While the instant appeal was pending, the father and the mother compromised and settled their child support dispute. Thus, the courts could no longer grant any sort of meaningful relief to the mother. Therefore, the substantive issue regarding the father's obligation to pay back child support was moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to dismiss the father's petition challenging the constitutionality of a statute. The costs were taxed in equal proportions to the father and the State.

 

1208 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Lanthorn v. Sobieski, Messer & Assocs.


No. E2005-01850-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 254


January 31, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
April 20, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Washington County. No. 9085. Thomas J. Seeley, Jr., Judge.
Ellis v. Washington County, 198 F.3d 225, 1999 U.S. App. LEXIS 30713 (6th Cir.), 1999 FED App. 396P (6th Cir.) (6th Cir. Tenn., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Washington County, Tennessee, denied plaintiff client's motion to recuse in her legal malpractice action against defendants, her former attorneys. The client argued that the judge presiding over the trial court was the same judge who had earlier dismissed her wrongful death case. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client argued that the trial court judge abused his discretion in refusing to recuse himself on the basis of his presiding over the underlying wrongful death action. The appellate court found that the judge's involvement in the underlying litigation would not disqualify him from hearing the legal malpractice action. His dismissal of the wrongful death action did not address, expressly or by implication, whether the dismissal was proximately caused by or even remotely associated with any act of legal malpractice on the part of the attorneys in the instant case. The wrongful death suit was, in the judge's opinion, time-barred without regard to whether the client's lawyers in that case had pursued their representation in keeping with the applicable standard of care or not. No reasonable person could question the judge's impartiality in hearing the instant litigation simply because he ruled, as a matter of law, that the underlying suit was filed outside the period of the applicable statute of limitations. There was no conceivable subject that would require the judge to trade his seat on the bench for a seat on the witness stand. The attorneys' issues were without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1209 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Saturn Corp. v. Johnson


No. M2004-02067-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


197 S.W.3d 273; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 252


October 14, 2005, Session  
April 18, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-2684-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee revenue commissioner in the taxpayer's action seeking a refund of a percentage of franchise and excise taxes paid in fiscal year 1999-2000 pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-4-217(b) (Supp. 2005).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that because the premium tax credits allowed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-4-217(a) applied to workers' compensation self-insurers, the franchise and excise tax credits allowed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-4-217(b) applied to self insurers as well. The court held that although a tax credit was allowed under § 56-4-217(a) for premium taxes paid by self-insurers, the tax credit for franchise taxes under § 56-4-217(b) did not apply to self insurers because § 56-4-217(b) was added to the statute at the same time and in conjunction with § 56-4-217(c), which restricted its application to insurance companies as defined in Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-1-102(2); thus the credit described in § 56-4-217(b) was also restricted to insurance companies and did not apply to the taxpayer as a self-insurer. The court rejected the taxpayer's equal protection claims because the classification of insurance companies versus self-insurers rested rest upon a reasonable basis. The court held that alleviating the effects of retaliatory taxation by other states to the disadvantage of Tennessee's domestic insurance companies standing alone was a sufficient basis to withstand equal protection scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and remanded the case for any necessary further proceedings.

 

1210 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Crull v. Crull


No. E2005-01430-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 201


November 17, 2005, Session  
March 27, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Vacated in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 95844-3. Sharon Bell, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Vacated in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, held that the language of a divorce decree mandated that appellee wife was entitled, without limitation, to one-half of appellant husband's retirement benefits. The trial court found that the husband's retirement, when it happened, would constitute a change in circumstances. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the wife's entitlement with respect to the retirement benefits should be limited to a share of the benefits that accrued before the divorce. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's interpretation of the divorce decree because, simply stated, the wife was entitled, without limitation, to half of the husband's retirement. The issue before the appellate court was the intention of the court as gathered from all of the judgment. The issue was not what the court should have intended. The addition of the limiting language sought by the husband would change the meaning of the judgment as it pertained to the annuity plan. The doctrine of res judicata precluded the appellate court from going behind the final judgment to test whether the trial court erred, factually or legally, in awarding the wife, without limitation, one-half of the husband's retirement benefits. The husband had ample options available to him at a much earlier time to correct any errors. The trial court could not examine the totality of the circumstances surrounding the husband's retirement to ensure that it was objectively reasonable as he had not retired or set a date for retirement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed except the judgment regarding whether the husband's retirement constituted a change in circumstances was vacated.

 

1211 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Harvey v. LaDuke


No. E2005-00533-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 187


February 10, 2006, Session  
March 20, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 3-270-04. Wheeler Rosenbalm, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment to appellees, a judicial commissioner, a county, and a surety, in an action seeking relief from a failure to issue a Tenn. R. Crim. P. 4(a) criminal summons. The complaint sought mandamus relief, a declaratory judgment, and alleged a failure/neglect to perform duties and malicious harassment.


OVERVIEW: The owner contended that several law enforcement officers trespassed on his property and assaulted him. He went to the judicial commissioner in an attempt to obtain a criminal summons. The judicial commissioner refused to issue such, citing Knox County, Tenn., Gen. Sess. Ct. R. 20 and Knox County, Tenn., Gen. Sess. Ct. R. 25. Summary judgment was granted, and the owner sought review. On appeal, the reviewing court determined that, based on the clear language of Tenn. R. Crim. P. 4(a), a police report was not a prerequisite to the issuance of a criminal summons. Due to the conflict with Rule 4(a), Knox County, Tenn., Gen. Sess. Ct. R. 20 was invalid. Next, the appellate court held that there was no cause of action under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-701 because the owner was unable to show that the actions were based on discrimination. The Tennessee Court of the Judiciary was vested with the authority to hear the claims relating to the neglect of duty under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-101. Finally, the judicial commissioner was immune from liability under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-38-102, and there was no authority for the recovery of damages under Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 35.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination relating to the validity of a local rule. The rest of the decision was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1212 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Ben. Tenn., Inc. v. Metro. Gov't


No. M2004-01071-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 164


September 14, 2005, Session  
March 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Benefit Tenn., Inc. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 811 (Tenn., Sept. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-801-III. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee lienholder filed suit against appellant county seeking damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging the county failed to provide adequate notice to it of the delinquent taxes and scheduled tax sale in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2502 and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) held that due process required certified mail. The County appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county did not dispute that the lienholder's interest was a protected property interest that could not be disturbed absent due process of law under the Fourteenth Amendment. The issue was whether the county was required by due process to notify lienholders by certified mail, as opposed to regular mail, that it was preparing to sell the secured property to collect delinquent taxes. The appellate court held that even though certified mail might have been "better" notice and the county might elect to use that notice in the future, constitutional due process did not require the adoption of other, more expensive delivery methods, and the county's practice of sending notice to lien holders of a tax sale by regular mail did not violate due process. The U.S. Supreme Court in Mennonite found regular mail was a sufficient means to provide lienholders notice of a tax sale. The fact that the lienholder did not receive the notice in the instant case did not nullify the efficacy of the use of regular mail. The Supreme Court in Mullane recognized that in order to meet minimum due process, the method of notice did not have to be fail proof since constitutional law had to take some chances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. Costs were assessed against the lienholder.

 

1213 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. La Selva v. Ziomek


No. E2005-00542-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 112


February 8, 2006, Session  
February 23, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sevier County. No. 01-CS80. Ben W. Hooper, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Sevier County (Tennessee) held that a child support judgment entered by a Canadian court was entitled to registration, but was not entitled to enforcement in Tennessee pursuant to the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-2001 et seq. The circuit court ordered appellee father to pay significantly less than the amount previously ordered by the Canadian court. Appellant State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judgment entered by the Canadian court set the father's child support obligation based on an annual income of $ 250,000. The Canadian court stated that had he properly disclosed his income in 1997, the table amount under the guidelines on income of $ 250,000 was $ 2,801 per month. In accordance with Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-2611, the circuit court was without subject matter jurisdiction to modify the Canadian child support judgment. The father claimed that the circuit court really did not modify the Canadian judgment, but rather enforced that judgment only to the extent that the father actually could pay the support, i.e., $ 500 or $ 600 per month. The appellate court was at a loss as to how the circuit court's holding that the father should pay only $ 500 to $ 600 per month in child support could be deemed anything other than a direct modification of the Canadian judgment, which both parties and the circuit court agreed the circuit court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to do. The appellate court also held that the father failed to prove the existence of any defense to the registration or the enforcement of the child support order issued by the Canadian court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed insofar as it registered the judgment of the Canadian court. The judgment which concluded that the Canadian judgment was not entitled to enforcement and that the father should be ordered to pay only $ 500 to $ 600 per month was reversed. On remand, inter alia, the court was to enforce the judgment of the Canadian court and determine the amount of arrearages since the entry of the Canadian judgment.

 

1214 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Tipton v. City of Knoxville


No. E2004-01359-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


205 S.W.3d 456; 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 29


November 14, 2005, Session  
January 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State ex rel. Tipton v. City of Knoxville, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 922 (Tenn., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 152487-2. Hon. Daryl R. Fansler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a decision of the Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, which in a quo warranto action voided the city's ordinance annexing plaintiff landowners' real estate.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the landowners could choose to either prove that the ordinance was unreasonable or they could prove that material retardation would not occur in the absence of annexation. The trial court found that the landowners carried their burden of proof of the latter under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-58-111(a). The court reversed and held that under § 6-58-111(a)(2), the landowners were required to prove that annexation would not materially benefit the welfare of the citizens and property owners of the city and the affected territory. The evidence established the territory would materially benefit from annexation in that the territory would gain better city services. The city would benefit as well given that the territory was an enclave surrounded by the city and there was confusion regarding the extent of city services in the area. It followed that the failure to annex the would materially retard the welfare of the citizens and property owners of the city and territory. The court also held that because § 6-58-111(b) was not an attempt to create a rule that applied only to one or a few chosen local governments, it did not violate Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

1215 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hassler v. Tenn. Dep't of Safety


No. M2003-02927-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 21


March 7, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
January 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hassler v. Tenn. Dep't of Safety, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 469 (Tenn., May 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 03C958. Hamilton Gayden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, upheld a decision of an administrative law judge (ALJ) for appellee, the Tennessee Department of Safety, which concluded that vehicles and cash allegedly owned by appellant, a father, were subject to forfeiture pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 53-11-451(a)(6)(A) (2005). The father, whose son had attempted to purchase a quantity of cocaine, sought review.


OVERVIEW: The record showed the father agreed to help his son, who had a record of drug offenses, start his own car business. While the father provided some start up money, the small dealership (in the father's name) was run by said son on a day to day basis. While the son was operating the dealership, an undercover informant arranged to sell him a large quantity of cocaine. The ALJ determined the father failed to demonstrate any legal interest in the cash or any ownership of the 33 vehicles that were seized (pursuant to forfeiture warrants from the Circuit Court for Wilson County). The appellate court rejected the father's argument that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-33-204 (2003), which permitted any state judge to issue a forfeiture warrant even when the property was not located within the judge's jurisdiction, violated Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8. The father presented no authority for the notion that a court of record could not constitutionally issue a warrant for the forfeiture of property that was not located in its judicial district. In addition, he presented no evidence that he experienced any difficulty in obtaining the information required to be kept by Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-33-204(b) (2003).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Sentinel Trust Co. v. Lavender (In re Sentinel Trust Co.)


Nos.: M2005-00031-COA-R3-CV, M2005-01773-COA-R3-CV, No. M2005-01073-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


206 S.W.3d 501; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 841


November 17, 2005, Session  
December 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Sentinel Trust Co., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 612 (Tenn., July 3, 2006)
Appeal denied by In re Sentinel Trust Co., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 613 (Tenn., July 3, 2006)
Appeal denied by Sentinel Trust Co. v. Lavender, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 614 (Tenn., July 3, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sentinel Trust Co. v. Lavender, 127 S. Ct. 566, 166 L. Ed. 2d 412, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8410 (U.S., 2006)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by In re Sentinel Trust Co., 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 260 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Trial Courts Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Lewis County. No. 4781. The Honorable R. E. Lee Davies, Chancellor. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-1934-I. The Honorable Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Courts Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trust company challenged decisions of the Chancery Courts for Davidson County and Lewis County (Tennessee), which denied its petition for supersedeas and dismissed the writ of certiorari in an action filed by the trust company after appellee Commissioner of the Tennessee Department of Financial Institutions took emergency possession of the company under Tenn. Code Ann. § 45-2-1502 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The company had no written policies for its trust administration department and the sole shareholder had virtually no oversight. When it was determined that the company had a deficit fiduciary cash position of over $ 7 million, and the company failed to prepare a capital plan as ordered, the Commissioner took emergency possession. The court held that § 45-2-1502 did not violate the separation of powers provision of Tenn. Const. art. II, § 2, because the Commissioner's powers were limited to the judicial powers reasonably necessary to the accomplishment of the purposes of the Department. Also, it was clear that the Tennessee Banking Act applied to trust companies from the language of Tenn. Code Ann. § 45-1-124(b) and (d). Given the shareholder's admissions of the deficit, there was ample evidence that the company was being run in an unsound manner and further, material evidence existed to support the decision to take emergency possession. The evidence of an admitted multi-million dollar fiduciary cash deficiency, the company's poor earning performance, operation at a net loss, and no plan to eliminate the deficiencies, provided a sound basis for the liquidation of the company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the trial courts.

 

1217 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Davenport v. Adair


No. E2004-01505-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 821


June 14, 2005, Session  
December 27, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Probate and Family Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Probate and Family Court for Cumberland County. No. 14260. Steven C. Douglas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Probate and Family Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an elderly resident and her purported attorney-in-fact, challenged a decision of the Probate and Family Court for Cumberland County, Tennessee, which ruled that two powers of attorney were void, and appointed a public guardian to serve as the resident's conservator. The action was brought by appellees, the resident's nieces, alleging that the resident suffered from dementia.


OVERVIEW: In 1996, the resident executed a purported durable power of attorney to a lawyer and to the lawyer's wife should the lawyer become incapacitated. She also appointed the lawyer as co-trustee over an inter vivos trust and named the wife as the successor trustee. The probate court held that the 1996 document was not properly executed, and appellants subsequently executed a second power of attorney, which the probate court held was invalid due to the resident's disability. The court held that the probate court erred in admitting a medical report from a court-appointed physician because it was hearsay in that nowhere in Tenn. Code Ann. § 34-3-105(a) (2003) did the legislature direct that the report be admitted without being tested by the evidentiary rules. However, the other testimony from lay witnesses was sufficient to show the resident's mental incapacity, such as the resident offering her yard person $800 to cut her yard, and her talk of people living in her basement. The court agreed that the two powers of attorney were invalid. Also, the trial court properly appointed a public guardian as conservator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the probate court's evidentiary ruling regarding admission of the medical report, but the error did not require remand. The court otherwise affirmed the orders of the probate court.

Westchester Co., LLC v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville


No. M2004-02391-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 798


October 10, 2005, Session  
December 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 03C-2002. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a zoning dispute, the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, issued a declaratory judgment in favor of defendant, the Metropolitan Government of Nashville and Davidson County (Metro), Tennessee, that plaintiff landowner did not have vested right in a previous zoning classification. The plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Metro rezoned property owned by the plaintiff from multi-family to single-family. As a result of the zoning change, plaintiff was unable to carry through with its contract to sell the property to a third party for the development of multi-family town houses. The plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment as to whether it had a vested right in the previous zoning classification. The trial court ruled in favor of Metro and dismissed the plaintiff's claims. The facts did not establish a vested right in the previous zone. The plaintiff had not yet incurred substantial liabilities relating directly to construction. Estoppel did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1219 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


City of Clarksville v. Dixon


No. M2004-01656-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 803


August 15, 2005, Session  
December 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. Nos. 50300483 and 50300535. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee individuals filed petitions alleging that a city court violated the $ 50 fine clause in Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14. The Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) denied appellant city's motion to quash the petitions and held, inter alia, that the fines were unconstitutional and the prospective application of Chattanooga v. Davis, and the doctrine of res judicata did not bar them from contesting the judgments. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the individuals' use of petitions for writ of certiorari were used impermissibly as a substitute for appeal, that the issues raised by them were barred by the doctrine of res judicata, and that the Tennessee Supreme Court's decision in Davis v. City of Chattanooga, applied prospectively and, thus, did not apply to the instant penalties, and that the city court's collection of the fines in chronological order was against public policy. Inter alia, the appellate court held that the individuals were attempting to render the amount of the fines imposed by the city's ordinances unconstitutional and in violation of art. VI, § 14. Thus, the circuit court's grant of the petition for writ of certiorari and its denial of the city's motion to quash the petitions were not an abuse of discretion. The individuals were not trying to re-litigate the issues when they petitioned for writ of certiorari. Rather, they sought relief from a void judgment of an inferior tribunal that exceeded its jurisdiction by rendering fines over $ 50 in violation of art. VI, § 14. Thus, the doctrine of res judicata did not bar the petitions for writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part and the case was remanded for further proceedings. Costs of the appeal were taxed equally to the city and to the individuals.

Club Sys. of Tenn., Inc. v. YMCA of Middle Tenn.


No. M2004-01966-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 793


November 15, 2005, Session  
December 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Club Sys. of Tenn. v. YMCA of Middle Tenn., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 565 (Tenn., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed in Part, Affirmed in Part, and Remanded. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 03-1102-1 (IV). The Honorable Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed in Part, Affirmed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group of for-profit health club owners, challenged the constitutionality and application of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-225, which provided for a real and personal property tax exemption for family wellness centers and the ruling by the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, that appellee Christian-based health club and family center satisfied the criteria of § 67-5-225.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of § 67-5-225, which provided that the real and personal property of a nonprofit family wellness center would be exempt from property taxes as a charitable use of property if the center was owned and operated by an I.R.C. § 501c(3) charitable organization. The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of the statute on its face as the classification for fitness centers contained in the statute was reasonably related to the expressed public policy to provide for the physical health and social well-being of citizens, and the statute did not violate Tenn. Const. art. II, § 28, as under the statute the property had to be used to further the purposes of a tax exempt organization. Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-225 was also constitutional as applied because the property was being used in a purely charitable manner. The appellate court reversed the trial court's ruling as to whether one of appellee's facilities met the requirements of § 67-5-225, as there was a question as to whether that particular facility provided access to children.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of the statute, but remanded the matter to determine if one of appellee's facilities met the requirements set forth in the statute.

 

1221 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Guerra v. State


No. M2004-02559-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 777


October 11, 2005, Session  
December 6, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed; Cause Remanded. Appeal from the Claims Commission for the State of Tennessee, Davidson County. No. 20201057. Stephanie Reevers, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners filed a complaint with the Tennessee Claims Commission against the State of Tennessee for an alleged unconstitutional taking of their property in connection with the State's issuance of a permit to the homeowners to install a subsurface sewage disposal system. The Commission ruled in favor of the State, finding among other things that the homeowners' claim was time barred. The homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the homeowners' suit was timely filed. The applicable statute of limitations allowed a landowner one year within which to commence an action for taking of land after the landowner realized or reasonably should have realized that their property had sustained an injury that was permanent. The homeowners contended they did not realize that they had suffered permanent injury until the State eliminated the possibility that the injury to their property could be resolved. The Commission concluded that an Administrative Law Judge's final order reasonably should have put them on notice that any taking of their property by reason of the denial of their permit was permanent. They were therefore required to exercise due diligence to ascertain the pertinent facts within one year of this occurrence and to initiate suit. The proof demonstrated that they did not do so and therefore the Commission concluded the claim should be dismissed as time barred. The evidence did not preponderate against the finding of the Commission that the homeowners did not exercise due diligence to ascertain the pertinent facts within one year of the order of the administrative law judge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Baker v. He (In re A.M.H.)


No. W2004-01225-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 736


February 16, 2005, Session  
November 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by In re A.M.H., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 316 (Tenn., Apr. 24, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Adoption of A.M.H., 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 13 (Tenn., Jan. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-01-1302-3-III. Robert L. Childers, Chancellor By Designation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) that terminated their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: At the conclusion of a three month foster care period, the biological parents agreed to the transferring of custody of the child to appellees foster parents. The biological parents continued limited visitation with the child but paid no child support. The biological parents argued, inter alia, that termination was not in the child's best interests. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court concluded that the child had developed a strong psychological and emotional attachment to the foster parents, and that removal of the child from them would cause substantial harm to the child. The foster parents provided a stable, loving environment for such a length of time that removal of the child would cause substantial harm. The continuation of a parent-child relationship between the child and the biological parents would diminish the child's chances of early integration into a permanent home. The trial court also concluded that there was misconduct, that the biological parents were unfit, and that they were of questionable character as evidenced by their defiance to legal authority and untruthful statements over the course of events giving rise to the appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment that the parents willfully failed to support the child for four months immediately preceding the petition to terminate parental rights was reversed. The judgment was reversed as to the trial court's finding that at the time the petition was filed, the father was not the legal parent or guardian of the child. The court erred in finding that Tenn. Code Ann. 36-1-113(g)(3)(A) did not apply. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Bailey v. County of Shelby


No. W2005-01508-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 725


September 20, 2005, Session  
November 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Bailey v. County of Shelby, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 141 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)
Reversed by Bailey v. County of Shelby, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 208 (Tenn., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-04-0550-3. D.J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, elected members of the county board of commissioners, challenged a decision of the Chancery Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, the county and the county election commission, in appellants' action seeking a declaration that term limits on their board seats under Shelby County, Tenn., Charter art. II, § 2.03(G) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were candidates for the board, and under Shelby County, Tenn., Charter art. II, § 2.03(G), they were ineligible to be elected when there current terms expired. The trial court held that § 2.03 (G) was not invalid under Tenn. Const. art. VII, § 1. The court held that the plural "terms" in art. VII did not mandate that each officer should be entitled to be elected to more than one term and that Shelby County, Tenn., Charter art. II, § 2.03(G) did not violate Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210. The court reversed, though, and held that a plain reading of § 5-1-210(12) compelled the conclusion that county governments must include the constitutional officers prescribed by Tenn. Const. art. VII. Also, nothing in art. VII supported the proposition that the General Assembly's duty to prescribe the qualifications of constitutional officers was not mandatory or that the General Assembly could delegate the authority. Because art. VII, § 1, para. 3 could not be read as a stand-alone provision, members of board were constitutional officers, and the court elided the phrase "qualifications for holding office" from Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210(4).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and awarded summary judgment to appellants. The court enjoined the county from enforcing the charter provision at issue.

In re Marr


No. M2005-01119-COA-R3-PT


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


194 S.W.3d 490; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 716


October 12, 2005, Session  
November 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re S.A.M., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 348 (Tenn., May 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Williamson County. No. 45935. Lonnie R. Hoover, Judge.
Osborn v. Marr, 127 S.W.3d 737, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 45 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother and her husband filed a second petition in the Juvenile Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) to terminate appellant incarcerated biological father's parental rights. The petition was based solely on the ground for termination in Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(6) and the claim that terminating the father's parental rights was in the child's best interests. The trial court granted the termination petition. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father asserted that many of the factors in § 36-1-113(i) for determining a child's best interests did not apply to him because he was incarcerated and that the court placed undue weight on his failure to support the child financially. All or virtually all of the statutory factors weighed in favor of terminating the father's parental rights. He lived in a prison, continued to use illegal drugs, and had amassed a record of 14 disciplinary violations while incarcerated. He had not seen the child in well over five years, had made no more than token efforts to establish a relationship with the child during that time, and had paid far less to support his child than he could have even given his meager resources. The fact that he decided to conceive a child at a time when he knew he was facing almost certain conviction for a heinous crime and would therefore most likely be unavailable to support or care for the child for a large portion of the child's early life spoke volumes about his lack of a sustained commitment to the child. By contrast, the husband had demonstrated his commitment to the welfare and long-term well being of the child through years of concrete action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the father.

Hooker v. Bredesen


No. M2004-02185-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 668


September 13, 2005, Session  
October 25, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 04-405-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Because of appellee's numerous suits regarding the constitutionality of out-of-state contributions to political campaigns, a special master was to review his fillings and determine if they should proceed. The special master determined that the instant case could proceed. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granted a motion to dismiss but denied the imposition of Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11 sanctions. Appellant attorney general appealed.


OVERVIEW: The "fail-safe" order specified that the special master had to determine whether appellee's new lawsuits were frivolous or duplicative of other lawsuits previously filed by him. The difficulty with faulting the chancellor for refusing to impose sanctions was that it was plain from the special master's report that after reciting both the provision regarding Tenn. Const. art. X, § 3 together with Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-19-126 and the provision relative to legally frivolous or duplicative lawsuits, the special master specifically ruled only on the constitutional and statutory provisions without addressing the issue of frivolous or duplicative matters. No party appealed the action of the special master. If the attorney general was dissatisfied with the report of the special master, the remedy was to appeal to the Chancellor or the Presiding Judge of Davidson County State Trial Courts. Having failed to do so, he now sought to hold the chancellor to an abuse of discretion for refusing to impose sanctions regardless of the "fail-safe" mechanism. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, at Nashville was not prepared under those circumstances to hold that the chancellor abused her discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancellor was in all respects affirmed with costs assessed to the attorney general.

 

1226 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hargrove v. State


No. M2004-00410-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 585


August 16, 2005, Session  
September 15, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 03-1197-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a decision by an administrative law judge, an automobile belonging to appellee motorist was forfeited, after notice and hearing, for a violation of the driving under the influence of an intoxicant (DUI) law. However, for undisclosed reasons, an order nolle prosequi was later entered. The motorist sought review, and the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, reversed the forfeiture. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The chancery court held that a conviction for DUI was a prerequisite to a forfeiture under Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-403(k). On appeal, the State (the Tennessee Commissioner of the Department of Safety) presented for review the issues of: (1) whether a conviction for DUI was a condition precedent to a forfeiture of the vehicle, and (2) whether an administrative finding that a driver had violated the DUI statute unconstitutionally infringed upon the driver's right to a trial on the DUI offense. Examining the relevant statutory language and legislative history, the appellate court held that a conviction for driving under the influence of an intoxicant (DUI) was not a prerequisite to a forfeiture of a vehicle under § 55-10-403(k). Secondly, the matter involved a civil proceeding, requiring a preponderance of the proof as opposed to proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court concluded that the various statutory schemes, and the various statutes, clearly revealed the legislative intent to authorize forfeiture even in cases where the party was found innocent of the offense giving rise to the forfeiture action, an in rem proceeding against the property only.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded to the administrative agency. Costs were assessed to the motorist.

City of Humboldt v. McKnight


No. M2002-02639-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 540


April 13, 2004, Argued  
August 25, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by City of Humboldt v. McKnight, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 157 (Tenn., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 99-466-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county and Gibson County Special School District (GCSSD), challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court, Davidson County (Tennessee) that granted summary judgment in part for appellees, city and its officials, holding that the county was obligated to operate a county school system and to levy a countywide property tax for schools, and that 2002 Tenn. Pub. Acts 770 (codified as Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-2-501(b)(2)(C)) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county ceased operating schools because all of its students were served by the GCSSD or other special districts. The city claimed the county had a constitutional and statutory duty to oversee education in the county, operate a school system, and levy a countywide property tax to fund schools, and that its failure to do so resulted in an unequal educational opportunity to county students in violation of Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 12. The trial court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-1-102 placed a duty on the county to operate a school system and that Tenn. Code Ann. § 49-2-501(b)(2)(C), which stated that the county was not required to operate a separate county school system, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that § 49-2-501(b)(2)(C) was constitutional because it was not special legislation and it was rationally related to legitimate legislative interests. The court held that the county was not required to operate a school system or to levy a countywide property tax because the legislature had wide discretion in establishing its education system and it was not shown that the method used to raise revenue for schools had resulted in unequal educational opportunities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment.

Ashley v. Jones


No. M2003-02411-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 529


October 1, 2004, Session  
August 24, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County. No. 98DR-82. J. S. Daniel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee), which dismissed her complaint against appellee father regarding the modification of his child support obligation.


OVERVIEW: The father was ordered to pay weekly child support. After the father was laid off, he asked the Tennessee Department of Human Services to lower his obligation. The Department granted the request under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(f) (repealed January 1, 2005). The mother then filed a complaint, which alleged that the Department had taken away her property right without due process of law. The complaint was dismissed, and the mother sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the former version of § 36-5-103 did not have a requirement of notice of a request for modification to the affected party, notice of a proposed adjustment, or the opportunity to object and be heard before the modification became effective. As such, the court held that this procedure violated the Fourteenth Amendment and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8. At the very least, the court found that the agency was not permitted to unilaterally reduce child support without pre-deprivation notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court noted that the amended version of § 36-5-103 ensured pre-deprivation due process. Finally, the court declined to consider the mother's remaining constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the modification of support order was declared void. The case was remanded to the trial court for a determination of the appropriate amount to compensate the mother for the temporary loss of support.

State ex rel. Dean v. Vanhorn


No. M2002-01969-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 476


November 4, 2003, Session  
August 10, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 3237. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city filed suit in the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, seeking to enjoin the operation of a brothel on appellant property owner's land and requiring it to post a $ 20,000 bond to assure compliance with the injunction. The trial court granted the city its requested relief. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's predecessors in interest were the original parties to the abatement proceedings. During the pendency of those proceedings, the property was conveyed to the property owner. The property owner agreed to permit the city to remove all items on the premises that were used for the purpose of maintaining a brothel and to permit the entry of a permanent injunction against operating a brothel on the premises, but the city insisted on a $ 20,000 surety bond to assure compliance with the injunction. The property owner appealed the portion of the trial court's order requiring it to post a bond to assure continued compliance with the abatement order. The appellate court held that contrary to the trial court's belief that the bond requirement did not restrict the property owner's lawful use of its property, the requirement of posting a bond effectively deprived it of all economically beneficial use of its property unless it posted an acceptable $ 20,000 bond and then maintained that bond as long as it owned the property. The appellate court concluded that the trial court's order went well beyond Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-3-110 and amount to an unconstitutional taking of property.


OUTCOME: The trial court's abatement order was affirmed, as modified to enter a revised order omitting the bond requirement.

 

1230 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Esquinance v. Polk County Educ. Ass'n


No. E2004-02408-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


195 S.W.3d 35; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 446; 178 L.R.R.M. 2419


June 14, 2005, Session  
July 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Esquinance v. Polk County Educ. Ass'n, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 31 (Tenn., Jan. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County. No. CV-03-074. The Honorable Lawrence Puckett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher and union member brought a suit against appellee union alleging, inter alia, that his union dues were being used in violation of his rights to free speech, free assembly and petition, and freedom of religion set out in Tenn. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 19, and 23. The Circuit Court for Polk County (Tennessee) dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The teacher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The teacher also claimed that his due process rights under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 had been violated and that the state granted the education association a monopoly in violation of Tenn. Const. art I, § 22. The controversy sprung from the Education Professional Negotiations Act (EPNA), Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 49-5-601 - 49-5-613 (2002). The Supreme Court of Tennessee believed that the complaint, though premised on state constitutional violations, could also have been construed to have alleged other wrongs upon which relief could have been granted. For instance, the complaint alleged that the teacher paid his dues but protested the use of a portion of his dues. The EPNA contained authority for a collective bargaining organization for the purpose of a relationship of the various employees with the board of education, and it could have been interpreted to mean that a voluntary donation of a portion of the dues collected from the employees exceeded the authority granted. Giving the complaint its liberal construction, the supreme court found that the complaint, as to the first four counts thereof, stated a cause of action upon which relief could have been granted.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. Costs of the appeal were assessed one-half to the teacher and one-half to the union.

Consol. Waste Sys., LLC v. Metro Gov't of Nashville


No. M2002-02582-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 382


May 7, 2003, Session  
June 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Consol. Waste Sys., L.L.C. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 740 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 01C895. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a metropolitan government and county, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Davidson County (Tennessee), that found two zoning ordinances violated due process and equal protection rights on their face and that appellee landfill developer was not entitled to an injunction or damages and did not have standing to bring a takings claim. The developer challenged the finding that the ordinances did not constitute exclusionary zoning.


OVERVIEW: The developer claimed the ordinances, which regulated the location of construction and demolition (C & D) landfills, were unconstitutional on their face and exclusionary as they treated C & D landfills differently and precluded the construction of such landfills in the county. On appeal, the court rejected appellants' claim that the landfill developer was precluded from bringing its facial challenges to the ordinances. The court held that the U.S. Supreme Court had not adopted a position that substantive due process claims related to a zoning ordinance were always subsumed into a takings claim and had rejected the view that the applicability of one constitutional amendment preempts the guarantees of another. Also, the Tennessee courts had traditionally analyzed zoning ordinances under the rational basis test as an exercise of the local government's police power. The court rejected appellants' ripeness claims, holding that the ripeness requirements that applied to takings claims did not apply to facial challenges of an ordinance. The court held that the ordinances failed to meet the rational basis test and that the developer was entitled to attorney fees as the prevailing party.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and the award of attorney's fees. The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the developer was not precluded from bringing its facial challenge to the ordinances on substantive due process and equal protection grounds and that the trial court's determination that the ordinances violated those constitutional protections. The court assessed the costs of the appeal to appellants.

Buettner v. Buettner


No. W2004-01788-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


183 S.W.3d 354; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 324


February 15, 2005, Session  
June 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Buettner v. Buettner, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 929 (Tenn., Oct. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part; Reversed in part; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Henry County. No. 17787. Ron E. Harmon, Chancellor.
Buettner v. Buettner, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 230 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 20, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part; Reversed in part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court for Henry County (Tennessee) that modified his child support and failed to modify his alimony obligation.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in refusing to modify the award of alimony provided by the marital dissolution agreement (MDA). The court of appeals disagreed. The award of alimony was not determined by the trial court but was agreed to by the parties as a contractual provision of a very detailed MDA. The alimony provision provided for annual fluctuations in the amount of alimony based on the consumer price index. It also established a minimum alimony payment notwithstanding potential fluctuations and provided for increases in alimony upon the emancipation of the parties' children. When the MDA was executed, the mother was a registered nurse, although she was not working as a nurse and had minimal income. The father argued that his alimony obligation should be reduced to the $ 1,500 minimum amount established by the MDA because he did not anticipate that the mother would return to work as a registered nurse on a full-time basis. However, the trial court properly found that there had been no substantial and material change of circumstance warranting modification of the alimony provision of the parties' MDA.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed with regard to the trial court's finding that the mother was entitled to an additional increase of child support upon emancipation of the parties' younger child. Other child support and alimony provisions were modified. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Hooker v. Alexander


No. M2003-01141-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 304

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, independent candidate, challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissing his action which sought to have the election for United States Senate declared void, pursuant to the motion to dismiss, Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6), filed by defendant, incumbent candidate.


OVERVIEW: The independent candidate sought to have the election declared void on the basis that the incumbent candidate used his own money and accepted campaign contribution in support of his candidacy. The main thrust of the independent candidate's argument was that such contributions, and the necessity therefore, constituted an additional property qualification, available only to those who had money or could raise money and unavailable to candidates lacking such good fortune. The independent candidate asserted that the giving and receiving of campaign contributions added property qualifications to the electoral process which was prohibited. The independent candidate asserted that Tenn. Const. art. IV provided that the only qualifications for those seeking public office were citizenship, age and residency. By the independent candidate's reasoning, the need to raise money constituted an additional qualification in violation of the Tennessee Constitution. The court ruled that the zeal of the independent candidate's crusade could not vest the judiciary with powers that were essentially legislative in character.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1234 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boyd


No. M2003-02557-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 291


April 13, 2005, Session  
May 17, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Boyd, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 908 (Tenn., Oct. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 2003-T-5. Carol Soloman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating the implied consent law for refusing to take a test to determine his blood alcohol content when he was arrested for driving under the influence of an intoxicant. A jury found him not guilty of DUI. However, the trial judge in the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, sitting without a jury, found that the defendant violated the implied consent law and revoked his license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The arresting officer had reasonable grounds to believe that defendant was driving while under the influence of an intoxicant. By refusing to take a blood alcohol test, he violated the implied consent law. His license was revoked by the judge under Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-406(3). Defendant claimed that Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-406(3) was unconstitutional, because it required the judge to also serve as an administrative officer of the Tennessee Department of Safety and rule on the civil charge of the alleged violation of the implied consent law. Defendant's claim lacked merit, because the implied consent law did not violate the separation of powers clause. Conviction under Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-406 with the right of the trial judge to prohibit the person from driving was a judicial act, and it had no relation whatever to the Department of Safety's power to grant, revoke and suspend licenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.
