Tenn. Div. of the United Daughters of the Confederacy v. Vanderbilt Univ.


No. M2003-02632-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


174 S.W.3d 98; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 272


January 5, 2005, Session  
May 3, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-3095-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff donor organization appealed a decision of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant university in plaintiff's action for breach of an agreement when defendant decided to change to name of a dormitory because of the stigma attached to the name "Confederate." The dormitory was built in part with funds donated by plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Defendant merged with another college, which owned the dormitory and defendant succeeded to all of the college's legal obligations. Defendant renovated the dormitory and, it was decided that the name would be changed. The court held: (1) because plaintiff did not claim that it intended to create a revocable charitable trust when it entered into the agreements with the college, the contracts reflected a charitable gift subject to conditions; (2) the contracts did not specify the duration of the conditions, but the court concluded that the conditions were limited to the life of the building itself; (3) the original placement of the plaque did not constitute substantial performance; (4) defendant's legal obligation to comply with the conditions of the gift agreement arose defendant's own decision to enter into a merger agreement with the college, so defendant's assertions of academic freedom did not apply; (5) because defendant presented no legal basis for permitting it to keep the gift while refusing to honor the conditions attached to it, defendant had to either return the present value of the gift to plaintiff or abide by the conditions originally placed on the gift.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of defendant.

Bean v. Bredesen


No. M2003-01665-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 267


September 10, 2004, Session  
May 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bean v. Bredesen, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 328 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 2, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 91-2558-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.
Bean v. McWherter, 24 S.W.3d 325, 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 801 (Tenn. Ct. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 70-4-403(4)(B), defendant, the State, banned the importation of white-tailed deer based on concerns of the spread of Chronic Wasting Disease (CWD) to Tennessee's white-tail deer population. Plaintiffs, numerous individuals, asserted the statute violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, upheld the statute. Plaintiffs sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs included persons who imported wildlife or exotic animals for business purposes and for sale to customers. Chronic Wasting Disease (CWD), was a fatal, transmissible disease of the central nervous system found in white-tailed deer, mule deer, and Rocky Mountain elk and scientists appeared to have agreed that captivity of elk and deer facilitated the transmission of the disease. However, mule deer and elk could be tested for CWD before they were imported into Tennessee. There was no similar test for white-tailed deer, which could be tested only by an autopsy following their death. The appellate court noted that preventing the spread of CWD to Tennessee's indigenous white-tailed deer was an interest of the highest order and therefore the subject legislation was reasonable. The appellate court held that plaintiffs' assertion that Tenn. Code Ann. § 70-4-403(4)(B) unconstitutionally burdened interstate commerce failed to demonstrate that the statute discriminated against interstate commerce or that its incidental burdens on interstate commerce were clearly excessive in relation to the benefits it provided by protecting the health of Tennessee's indigenous white-tailed deer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Moore v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


No. M2003-03110-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 269


March 7, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
May 2, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 03-2239-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.
State v. Moore, 614 S.W.2d 348, 1981 Tenn. LEXIS 429 (Tenn., 1981)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a prisoner, filed a petition for common law writ of certiorari, contending that the refusal of appellee, the Tennessee Board of Probation and Parole, to release him violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto enactments. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed the petition. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1977, appellant was sentenced to life in prison for a first degree murder. In 2000, three out of seven members of the parole board voted to parole him. Because of a 1997 statute that required four members of the parole board to concur, parole was denied. He did not file his complaint for writ of certiorari until 2003. Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 27-9-101, -102 required him to seek review within sixty days of entry of the final order. Therefore, appellant's petition was untimely. As for the merits of appellant's ex post facto claim, the parole board's application of the four vote provision of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-105(d)(3) was not constitutional. At the time he committed his crime, the parole board was composed of three members, and a majority vote or 67% was required to grant parole. Requiring a vote of four out of seven members or 57% did not disadvantage his quest for parole.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Flautt & Mann v. Council of the City of Memphis

2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 235


February 15, 2005, Session  
April 22, 2005, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. 75359-4 T.D. Rita L. Stotts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision of the Circuit Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, which remanded this zoning case to the city council after appellee landowner filed a petition for contempt under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-9-102 (2003) in the circuit court. Originally, the landowner's petition for rezoning of property was rejected and the circuit court reversed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought to have the property zoned from agricultural to commercial in order to allow billboards on the property. Because the circuit court reversed the city's denial and remanded to have the city council again deny the landowner's request, the trial court found that the city violated the court's order but that it was not willful. The court reversed and held that neither party filed a notice of appeal seeking to contest the trial court's amended order and therefore the court could not examine the correctness of the trial court's order on the original petition filed by appellee. The court also held that the trial court failed to identify and apply the correct legal principle to the petition for contempt. Accordingly, the trial court abused its discretion in finding that the actions of the city council did not constitute contempt due to the erroneous advice of its lawyer. On remand, should the trial court determine that the actions of the city council constituted willful contempt of the court's order, the trial court was instructed to fashion an appropriate sanction authorized by law under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-9-103 to -105 (2003).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a determination of whether the actions of the city council constituted contempt of the trial court's order.

Meeks v. Traughber


No. M2003-02077-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 76


January 10, 2005, Assigned on Briefs  
February 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Meeks v. Traughber, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 720 (Tenn., Aug. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed as Modified. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-3535-I. Claudia Bonnyman, Chancellor.
Meeks v. State, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 447 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 19, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Chancery Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant's effective sentence was 48 years. He was eligible for parole in 2001, and in 2002 the board of parole declined parole owing to a substantial risk that he would not conform to the conditions of his release and ordered no further review for 15 years. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed appellant's petition for certiorari that alleged that the board's action was ex post facto. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed, inter alia, that the board, not only denied him parole, but unconstitutionally ordered no further review for 15 years. The policy of the board was later changed. The appellate court agreed with the State that the Policy Change Notice, which amended Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. Policy 501.30 by omitting the provision for annual parole hearings, was an administrative change and did not add to appellant's punishment. He was convicted of aggravated kidnapping, especially aggravated robbery, aggravated burglary and extortion for which he received an effective sentence of 48 years. The board declined parole finding that there was a substantial risk that he would not conform to the conditions of his release and that his release from custody would depreciate the seriousness of his crimes. The board set his next parole review for February 2017. The appellate court held that appellant had no constitutional or inherent right to conditional release prior to the expiration of a valid sentence. There was no change in any law which had retroactively inflicted a greater punishment on defendant; therefore, his ex post facto claim was without merit and was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment deferring parole consideration until 2017 was reversed; otherwise the judgment was affirmed. Costs were assessed to appellant.

B. F. Nashville, Inc. v. City of Franklin


No. M2003-00180-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 32


October 8, 2003, Session  
January 21, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 28940. Russ Heldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant restaurant owner was notified by appellee, the City of Franklin, Tennessee, that appellant could not reconstruct its free-standing advertising sign since it did not conform to a new sign ordinance. Appellant filed a complaint, seeking a declaration that it had a vested right to erect a non-conforming replacement sign. The Chancery Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, dismissed the complaint. Appellant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Three years after its free-standing advertising sign was damaged in a thunderstorm and removed, the restaurant owner decided to erect a replacement sign. The restaurant was notified by the city that it had remove the support posts remaining from the original sign. That notice also stated that the old sign could not be reconstructed since it did not conform to a new sign ordinance. The restaurant owner filed a complaint for declaratory judgment, seeking a declaration that it had a vested right under Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208 to erect a non-conforming replacement sign. Although the protections of Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208 applied generally to on-site advertising signs, the restaurant owner was not entitled to a declaratory judgment that its sign could be reconstructed without regard to the city's sign ordinance. The restaurant owner should have appealed the Sign Codes Administrator's interpretation or determination to the Board of Zoning Appeals. Its failure to exhaust this administrative remedy justified the trial court's dismissal of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1243 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Jackson Energy Auth. v. Diamond


No. W2004-01090-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


181 S.W.3d 735; 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 22


October 28, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
January 20, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Jackson Energy Auth. v. Diamond, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 700 (Tenn., Aug. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C-03-294. Donald H. Allen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Madison County, Tennessee, granted judgment in favor of plaintiff utility company on its claim against defendant building owner for past due utility payments by dismissing the owner's appeal from general sessions court on the basis that it was not filed within ten days of the final general sessions judgment entered. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the ten-day time limitations was tolled by his general sessions petition to rehear and that the ten day period under Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-5-108 for filing an appeal from general sessions court began to run the day after it entered its August 6, 2003, denial of his petition to rehear. The appellate court found that the petition to rehear was filed within the ten-day time period for appeal to circuit court, and the denial of the petition was likewise filed within that time period. Thus, the question was whether a petition to rehear filed and decided by the general sessions court within the ten-day period for appeal tolled the period for appeal to the circuit court. The authority of the general sessions court ended when it entered a judgment in the case. It had no statutory authority to grant the relief requested and the petition did not toll the appeal period. Thus, the ten-day period for seeking a de novo review in the circuit court began to run when the general sessions final judgment was entered. Due process did not require a tolling of the ten-day period for appeal where the owner simply mistakenly presumed that the ten-day period for appeal would be tolled.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1244 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. Lee


No. W2003-01053-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 892


March 22, 2004, Assigned on Briefs  
December 29, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. D-27933-III. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.
Lee v. Lee, 66 S.W.3d 837, 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 465 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought an order changing his child's custody from respondent mother in the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), alleging that there had been a material change of circumstances and that the mother had tried to minimize or negate his relationship with the child. The trial court held that it did not have continuing jurisdiction over custody and visitation decisions involving the child. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother moved to California with the child when he was two and was granted a divorce and custody by the Tennessee court. The father exercised visitation in both California and Tennessee, but primarily in California. The court found that the mother was correct to file in Tennessee because the child had not lived in California six months at the time and the Tennessee trial court had the jurisdiction to make an initial child custody determination under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-216(a)(1). The trial court properly found that it had lost jurisdiction pursuant to Tenn. Code § 36-6-217(a)(1). The first part was met because the child and his mother had lived in California since 1996. The other requirement, that the child no longer had a significant connection with Tennessee and that substantial evidence was no longer available in Tennessee concerning his care, protection, training, and personal relationships, was also met. There was no evidence of any current connection between the child and Tennessee other than that his father lived there. Two affidavits of persons who had seen the child in Tennessee at his last visit did not support a finding of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order dismissing the father's petition to change custody for lack of jurisdiction was affirmed.

State ex rel. Williams v. Town of Midtown


No. E2004-01007-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 844


October 25, 2004, Session  
December 16, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right. Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Roane County. No. 14,005. Frank V. Williams, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, citizens, contested incorporation. Appellant, the City filed a counter-complaint, alleging that statutory minimum population and distance requirements unconstitutionally deprived it of equal protection. Appellee, the Tennessee Attorney General (State), answered, denying that the statutory provisions were unconstitutional. The Chancery Court for Roane County, Tennessee, dismissed the City's counter-complaint. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City challenged the requirements in Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-1-201(a)(1) and 6-1-201(b)(1)(A), which precluded incorporation of territory unless such territory contained not fewer than 1,500 persons. The statute also set a three mile to five mile minimum distance for incorporation from an existing municipality, depending on the population of the municipality. In the instant case, the three mile distance applied. The appellate court rejected the City's argument that the requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-1-201(a)(1) and 6-1-201(b)(1)(A) were arbitrary and capricious and violated the equal protection of the laws guaranteed by the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. The appellate court held that the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution was not implicated under the circumstances of the case. Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-1-201(a)(1) and 6-1-201(b)(1)(A) was a general law and was constitutional. Further, Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8 was not implicated by the general law regarding the incorporation of cities statewide.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court dismissing the City's counter-complaint was affirmed, as was the trial court's ruling in its entirety. Costs on appeal were assessed to the City.

Mosley v. Tenn. Dep't of Commerce & Ins.


No. M2003-01998-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


167 S.W.3d 308; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 784


August 6, 2004, Session  
November 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mosley v. Tenn. Ins. Div., 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 448 (Tenn., May 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-1532-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted judgment in favor of appellant Tennessee Department of Commerce and Insurance by finding that the record supported the department's conclusion that appellee insurance agent had sold policies in states where he was not licensed, but determined that the agent's license had to be suspended for six months rather than revoked. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department argued that the agent's license should have been revoked. The appellate court noted that the undisputed facts of the case established that the agent knew that he was repeatedly violating the laws of Georgia and Virginia and that he was exceeding the authority of his Tennessee license by his deliberate actions. Tenn. Code Ann. § 56-6-161 of the Tennessee Uniform Administrative Procedures Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-101 et seq., was applicable to proceedings to revoke or suspend the license of an insurance agent. The sanctions imposed by the administrative tribunal upon the agent were clearly warranted in law. No basis existed for finding that the sanction of revocation of license was without justification in fact. The agent's repeated transgressions in taking applications for policies of insurance in Georgia and Virginia while indicating that they were executed in Tennessee were committed intentionally and with deliberation. Neither the chancery court nor the court of appeals was empowered to substitute judicial judgment in the place of the judgment of an administrative tribunal acting within the scope of its statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Byrd v. City of Memphis

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, granted the trial court clerk's motion in 2003 to dismiss plaintiff residents' suit for lack of prosecution. The residents had filed suit in 1988 against defendant municipal officials for allegedly enacting an unconstitutional and unreasonable annexation ordinance. The residents appealed.

The case languished on the trial court's docket for over 15 years with little or no activity. The residents were certainly aware that continued inaction would result in dismissal, but the residents made no further efforts to prosecute their case. It was the residents' burden to prosecute their case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis


No. W2003-01300-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 724


September 21, 2004, Session  
November 3, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 247 (Tenn., Mar. 21, 2005)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 313 (Tenn., Apr. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in part, Vacated and Remanded. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-007680-01. The Honorable Robert A. Lanier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city cited appellants, adult bookstores, for violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1402. The stores filed a complaint for declaratory judgment which also requested a temporary and permanent injunction challenging the constitutionality of the Act. The Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) entered an order denying the injunction and dismissed the case for lack of jurisdiction and upheld the statute. The bookstores appealed.


OVERVIEW: The civil court did not have authority to enjoin the enforcement of a criminal statute. While it was correct in denying the stores' motions for temporary and permanent injunction, the trial court erred in finding that the doctrine of former suit pending barred the stores from bringing an action in civil court while the prosecutions proceeded against their employees, for violation of the Act, in criminal courts. The stores alleged that the court's sua sponte dismissal of all of their claims was improper because they were denied the opportunity to argue those claims fully. The trial court, in ruling on the merits of the constitutional claims upon a hearing of their motions for temporary injunction, either effectively issued a declaratory judgment or dismissed the action on its merits. In either event, the trial court went beyond the proper scope of a hearing on a motion for temporary injunction. The appellate court found nothing in the record that indicated that the trial court properly ordered the consolidation of the hearing of the application for temporary injunction with a trial on the merits, and it was clear that both sides desired a full trial on the merits at a later date.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court denying the motions for temporary injunction was affirmed, and the order in all other respects was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for such further proceedings on the declaratory judgment action consistent with the appellate opinion. Costs of the appeal were assessed one-half to the bookstores and one-half to the city and the Attorney General.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties, petitioner mother and respondent father, appealed the orders of the Juvenile Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that modified child support.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals found that the trial court's refusal to award retroactive child support was erroneous. February 23, 2004, Assigned on Briefs

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Abdur'Rahman v. Bredesen, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 124 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)
Affirmed by Abdur'Rahman v. Bredesen, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 828 (Tenn., Oct. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-2236-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
Abdur'Rahman v. Tennessee, 541 U.S. 1011, 158 L. Ed. 2d 622, 124 S. Ct. 2066, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3094 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row inmate filed a petition challenging the Tennessee Department of Correction's lethal injection protocol. Appellee State filed a motion to dismiss the inmate's claims, which the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate asserted that the procedure used to adopt the protocol was legally flawed, that the protocol violated various licensing and regulatory requirements, and that the protocol itself violated the prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishments in Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16 and U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The appellate court rejected the inmate's arguments and held: (1) the Department was not required to follow the rules and regulations of the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act in establishing the lethal injection protocol; (2) the Nonlivestock Animal Humane Death Act did not apply to the execution of a human being by lethal injection pursuant to Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16 or the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Graham v. Gen. Sessions Court


No. M2003-02231-COA-R3-CO


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


157 S.W.3d 790; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 642


August 4, 2004, Session  
October 5, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Franklin County. No. 13405 CV. The Honorable Thomas W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs professional bondsmen sued defendants, general sessions court, the general sessions judge, and the sheriff, and sought a declaratory judgment that an order of the general sessions court concerning bonds for some offenses was invalid as contrary to the statutes of the State of Tennessee and the Tennessee Constitution. The Circuit Court for Franklin County, Tennessee, entered judgment for defendants. The bondsmen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bondsmen filed their action after the court decreed that all bonds set by that court in the amount of $ 4,400 or less were to be granted bond by the signature of two property owners living in the county, and that property tax receipts and signatures of the parties were sufficient for release from custody. The bondsmen claimed that the trial court's order violated the Release from Custody and Bail Reform Act of 1978 (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-101 - 40-11-144 (2003) as the order purported to take away the authority of the sheriff or judicial commissioner to determine the sufficiency of the surety, a power set out in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-106(b)(1). The appellate court agreed and held that the statutory scheme of the Act clearly contemplated that while the judge or magistrate would determine whether defendants would be released upon their own recognizance, upon conditions, or upon admission to bail, it was within the authority of the sheriff or judicial commissioner to determine the sufficiency of a surety or validity of a bond. Thus, the trial court's judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that denied the bondsmen's summary judgment motion was reversed, and the costs of appeal were assessed to the general sessions court.

Gill v. City of Church Hill


No. E2004-00200-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


156 S.W.3d 846; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 569


August 12, 2004, Session  
August 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Daniel Wayne Gill v. City of Church Hill And Rodney E. Miller, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 169 (Tenn., Feb. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hawkins County. No. CV-201. Hon. John K. Wilson, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father, individually and for use and benefit of a decedent, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Hawkins County (Tennessee) that granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a city and a police officer, based on the privileges provided in Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-8-108(e), in the father's wrongful death action that arose as the result of a high speed police chase of his son.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed the trial court erred in dismissing the action because it could not be established from the complaint that the decedent was an "actual or suspected violator of the law" for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-8-108(e) where the complaint demonstrated that the police officer was aware that he was pursuing a juvenile, and "knew," because of the decedent's age,that he did not have the capacity to commit a crime. The court held that the issue of whether or not decedent had the capacity to commit a crime was not determinative because the scope of § 55-8-108(e) was very broad and applied to both criminal and civil violations. The court found that the complaint alleged that the officer pursued the decedent based on a description of the vehicle and driver, thus decedent was a "suspected violator of a law or ordinance," and defendants were not liable for his injuries. The court rejected the father's claim that § 55-8-108(e) was unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions because the issue was not properly before the court. The trial court did not rule on the issue, and the notice requirements of Tenn. R. Civ. P. 24.04 were not complied within the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment dismissing the father's wrongful death action and remanded the case with costs assessed to the father.

Snell v. City of Murfreesboro


No. M2003-02716-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 564


June 24, 2004, On-brief  
August 27, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. 47874. The Honorable Robert E. Corlew, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Rutherford County, Tennessee, dismissed appellant landowners' complaint against appellee city for failure to state a cause of action. The landowners filed a declaratory judgment seeking to have a city ordinance that annexed property across from the landowners null and void as a violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-101 et seq. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners asserted that they were entitled to bring the action, being adjoining landowners. The appellate court determined that the statute the landowners relied upon, Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103, had been declared unconstitutional. The legislature did not take further actions concerning the provisions of the statute since 1989, and thus, the only property owners allowed to contest an annexation ordinance by way of the quo warranto proceeding were those who owned property within the annexed area. It was the appellate court's duty to grant the city's motion to dismiss because there were no other statutes which allowed adjacent landowners to contest annexation ordinances. The landowners did not own property within the annexed territory, and thus could not claim the right to challenge an annexation ordinance under Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-51-103. The annexation ordinance did not include the landowners and their property. The quo warranto remedy was not available to the landowners. The landowners lacked legal standing to challenge the annexation ordinance at issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Evans v. Evans


No. M2002-02947-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 547


September 4, 2003, Session  
August 23, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Lawrence County. No. 7352-95 Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.
Wright v. Quillen, 83 S.W.3d 768, 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 7 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court for Lawrence County (Tennessee), which denied his petition to be relieved from his obligation to pay alimony in futuro to appellee former wife.


OVERVIEW: The husband claimed that the wife's cohabitation with another man terminated his obligation, as she was being supported by that third person and was in no need of alimony. The trial court held that the wife was no longer living with the third person and had rebutted the presumption that she did not need the alimony and that no material change in circumstances had occurred to warrant modification of the initial alimony award. The court found that the evidence supported those holdings. Because the wife was not receiving support from the third person as of the trial, the situation justifying alimony reduction or termination had ceased to exist. The wife's financial support to the parties' adult child was not unforeseeable or unanticipated, and she demonstrated that she was in need of the continuing alimony payments. The court concluded that, while Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(c) authorized a trial court to award attorney fees to an alimony recipient who was forced to defend an action to reduce or terminate that alimony, fees should not have been awarded to the wife, because it could not be said that the husband's attempt to reduce or terminate alimony was unwarranted or without basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the husband's petition for modification of spousal support, but reversed the award of attorney fees to the wife.

Am. Chariot v. City of Memphis


No. W2004-00014-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


164 S.W.3d 600; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 529


June 24, 2004, Assigned on Brief  
August 19, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Am. Chariot v. City of Memphis, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 75 (Tenn., Jan. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-02-1350-3. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, denied plaintiffs', horse-drawn carriage operators, declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of a provision of one section of an ordinance adopted by defendant city council. The trial court elided the provision as an unlawful delegation of the city's police power and enforced the remainder of the ordinance. The operators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The operators asserted that the trial court erred in its application of the doctrine of elision. The city cross-appealed, arguing that the trial court erred by finding the elided portion unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that the ordinance prohibited horse-drawn carriages from standing within 100 feet of a restaurant not for the protection of the restaurant business per se, but as a matter of public health and welfare. The section was part of an overall regulatory scheme affecting matters of public health and welfare. The consent provision permitted restaurant owners to waive a restriction that served to protect the public health and welfare. It contained no standards for determining when such a waiver was appropriate or for review by the city of whether the waiver adversely affected those that the section protected. Therefore, the consent provision unlawfully delegated the city's police and legislative powers to private citizens. Absent the consent provision, the section fulfilled its objective of protecting the public health and welfare. The doctrine of elision was properly applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Alexander v. Williams


No. W2003-01485-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 494


June 22, 2004, Argued  
August 2, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Vacated and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Haywood County. Nos. 6623 and 5280. J. Roland Reid, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Haywood County, Tennessee, in two actions, dismissed appellant State's petitions for contempt against appellee parents and refused to enforce or modify child support orders administratively issued under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(f). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by refusing to enforce or modify child support orders administratively issued by the department of human services (department) under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(f). The appellate court noted that the pivotal issue was whether the courts had subject matter jurisdiction to enforce or modify administrative orders issued under § 36-5-103(f). Section 36-5-103(f) unambiguously provided that reviews and adjustments made pursuant to the section may be conducted by the court or the department by issuance of an administrative order. Reading Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-5-812 and 813 together, the legislature clearly conferred to the courts subject matter jurisdiction over enforcement of administrative orders of support issued under § 36-5-103(f). The court may enforce its own support orders and those issued by the State pursuant to contempt orders. The trial court clearly had jurisdiction to modify the child support order previously modified by the department. The trial court erred in dismissing the State's petition to modify without reaching the merits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded.

The father was obligated by two judicial orders to keep his wife and mother-in-law informed of his address. He simply failed to do so for years. He basically just allowed the child to not be a part of his life. He had no mailing address; he maintained contact "with the world" through his sister; he resided in a dilapidated trailer; he had no drivers license, no job, no funds. He appeared to be a vagabond by choice, as he found employment when he chose to do so.

State v. Delinquent Taxpayers


No. M2001-00531-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 327



May 20, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court of Davidson County. No. 00-781-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
State ex rel. Metro. Gov't of Nashville & Davidson County v. Delinguent Taxpayers, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 529 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 29, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, buyer, challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Davidson County, Tennessee, overruling the buyer's motions to intervene and dismiss, and granting of the statutory right of redemption from a real property delinquent tax sale in favor of respondent, creditor.


OVERVIEW: The State of Tennessee filed a delinquent tax suit against the taxpayer. Notice of the tax sale was given to the taxpayer and the creditor, who held an equitable interest in the property through a second mortgage. The buyer purchased the property at the tax sale, and the sale was confirmed on October 2, 2000. On November 14, 2000, the creditor filed a notice of redemption for the property, and the buyer was sent a notice of redemption informing him that he had 30-days from November 14 to seek additional lawful compensation or to otherwise protest the redemption. The buyer did not file any claims in accordance with the notice he received on November 15, 2000. The appellate court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2702(a) granted the trial court in rem jurisdiction of the taxpayer's property for up to a year after the tax sale, until August 2001. The buyer was sent the letter of notice well within the statutory requirements of due process, and the buyer was provided the right to protest at a hearing, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2704. The State followed the statutory requirements and the trial court afforded the buyer his day in a court of appropriate jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1259 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Freeman Indus. L.L.C. v. Eastman Chem. Co.


No. E2003-00527-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 321; 2004-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,412


December 2, 2003, Session  
May 18, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Appeal granted by Freeman Indus., LLC v. Eastman Chem. Co., 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 857 (Tenn., Oct. 4, 2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Freeman Indus. v. Eastman Chem. Co., 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 668 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Law Court Affirmed, as Modified; Case Remanded. Interlocutory Appeal by Permission from the Law Court for Sullivan County. No. C34355-L. Richard E. Ladd, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, as Modified; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff product purchaser appealed from a judgment of the Law Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee), which denied its motion for class certification in its illegal price-fixing action against defendant product seller. The trial court had granted the purchaser's motion to dismiss a claim under the Tennessee Trade Practices Act (TTPA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-101 et seq. (2001), but denied its motion for summary judgment on unjust enrichment.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser alleged that the seller engaged in illegal price-fixing of sorbates. Although the purchaser bought and sold sorbates directly, the action was based on its indirect purchases from supermarkets as an end-user of sorbates that were in the products purchased. Previously, the sellers had pled guilty to price-fixing of sorbates and had settled lawsuits by both direct and indirect purchasers. The trial court's dismissal of the TTPA claim was based on its holding that the TTPA did not apply to indirect purchasers or out-of-state transactions. On appeal, the court found that, based on a recently issued opinion, the TTPA did apply to indirect purchasers. However, as the purchaser was unable to show that its purchases of sorbates "substantially affected" Tennessee commerce, the holding that the TTPA did not apply to the purchaser's claim was proper. The purchaser did not show compliance with Tenn. R. Civ. P. 23.02(3) for purposes of class certification, nor were the prerequisites of a common question of law or fact and typicality of claim satisfied. Lastly, summary judgment on the unjust enrichment claim was properly denied, as questions of fact as to the choice of law remained.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by noting that the TTPA applied to indirect purchasers. As modified, the court affirmed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1260 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hooker v. Sundquist


No. M2003-02042-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


150 S.W.3d 406; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 270


March 17, 2004, Session  
April 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Hooker v. Sundquist, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 437 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 01-C-3804. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
Hooker v. Sundquist, 107 S.W.3d 532, 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 890 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual filed a lawsuit against appellee Governor, challenging the practice of serving meat and drink at political fund raisers, alleging that the practice violated Tenn. Const. art. X, § 3. The Governor filed a motion for sanctions, pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11. On remand, the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granted the motion and imposed as a sanction a screening mechanism. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual claimed that the screening mechanism imposed against him violated his constitutional rights. He acknowledged having filed a series of lawsuits asserting violations of Tenn. Const. art. X, § 3 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-19-126 and that various courts had declined to accept his interpretation of those laws. He claimed, however, that those lawsuits were filed in order to protect the constitution. The appellate court held that the two year screening mechanism imposed by the trial court was narrowly tailored and short in duration, effectively curbing for a defined period of time any repetitive or frivolous lawsuits filed by the individual, and was fully warranted, given his undisputed history of filing such lawsuits. The screening mechanism did not prevent him from filing another lawsuit. It prevented him only from relitigating essentially the same lawsuit. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, Nashville, had great respect for the need to litigate novel interpretations of the constitution and had respect as well for the sincerity of the individual's beliefs. However, the appellate court had to respect the need for other litigants to have the courts hear their lawsuits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs on appeal were taxed to the individual.

Byrd v. State


No. W2003-00302-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


150 S.W.3d 414; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 245


July 14, 2003, Assigned on Brief  
April 19, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Tennessee Claims Commission No. 20-200-294 Randy Camp, Commissioner.
Byrd v. State, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 937 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant independent contractors were hired to clean a medical clinic operated by appellee state. They alleged that they were sexually harassed by one of the clinic's physicians, and that when they complained about it, they were subjected to retaliation and further sexual harassment. The State filed a motion to dismiss arguing lack of subject matter jurisdiction which the Tennessee Claims Commission granted. The contractors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, in the complaint, the contractors also asserted a violation of the prohibition against malicious harassment, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-701. They argued that the claims commission had jurisdiction over that claim under Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(N), which stated that the claims commission had jurisdiction to determine a claim against the State for the negligent deprivation of a statutory right. The appellate court held that that section required that the contractors showed that the legislature expressly conferred a private right of action against the State. The claims commission found that it lacked jurisdiction over that claim, holding that there was no express private right of action by an individual against the State conferred by the statute. However, since a state university was considered a "person" under the Human Rights Act, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-701 expressly granted a right of action against such a "person" for malicious harassment, the appellate court concluded that the claims commission had had jurisdiction over the malicious harassment claim pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(N).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part, the holding by the commission that it lacked jurisdiction over the claim of malicious harassment was reversed. The case was remanded. Costs were taxed one-half to the contractors and one-half to the State.

City of Chattanooga v. Cinema 1, Inc.


No. E2003-01038-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an adult bookstore and its owner, appealed a judgment of the Chancery Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, affirming the decision of the Chattanooga, Tennessee, City Council, revoking their license to operate an adult oriented business.

Hogue v. Hogue


No. M2002-02500-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


147 S.W.3d 245; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 182


November 4, 2003, Session  
March 24, 2004, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 28527. R. E. Lee Davies, Judge.
Hogue v. Hogue, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 5 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father filed a petition to rehear the decision of the Chancery Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, finding him in contempt of court for violating a restraining order.


OVERVIEW: The chancellor issued a restraining order upon the filing of the divorce complaint, which prohibited the father from exposing the child to his gay lifestyle. Thereafter, the father was held in contempt for telling the child he was gay. 1264 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Crew One Prods., Inc. v. State


No. M2003-00585-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


149 S.W.3d 89; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 127


November 5, 2003, Session  
February 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application denied by Crew One Prods. v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 823 (Tenn., Sept. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Tennessee Claims Commission Reversed. Direct Appeal from the Tennessee Claims Commission. No. 068301. W. R. Baker, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Tennessee Claims Commission Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an employment tax case, appellant, the State of Tennessee, appealed the determination of the Tennessee Claims Commission that appellee employer was not liable for state employment tax by virtue of a federal safe harbor provision. The commissioner thus entered judgment for the employer, ordering the State to return all funds paid under protest by the employer and awarding the employer post judgment interest of 10 percent. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Tennessee Department of Labor and Workforce Development (DLWD) determined that the employer's stage hands were employees and not independent contractors, and that the employer accordingly was liable for state employment taxes. The policy behind the Tennessee's Employment Security Law was to protect workers in Tennessee from involuntary unemployment. The statute contained no safe harbor provision parallel to the federal safe harbor provision known as § 530, 26 U.S.C.S. § 3401 note, and that federal provision did not further the state's public policy as defined by the Tennessee legislature. The State, therefore, was not bound to provide liability protection parallel to § 530 for state employment tax purposes. Thus, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 50-7-102 and -104 (1999) did not mandate a safe harbor provision parallel to § 530. Therefore, the State was not required to relieve the employer from state employment tax liability when the employer had obtained § 530 relief from federal employment tax liability. Additionally, the employer withdrew its challenge regarding whether its workers were employees and not independent contractors; thus, the employer was liable for state employment taxes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the Tennessee Claims Commission's judgment.

Lucas v. State


No. M2002-02810-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


141 S.W.3d 121; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 83


November 3, 2003, Session  
February 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Lucas v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 583 (Tenn., June 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Tennessee Claims Commission Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Tennessee Claims Commission. No. 1,604,201 AND 20,100,376. En banc, Commissioners, Randy C. Camp, Vance W. Cheek, Jr., and W.R. Baker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Tennessee Claims Commission that denied its motion for summary judgment, which was based on the State's claim of discretionary function immunity in a suit by plaintiffs against the State involving claims of unsafe roads.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the Commission erred by denying the motion for summary judgment because it was entitled to discretionary function immunity. The court of appeals disagreed. Under no circumstances was any immunity available to the State which could not be characterized as "absolute immunity," such being the only type of immunity that survived the enactment of the Tennessee Claims Commission Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-301, et seq. Discretionary function immunity was a qualified (good faith) immunity rather than an absolute immunity and by the express provisions of Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(d) could not be relied upon by the State in an action before the Commission. The question of notice of a dangerous conditions remained for trial, and therefore, the trial court properly denied the motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded for trial on the merits.

Williams v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


139 S.W.3d 308; 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 43


October 20, 2003, Assigned on Briefs

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Williams v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 396 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 29, 2004)
Appeal denied by Williams v. State, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 530 (Tenn., June 1, 2004)
Appeal denied by Williams v. Parker, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 9 (Tenn., Jan. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Claims Commission Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Claims Commission for the Eastern Grand Division No. 20300711 Vance W. Cheek, Jr., Commissioner.
Williams v. State, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 107 (Tenn., Feb. 3, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate, who absconded while on bond, was tried, convicted, and sentenced on drug charges in absentia. Years later, the inmate was apprehended and placed in prison. The inmate sued defendant, the State of Tennessee, claiming that the trial and sentencing violated various statutory rights of his. The State filed a motion to dismiss, which the Tennessee Claims Commission for the Eastern Grand (Commission) granted. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to conversations with his attorney, the inmate knew he was being tried, convicted, and sentenced in absentia. Eventually, the inmate filed his claim against the State with the Tennessee Division of Claims Administration alleging that the trial judge deprived him of his statutory rights because the indictments against him were void and because he was tried, convicted, and sentenced in absentia. The case was transferred to the Commission. The appellate court found that the Commission properly held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the inmate's claim and that the inmate failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted because none of the statutes he based his claim on conferred a private right of action on him. Additionally, the inmate filed his claim against the State well beyond the one-year statute of limitations. Also, the inmate had full knowledge of the facts relevant to his alleged injury when it occurred because he knew that he was being tried and sentenced in absentia. Thus, the Commission properly held the inmate's claim was barred by the statute of limitations. Therefore, the Commission did not err when it dismissed the inmate's claim.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the Commission's judgment.

Hogue v. Hogue


No. M2002-02500-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 5


November 4, 2003, Session  
January 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, in part Hogue v. Hogue, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 52 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 23, 2004)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Hogue v. Hogue, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 182 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 28527. R. E. Lee Davies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A temporary restraining order was issued when a marital dissolution was filed. Appellee mother then filed a petition for contempt, alleging that appellant father had violated the order by allowing their child to be in the presence of the father's "gay lover" at the father's apartment and that the father told the child that he was gay. The Chancery Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) found the father in contempt. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father asserted that the restraining order was overbroad and/or vague, not issued pursuant to Tenn. R. Civ. P. 65.03, and had expired prior to the alleged offense. The appellate court found that the prohibition against "taking the child around or otherwise exposing the child to his gay lover(s) and/or his gay lifestyle" was not so vague or overly broad as to have been unenforceable. However, the appellate court found that it did not put the father on notice that he was restrained from telling his son that he was gay. The appellate court did not read the restraining order to prohibit such a statement. Thus, the appellate court found that the father did not have notice that he was prohibited from telling his son he was gay and therefore could not have been held in contempt for having done so. The mother argued that the father's act of telling his son that he was gay was against the advice of their child's counselor. The appellate court held that, while the father violated the understanding he had with his child's counselor, that understanding was not the equivalent of an order of the court, thus the father's violation of that understanding was not a contemptuous act.


OUTCOME: The chancellor's finding of contempt was reversed, and the chancellor's issuance of the restraining order was affirmed. The order had not expired and remained in effect. The case was remanded. Costs were assessed equally against the parties.

Hale v. Culpepper


No. M2002-01955-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 899


September 3, 2003, Session  
December 22, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Coffee County. No. 30713. L. Craig Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Coffee County (Tennessee) that awarded visitation to the child's maternal grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court erred by granting visitation to the grandmother. The court of appeals agreed. The trial court found that prior to the mother's death there existed a significant relationship between the child and his grandmother. However, regardless of whether the evidence supported that finding, there was simply no evidence of the danger of substantial harm to the child because of the cessation of that relationship or otherwise. There was no evidence that the father was anything but a fit parent or that the child was in any danger of harm from his living environment or from the father's parenting decisions. The trial court found that the total absence of a relationship with the grandmother and the maternal side of his family would result in substantial harm to the child. There was simply no proof of such harm. The psychologist appointed by the trial court, relying in part on the child's statements, reported a conclusion contrary to that finding. Therefore, the trial court erred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Admiralty Suites & Inns, L.L.C. v. Shelby County


No. W2002-02155-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


138 S.W.3d 233; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 835


March 31, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
November 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Admiralty Suites & Inns v. Shelby County, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 406 (Tenn., May 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. No. 99-0036-3. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, certain hotels, motels, and taxpayers, challenged a decision from the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which entered judgment in favor of defendant municipalities by finding that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1425 (2003) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1425 (2003) governed occupancy taxes on hotels and motels. The hotels, motels, and the taxpayers challenged the constitutionality of § 67-4-1425. After the trial court determined that § 67-4-1425 was constitutional, an appeal was filed. On review, the court determined that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to hear some of the claims. The taxpayers were not required to pay the tax "under protest" pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-911 before challenging the tax. The claims against one municipality should have been dismissed for lack of ripeness because the tax had not been imposed there. Further, the hotels and motels lacked standing to bring the action because they were not the taxpayers in the case. Turning to the merits of the case, the court determined that the proper standard of review was the rational basis standard. The court held that the double taxation exclusions in Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-1425(c), (d) (2003) did not violate Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 8 and Tenn. Const. art. 11, § 8. The rapid growth of other counties excluded from double taxation was a reason to justify the classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision regarding the claims against one municipality and the claims brought by the hotels and motels. The rest of the trial court's decision was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC.


No. E2002-01143-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 821


July 2, 2003, Session  
November 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 499 (Tenn., June 1, 2004)
Affirmed by, Remanded by City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 606 (Tenn., June 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] This appeal questions the constitutionality of Knoxville Code § 16-468 and asserts that the Trial Court erred in its grant of a temporary injunction against the Appellant, Entertainment Resources, LLC. We declare the ordinance unconstitutional, reverse the judgment of the Trial Court and remand. Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Cause Remanded. No. 98-140736-2. Daryl Fansler, Chancellor. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant video company (company) sought review of the decision of the Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which found in favor of appellee City of Knoxville (city) in the city's action alleging that the company violated the City of Knoxville Code § 16-468 by operating an "adult bookstore."


OVERVIEW: The company owned and operated videotape movie rental stores and opened up a store in Knoxville where it began selling and renting videotapes for home viewing. The front room of the store was stocked with a mix of videotapes rated G, PG-13, and R, and the back room of the store was stocked with sexually explicit X-rated tapes. The city filed a complaint requesting that temporary and permanent injunctions be issued against the company alleging that it violated Knoxville City Code § 16-468 because it was operating an "adult bookstore" in violation of that section. The trial court enjoined the company from operating the video store, but the court reversed, stating that § 16-468 was unconstitutional and unenforceable. The court stated that the problem with the use of terms such as "significant" or "substantial" contained in § 16-468 was that they must suffice for application to a wide range of situations across a broad spectrum. Without more specificity, there would be inevitable disagreement as to those situations near the middle of the spectrum. Thus, § 16-468 was unconstitutionally vague, and therefore unenforceable. The temporary injunction violated Tenn. R. Civ. P. 65.02(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and declared the relevant City of Knoxville Code section unconstitutional. The court further remanded the cause as to the matter of damages.

 

1274 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Toyota Motor Credit Corp. v. State Dep't of Safety


No. M2003-00147-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 792


September 5, 2003, Session  
November 7, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-2062-II. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge by Interchange.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A leased vehicle was seized pursuant to laws that provided for the forfeiture of a vehicle used in the commission of a person's second or subsequent offense of driving while intoxicated. Appellee credit corporation owned the vehicle. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, held that appellant, the Tennessee Department of Safety, failed to give the credit corporation proper notice of the forfeiture proceeding. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department sent certified letters containing information about the forfeiture warrant to the credit corporation (for a major automobile manufacturer) at the address listed on the vehicle's certificate of title and registration. However, the certified letter sent to the credit corporation was returned and marked "Not Deliverable as Addressed Unable to Forward." Thereupon, the Department issued a summary order of forfeiture. The trial court noted the credit corporation was the kind of entity that anyone with the least bit of sense would have known could have been located with little effort. Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 prohibited the State from taking property without due process of law. The appellate court noted that adequate notice was an essential element of due process, and notice had to be given in a manner reasonably calculated to notify all interested parties of the pending forfeiture. Here, no such effort was made. Because the Department failed to exert the minimal effort required to ascertain the credit corporation's correct address, it was deprived of the opportunity to be present at a hearing to assert its claim. Thus, the notice failed to satisfy due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs on appeal were taxed to the Department.

 

1275 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Goodman v. City of Savannah


No. W2002-02898-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


148 S.W.3d 88; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 788


May 21, 2003, Session  
November 5, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Goodman v. City of Savannah & Savannah Bd. of Comm'Rs, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 444 (Tenn., May 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hardin County. No. 5999. Ron E. Harmon, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firefighter who was employed by appellee city and forced to retire at age 62 pursuant to the city's mandatory retirement policy, filed a lawsuit against the city asserting that the mandatory retirement policy violated the Tennessee Human Rights Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-401, by discriminating against him based on his age. The Chancery Court for Hardin County (Tennessee) granted summary judgment for the city. The firefighter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The firefighter argued that the city was required to show age to have been a bona fide occupational qualification (BFOQ). The parties did not dispute that the city was permitted to establish age 62 as a mandatory retirement age if it had proven age to have been a BFOQ for a firefighter. The threshold issue was whether the city was required to prove that age was a BFOQ. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, at Jackson, held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-36-205 authorized the city to adopt a mandatory retirement policy, not less than 60 years old, for firefighters, without being required to establish age as a BFOQ. Since the Tennessee legislature could not, of course, carve out an exception to the federal statute prohibiting age discrimination, § 8-36-205 included the proviso that the mandatory age requirement not violate the federal act. No such reference was made to the prohibition against age discrimination in the Tennessee Human Rights Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-401. The legislature intended to create an express exception to the Tennessee statute prohibiting age discrimination, to permit a municipality to adopt a mandatory age requirement for firefighters without having to show a BFOQ.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs were taxed to the firefighter.

 

1276 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Tenn. Waste Movers, Inc. v. Loudon County


No. E2002-02490-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 766


July 1, 2003, Session  
October 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Tenn. Waste Movers, Inc. v. Louden County, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 363 (Tenn., May 3, 2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by Tenn. Waste Movers, Inc. v. Loudon County, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 223 (Tenn., Mar. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Loudon County. No. 10100. Frank V. Williams, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill operator filed an application with appellee county commission seeking to expand an existing landfill in the county. The application was filed pursuant to the provisions of the "Jackson Law," Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-211-701, et seq. The commission denied the application. After petitioning for judicial review, the Chancery Court for Loudon County (Tennessee) held in favor of the commission. The landfill operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the operator contended that the trial court's consideration of the facts in light of the "substantial and material evidence" rule and its determination that the commission acted "arbitrarily or capriciously" were improper, as the Jackson Law's mandate of de novo review was, according to the operator, clearly a "species of the statutory writ of certiorari." The "substantial and material evidence rule" and the "arbitrary or capricious rule" required that some substantial reason be proven for refusing the permit before the commission could validly refuse the permit. Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-211-704(c) required the reviewing court to consider all evidence presented to the commission, plus any relevant evidence presented to the trial court and to decide de novo the factual question of whether a fact or facts exist which justified the refusal of the permit. Following Tucker, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's interpretation of de novo review under the Jackson Law. The trial court correctly refused to substitute its independent judgment for that of the commission, since such a substitution was "clearly not the legislative intent."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the case was remanded for the collection of costs assessed below, pursuant to applicable law. Costs on appeal were taxed to the landfill operator.
