Hunter v. Ura


No. M2002-02573-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 755


August 7, 2003, Session  
October 28, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Hunter v. Ura, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 254 (Tenn., Mar. 22, 2004)
Reversed by Hunter v. Ura, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 306 (Tenn., Mar. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated and Remanded. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 96C-3784. The Honorable Marietta M. Shipley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the administratrix of estate of deceased husband, filed a wrongful death action against defendants, an anesthesiologist and anesthesia services group. The jury in the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, returned a verdict for plaintiff, finding defendants at fault and awarding damages for medical and funeral expenses, and the pecuniary value of the life of the deceased. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: During voir dire in a medical malpractice trial, plaintiff exercised eight peremptory challenges. Ultimately, the jury found for plaintiff. On review, the court of appeals held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 22-3-105 (1994) limited a single plaintiff party in a civil action to four peremptory challenges. The trial court's failure to comply with the procedural guidelines set forth in § 22-3-105 constituted prejudice to the judicial process, and required a reversal in this case under Tenn. R. App. P. 36(b). The court of appeals also found reversible error in the improper use of medical literature to impeach an expert witness' credibility; counsel failed to establish the literature as reliable authority. Counsel also erred in asking the expert to cite to medical authority supporting his position on cross-examination. The trial court did not err in retrospective application of a rule allowing decedent's family to recovery loss of consortium damages. The trial judge did not improperly comment upon the evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment on the jury verdict was vacated, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1278 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Yovanovitch


No. M2002-01164-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 656


March 18, 2003 Session, Argued  
September 11, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. No. 97D-66. Muriel Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee mother's action for an increase in child support, appellant father challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), including the father's income in excess of $ 10,000 per month in calculating his child support obligation. Appellant attorney general filed a notice of appeal to defend the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-101(e)(1)(B).


OVERVIEW: The trial court made a factual finding that the father's gross income was $ 275,000 per year. Accordingly, child support was set at $ 3,342 per month. On appeal, the father asserted that the mother failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that the child support based on income greater than $ 10,000 per month was reasonably necessary to provide for the needs for the minor child, as contemplated in Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-101(e)(1)(B). The appellate court held that the mother showed that child support based on the father's net income in excess of $ 10,000 per month was reasonably necessary to provide for the child, as the mother was unable to afford her half of the child's private school education expenses, and she testified that if she received more child support, she would re-enroll the child in private school, and would provide art and dance lessons, as well as educational travel. Additionally, although the trial court did not use the term "reasonably necessary," its written finding was equivalent to a finding that the increased support was reasonably necessary to provide for the child's needs. Finally, the constitutional issue was waived by the mother.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, the mother's request for attorney's fees for the appeal was granted, and the case was remanded for a determination of the amount of attorney's fees for the appeal. Costs on appeal were taxed to the father and his surety, for which execution could issue, if necessary.

State Dep't of Children's Servs. v. R.S.


No. M2002-00919-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 657


April 10, 2003 Session Argued  
September 11, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Vacated in Part, and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Franklin County. No. 12,188-CV. Buddy D. Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Vacated in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Tennessee Department of Children's Services, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Franklin County (Tennessee), which denied its petition to terminate appellee parents' rights to their three minor children and ordered the children returned to the parents.


OVERVIEW: The Department filed a petition to terminate the parents' rights to their three children on the ground that one of the children was sexually abused by the father. The trial court denied the petition and ordered the children returned to the parents. On appeal, the Department contended that there was clear and convincing evidence to support termination. The court found that there had been no judicial finding of child abuse. There was no physical evidence of sexual abuse against any of the children. The Department did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that the father abused any of the children. The court further found that the Department failed to provide clear and convincing proof that the parents had abandoned the children by willful failure to support or visit. The Department's records refuted the claim that the parents demonstrated a lack of concern in the months immediately following removal of the children from their custody. The Department failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence the existence of any one ground for termination. However, the court found that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to order the children's return home.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the petition. The court vacated the order requiring a home study and directing the Department to prepare a plan for the return of the children to the parents. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

Dep't of Children's Servs. v. C. L.


No. M2001-02729-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 606


January 6, 2003, Session  
August 29, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Davidson County. No. 9919-47933. Andrei E. Lee, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents appealed the judgment of the Juvenile Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) that terminated their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by terminating his parental rights because he did not abandon the children. The court of appeals agreed. The father's conduct throughout the case did not evince a purpose to forego parental claims to his children or an overall lack of parental responsibility. To the contrary, the father sought custody early on and continued to seek custody. The only apparent and expressed reason the State took the children in custody after removing them from the mother's home was the unsuitability of the father's housing. The father attempted to comply with directives given him by the State, and it stated that he had substantially complied with those requirements. He cooperated with workers and agencies that attempted to help him. Therefore, the trial court erred in finding that the father had abandoned his children.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Nunley v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2002-02032-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 601


May 19, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
August 27, 2003, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review from the judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), challenging the denial of his request for placement at a minimum security facility.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought placement at a minimum security facility and claimed that the denial was based upon the fact that he allegedly had an escape charge and/or history. Specifically, the inmate challenged his security reclassification from minimum security trustee to minimum direct custody based upon the implementation of a new rule, regulation, law, policy, and/or practice. He sought a writ of certiorari, a declaratory judgment, and injunctive relief. The trial court dismissed the inmate's petition for failure to state a claim. The inmate appealed, contending that the application of the new rule, regulation, law, policy, and/or practice to his earlier infraction violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws and that the defendants were acting in an arbitrary, illegal, and unconstitutional manner. The court affirmed the trial court, finding that a writ of certiorari was not available, as there was no action taken by an inferior tribunal, board, or officer exercising judicial functions. The court further found that the case did not involve a violation of the ex post facto prohibition and that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to otherwise consider the inmate's petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed. The case was remanded.

Baldwin v. Tenn. Bd. of Paroles


No. M2002-01428-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


125 S.W.3d 429; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 575


April 1, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
August 15, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Baldwin v. Tenn. Bd. of Paroles, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1266 (Tenn., Dec. 22, 2003)
Related proceeding at Baldwin v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 706 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 01-2533-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner in the custody of the Tennessee Department of Correction became eligible for parole after serving over 20 years of his sentence. The Tennessee Board of Paroles conducted a hearing and voted to deny him parole. They also decided to defer further parole consideration for another 20 years. The prisoner filed a petition for writ of certiorari, which the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) denied. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both versions of the rule at issue stated that, if the case was continued or parole denied, a future hearing date should be specified, with the 1 year requirement deleted from the amended rule. The state's argument implied that the amended rule granted the board absolute and unbridled discretion over the timing of subsequent hearings. It appeared to the appellate court that the statutes relating to the Board of Paroles, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-28-116(a)(1) and 40-28-118(d), did not support that interpretation. Under the board's ruling, it was possible that the entire membership of the board could completely turn over more than once before the prisoner's case came up for decision again. The board's decision constituted an arbitrary withdrawal of the power to parole from future board members, and a 20-year deferral would undermine the very provisions of the parole statutes that empowered the board to grant parole. In addition, the essential effect of the board's action was to change the prisoner's sentence to life without parole, contrary to what the legislature intended. The appellate court held that the prisoner stated a cause of action that entitled him to a writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The costs on appeal were taxed to the Tennessee Board of Paroles.

Sherwood v. Microsoft Corp.


No. M2000-01850-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 539; 2003-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,109


January 31, 2001, Session  
July 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Sherwood v. Microsoft Corp., 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 648 (Tenn., Aug. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal By Permission. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 99C-3562 Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant software company appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), holding that plaintiff indirect purchasers of the company's software had a cause of action against the company pursuant to the Tennessee Trade Practice Act (TTPA) and the Tennessee Consumer Protection Act (TCPA). The indirect purchasers of the software appealed the decision of the trial court dismissing the claims of the direct purchasers.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers filed suit seeking damages, injunctive relief, and equitable remedies under the TTPA, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 47-25-101 to -2704, and the TCPA, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 47-18-101 to -1808. The purchasers bought the company's software, either separately or loaded in a computer. They alleged that the company engaged in conduct that eliminated or retarded the development of new software products that could support or become alternative platforms to the company's operating systems. They also contended that the price that they paid for their software was higher than it would have been in a competitive market. The appellate court concluded that the purchasers sufficiently alleged substantial effects on commerce within the State to state a claim under the TTPA and that the indirect purchasers could sue for injury caused them by violations of the TTPA. Thus, the trial court properly denied the company's motion to dismiss the purchasers' TTPA claims. However, the purchasers' TCPA claims had to be dismissed, as their claims based upon anticompetitive conduct were not cognizable under the TCPA. Thus, the trial court erred in denying the company's motion to dismiss those claims.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's denial of the company's motion to dismiss the TCPA claims. The appellate court affirmed the denial of the motion to dismiss the TTPA claims.

Far Tower Sites, L.L.C. v. Knox County


No. E2002-00647-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


126 S.W.3d 52; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 533


December 11, 2002 Session  
July 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by, Adhered to Far Tower Sites, L.L.C. v. Knox County, 126 S.W.3d 52, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 583 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 1-782-98. John F. Weaver, Chancellor. 1


1 Far Tower's earlier-filed petition for writ of certiorari was pending before Chancellor Weaver when this circuit court action was filed and consolidated with the chancery court matter. When the certiorari petition was voluntarily dismissed, Chancellor Weaver agreed to hear the circuit court case.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Knox County (Tennessee). The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendants, a county and the Tennessee Technology Corridor Development Authority (development authority), and dismissed the company's complaint, which had alleged that the county committed a taking when it revoked the company's permit to construct a cellular tower.


OVERVIEW: The company executed a sublease agreement that allowed it to construct a cellular telecommunications tower, for which the sublessor had obtained a building permit. After the sublease was executed, the company secured a new building permit in its own name. The county closed down the project when it received complaints from residents, who had discovered that the company had not obtained a certificate of appropriateness (COA) from the development authority, a prerequisite for a building permit. A county commission ruled in favor of the residents. The company alleged in its lawsuit against defendants that it acquired vested property rights in the building permit. The trial court entered judgment for defendants. The court affirmed. The issuance of a COA was a prerequisite to the issuance of a valid building permit, and the company's failure to obtain a COA before seeking the permit rendered the issued permit invalid. The company thus had not acquired a vested property right in the invalid permit. The company could not rely on estoppel because the statute that set forth the COA requirement, the Tennessee Technology Corridor Development Authority Act, was in the public domain.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.

State v. Stewart (In re L.J.C.)


No. W2001-01799-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


124 S.W.3d 609; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 515


November 7, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
July 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State Dep't of Child's Servs. v. Stewart (In re L.J.C.), 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1288 (Tenn., Dec. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Vacated in Part; Affirmed in Part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Tipton County. No. J4427. William A. Peeler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in Part; Affirmed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the judgment of the Juvenile Court for Tipton County (Tennessee) that terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by terminating her parental rights because the mother followed her permanency plan. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court found that the mother used "subterfuges" to resume her relationship with her boyfriend in contradiction to the stated goal of protecting the children from an alleged sexual perpetrator, and when finally confronted by the State, the mother admitted to being five months pregnant with the boyfriend's child. The trial court found that the mother's relationship with the boyfriend continued even at the time of the hearing. The permanency plan also required a stable home for the children. The mother had moved 13 times between 1994 and the time of the hearing, and, thus, had not provided a stable home. The mother acknowledged living at nine different addresses. The mother, by her own admission, was not in compliance with the counseling requirement. There was clear and convincing evidence of the mother's substantial noncompliance with the permanency plan, and therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The portion of the juvenile court's judgment finding that the mother willfully failed to support her children was vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

McCrone v. Richardson(In re Adoption of McCrone)


No. W2001-02795-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 510


March 31, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
July 21, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Reversed and Remanded. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-01-0321-1. Walter L. Evans, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) that denied her petition for adoption and granted appellee father's petition for custody, determining that the father had not abandoned the children and that substantial harm would not result from his having custody.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother argued that the trial court erred by awarding custody to the father because the evidence preponderated against the trial court's finding that the father did not willfully abandon the children. The court of appeals agreed. It was undisputed that the father knew where his children were and where to send the child support payments had he chosen to do so. The father's only explanation for his failure to support was that sometimes he did not make much money, and that his income depended on the jobs he received. It was therefore established by undisputed evidence that the father's failure to pay child support was willful. In addition, the father had abandoned the children for an extended period of time. Indeed, as of the date of the divorce, it was clear that the father had in fact abandoned them. The mother brought the children to Birmingham, where the father was living, and they saw him there. The father's visitation with the children as of the date of the divorce could only be characterized as "token." Therefore, the trial court erred by awarding custody to the father.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Doe v. Pedigo


No. E2002-01311-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 465


February 12, 2003, Session  
June 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, On rehearing at Doe v. Pedigo, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 605 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn.R.App.P 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Cause Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 2-380-95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which granted summary judgment on all claims to defendant county and defendant sheriff, and summary judgment on most claims to defendant county medical examiner. The minor had alleged liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 8-8-302, 8-19-301, and 29-20-205, after the examiner drugged the minor and took nude pictures of him.


OVERVIEW: The minor, who had an interest in a medical career, drove around with the examiner in the examiner's county vehicle for the purpose of observing him on the job. At one point, the examiner invited the minor back to the examiner's home where he drugged him and took nude photos of him. The court held that the county was not negligent under § 29-20-205 of the Governmental Tort Liability Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-20-205, because there was no evidence that any county employee was, or should have been, aware of the examiner's propensity to sedate and photograph young men. Although the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the county and the sheriff under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, it did vacate the grant of summary judgment to the examiner under § 1983 in his individual capacity because there was an issue of whether he misused his power and position as examiner in order to coerce the minor into a situation where he could be taken advantage of. The court also vacated the grant of summary judgment in favor of the county under Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-8-302 because there was an issue as to whether the examiner was acting as a deputy sheriff under color of his office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

State v. Any & All Parties with an Interest in Prop. Identified As Tax Map 158


No. M2002-01137-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 448


March 20, 2003, Session  
June 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation December 22, 2003.
As Corrected July 22, 2003.
Appeal denied by State v. Any & All Parties with an Interest in Prop. Identified As Tax Map 158, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 1272 (Tenn., Dec. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 99-1278-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for termination of use of land as a cemetery. Appellants, landowners, a tax assessor's office, and an interest group, filed a counter petition seeking money damages as well as an injunction preventing disinterment of the graves. The State filed a motion to dismiss the counter petition. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, granted the State's motion. Appellants filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State petitioned to disinter ancient Native American remains located on State property that had been acquired by eminent domain. The issue before the court on appeal was the dismissal of a counter petition filed by appellants after the court denied their right to intervene in the action. The court determined that appellants could not appeal the dismissal of their counter petition, as there never was a valid counter petition. In order for appellants to have filed a valid counter petition, they would have had to have been parties to the action which, by virtue of the denial of their motion to intervene, they were not. The grant of amicus curiae status upon appellants did not create a vested interest sufficient to prevent the State from taking a voluntary dismissal. The court's decision did not prejudice appellants' ability to have their concerns addressed, because the constitutionality of the encapsulation of the burial sites in concrete and subsequent paving over of the sites was being challenged in a separate lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State Dep't of Children's Servs. v. RB


No. E2002-01950-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 428


May 12, 2003, Session  
June 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. RB, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 962 (Tenn., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Carter County. No. J16615. Hon. John W. Walton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Carter County, Tennessee, entered an order terminating appellant father's parental rights based upon his failure to pay child support. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the father's testimony regarding his attempts to pay support was not credible and that his parental rights warranted termination for wilfully failing to support or make reasonable payments toward the support of his minor child. On appeal, the father argued the trial court erred by relying on a statute that had been declared unconstitutional to terminate his parental rights. The appellate court held willful non-payment of child support or failure to make reasonable payments toward child support for four consecutive months immediately preceding the filing of the petition to terminate rights, established a basis to sever a parent's relationship with his child. The appellate court noted the state supreme court had previously found later statutory definitions of abandonment unconstitutional because they effectively created an irrebuttable presumption that a mere failure to pay support constituted abandonment and reinstated the definition in Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(A)(I) (Supp. 1994). The appellate court concluded the trial court applied the correct legal standard and properly terminated the father's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and remanded with the cost of the appeal assessed to the father.

Tenn. Dep't of Children's Servs. v. R.G.T.

April 7, 2003, Assigned on Briefs

DISPOSITION: Affirmed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed from an order of the Juvenile Court for Greene County (Tennessee) terminating his parental rights to the youngest of five minor children.


OVERVIEW: The court had previously terminated the father's parental rights to the siblings of the child at issue, based in large part on his mental incompetence. After giving the father a second chance to establish a relationship with the child based on a psychological finding that he and the mother worked nicely as a team, appellee Department of Children's Services petitioned to terminate father's parental rights, alleging that he willfully abandoned the child by failing to pay child support, that the conditions that led to the child's removal persisted, and that he was mentally incompetent to parent the child. The court terminated his parental rights. On appeal, the father argued that no specific order had ever been entered requiring him to pay child support, so it was error to base the termination on his wilful failure to pay. However, the court noted that a parent's obligation of support was so obvious that the father's professed lack of knowledge militated for terminating his rights. The termination was upheld as being in the best interest of the child.

Tucker Corp. v. City of Clarksville


No. M2002-00627-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 401



May 30, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as a Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. C9-299. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee), which granted defendant city's motion for summary judgment in an action challenging the validity of Clarksville, Tenn., Codified Ordinance § 13-309.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was involved in the construction business. The city owned and operated a municipal water and sewer system. Under Clarksville, Tenn., Codified Ordinance § 13-309, a connection fee was based on the square footage of a house The corporation filed an action challenging the validity of § 13-309. After the trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment, the corporation sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the city was authorized to charge connection fees for new connections to a water or sewer system, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-34-104. However, the city did not have the authority to levy a tax for such a purpose. The fees did not constitute a tax because the revenues generated were not paid into the city's general fund. Moreover, they were not levied or used for the purpose of paying the city's general debts and liabilities. Further, Clarksville, Tenn., Codified Ordinance § 13-309 did not violate equal protection because there was a reasonable basis for the connection fee. Because the reasonable basis test was met, there was no violation of equal protection merely because there was a resulting inequality.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

State Dep't of Children's Servs. v. B.L.K.


No. E2002-01724-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 360



May 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 169,829 and 169,830 and 169,831. Suzanne Bailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) determined there were sufficient grounds to terminate appellant mother's parental rights to her three youngest children. The mother appealed, and claimed that appellee department of children's services (DCS) failed to prove that there were sufficient grounds to terminate her parental rights and that such termination would be in the best interests of the children.


OVERVIEW: The mother contacted DCS and asked for assistance in caring for her five minor children and informed DCS that she was two months behind on her rent, was having emotional problems, and was undergoing counseling. DCS obtained temporary custody of the five minor children. DCS later sought to terminate the mother's parental rights. Custody of the mother's two oldest children was transferred to their biological father. A permanency plan was developed with the stated goal of returning the children to the mother. The mother admitted that she was unable to care for the children for the two years they were in DCS custody. The present court did not believe that the juvenile court committed any reversible error in reaching its conclusion that clear and convincing evidence existed to terminate the mother's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the juvenile court was affirmed, and the cause was remanded to the juvenile court. The costs on appeal were assessed against the mother.

Wing v. Estate of Wing


No. M2001-01598-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 287



April 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Wing v. Parchman, 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 226 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 96D-1174. Marietta Shipley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) ordered a husband involved in a divorce to pay $ 230 per week in support payments to appellee wife after the husband retired. The husband designated his daughter as the beneficiary to receive the payments if he died within the 120 month period. After the husband's untimely death, the court ordered appellants, his ex-employer and/or his daughter, to make the payments to the wife and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both the daughter and the ex-employer objected to having been made parties and the court originally sustained the objection. But without any further process having being served, the court ordered them to take steps necessary to have seen that the wife received part of the pension. The appellate court held that the court's order was void because of a lack of jurisdiction over the ex-employer and the daughter. The trial court's subsequent joinder of the ex-employer and the daughter had no effect on the invalid judgment. In 1988 the General Assembly provided that a pension could be reached to provide support under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-501. That remained the only exception, however; therefore, the pension could not have been assigned to a spouse as a division of property. So, even with jurisdiction over the ex-employer it would have been an error to have ordered the ex-employer to have divided the pension. One way to divide a pension was to order the recipient to pay part of it to the other spouse. That was apparently what the trial court intended to do in the case at bar, but the order could not have bound the daughter because she had not been a party to it.


OUTCOME: The court's order attempting to bind the daughter and the ex-employer was reversed and the ex-employer was dismissed. The cause was remanded for further proceedings. The costs were taxed to the wife.

 

1296 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Dickson v. State


No. M2002-01426-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


116 S.W.3d 738; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 275



April 9, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-2823-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tennessee Petroleum Underground Storage Tank Act (USTA) made the release of petroleum from underground tanks illegal. Appellant service station owner contested a fine imposed by appellee Tennessee Department of Environment and Conservation (TDEC). The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) held that Tenn. Const. art. VI § 14 did not preclude imposition of a fine, even though the fine was punitive. The service station owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The TDEC found that the service station owner failed to submit a Site Status Monitoring Report on two occasions. Hence the total of $ 15,000 in penalties. Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14 had a provision called the "Fifty Dollar Clause," which provided no fine could be laid on any citizen that exceeded $ 50 dollars, unless it was assessed by a jury of a person's peers. The inquiry on appeal boiled down to a question of whether the latter provision applied to the government as a whole or only to the judiciary. The appellate court concluded that Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14 did apply only to the judiciary and not to the government as a whole. The statute under which the Board assessed the service station owner was titled "Civil Penalty," Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-215-121. Giving the TDEC the benefit of the doubt, the appellate court would not say that the service station owner's assessment was punitive, based on § 68-215-121 alone. However, the appellate court held the two $ 7,500 fines must have been assessed primarily to punish the service station owner, and they would be subject to the Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14 limitation, if that provision applied to administrative agencies.


OUTCOME: The chancery court's conclusion that the fines were remedial was reversed. The chancery court's judgment affirming the action of the petroleum underground storage tank board was affirmed. The cause was remanded to the chancery court for further proceedings. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the service station owner.

No. W2002-01648-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 232


February 3, 2003, Assigned on Brief  
March 21, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-01-2581-1. Walter L. Evans, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grocery store owner was found by appellee city beer board to have been in violation of a city ordinance prohibiting the sale of beer to a minor, Collierville, Tenn., City Ord. § 2-214. The board suspended the grocer's beer permit for 45 days. The grocer appealed and the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) affirmed the board. The grocer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grocer first contended that because the hearing before the board was opened with a prayer, that constituted a violation of the First Amendment of the Constitution of the United States and the board's action was therefore became a nullity. Based upon the record the appellate court found no violation of the Establishment Clause. The trial court's order stated that the court reviewed the administrative record, considered the additional testimony and documentary evidence offered by the grocer and found based upon said stipulations and the undisputed facts set forth in the administrative record, that the grocer had violated the ordinance by the sale of beer to a minor. The order indicated that the trial court had conducted a de novo review as it was required to have done. The testimony of the police officer was unchallenged and the past violations of the grocer, were stipulated. Collierville, Tenn., City Ord. § 2-223(8), allowed the board, in assessing a penalty, to have considered the past record of the permit holder and location. Having conducted a de novo review, the appellate court determined that the judgment of the trial court was supported by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the case was remanded. The costs of the appeal were taxed to the grocery store.

City of Oakland v. McCraw


No. W2002-01552-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


126 S.W.3d 29; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 234



March 17, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Fayette County. No. 12253. The Honorable William H. Inman, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed an action for injunctive and declaratory relief against defendants, a newly incorporated town, the county administrator of elections, the election committee and certain members, and the town mayor, claiming that Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-1-210(b) (2001), under which the town became incorporated, was unconstitutional. The Chancery Court for Fayette County (Tennessee) granted summary judgment to the city. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: An unincorporated territory voted to incorporate as a town, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-1-201 (1996). The city, which shared boundaries with the new town, filed the instant action to have the election declared invalid, arguing that Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-1-210(b) (amended 2001), which ratified the town's election, was unconstitutional. The town and the mayor claimed that the action was barred by the statute of limitations for election contests at Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-17-105 (1994). On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's grant of partial summary judgment to the city on constitutionality issue and the summary judgment for the city determining that the issue was not an election contest. The court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-1-210(b) (amended 2001) violated Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 9, as the statute enabled only certain territories to incorporate, namely those that held elections before a certain date, and there was no rational basis for the creation of that special class. The court also held that the city's claim was not an election contest, noting that the city had no standing to proceed in an election contest about a referendum involving the town's citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment for the city on the constitutionality of the statute at issue and the order granting the city's motion for summary judgment holding that the action was not an election contest. Costs of appeal were assessed against the town, the mayor, and members of county election commission and their sureties.

 

1300 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Smith County v. Enoch


No. M1999-00063-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 156


November 4, 1999, Assigned on Briefs  
February 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by Smith County v. Enoch, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 604 (Tenn., June 30, 2003)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Smith County v. Enoch, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 418 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 6, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county filed an action against appellee property owner to enjoin the maintenance of an automobile junkyard within 1,000 feet of a county road pursuant to the authority of 1987 Tenn. Priv. Acts chs. 95, and 97. The owner asserted that the county lacked standing and that the acts were unconstitutional. The Chancery Court for Smith County (Tennessee) sustained both the owner's defenses. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner first argued that the private acts violated Tenn. Const. arts. I, § 8 and 2, § 8, as well as the federal Equal Protection Clause, because they amounted to a suspension of the general law against the inhabitants of the county, and second, that the acts were so vague that they denied due process of law. The appellate court could have construed the private acts harmoniously with the general laws in the case at bar by determining if the statewide laws contemplated the possibility of stricter local regulations, which they did. The statutes applicable statewide provided that nothing in them should have been construed to have affected the provisions of any lawful ordinance, regulation or resolution that were more restrictive. Localities were thus left free under the statewide laws to regulate junkyards and automobile graveyards more rigorously than the state did. The appellate court held that the private acts were effectively county-specific regulations and their less-than-perfect wording presented a problem more of statutory ambiguity, than a case of unconstitutional vagueness. The appellate court also held that the trial court erred in holding at the county lacked standing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for further actions. Costs of the appeal were taxed to the property owner.

State v. A.N.G.


No. E2002-01114-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 157


January 30, 2003, Assigned on Briefs  
February 26, 2003, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents appealed the judgment of the Juvenile Court for Greene County (Tennessee) that terminated their parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by terminating their parental rights because the State had not proved the grounds necessary for the termination of their parental rights. The court of appeals disagreed. The parents were unemployed and did not have transportation. The mother admitted that she could not care for the children. It did not appear that the mother was actively looking for a job and there were no prospects on the horizon. The parents failed to maintain contact with one child. There was no proof that the father lived in a residence suitable for raising the children. The father did not remain drug free. There was no proof offered at trial that the conditions would be remedied in the near future. Therefore, the trial court properly terminated the parent's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1302 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re C.A.F.


No. M2002-00516-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


114 S.W.3d 524; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 134



February 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded. Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Putnam County. No. 603 DCS. Nolan R. Goolsby, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner department of children's services sought the termination of the parental rights of respondents, the three-year-old child's mother, biological father, and another man who had signed a voluntary acknowledgement of paternity. The Juvenile Court for Putnam County, Tennessee, terminated the parental rights of the mother and the biological father, but not of the other man. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court based its ruling on a narrow reading of Tenn. Code Ann. § 24-7-113, to allow the other man to retain the parental status he had obtained as a result of his voluntary acknowledgement of paternity. On review, the department argued that such a narrow reading of the statute violated public policy. The appellate court agreed, finding that by limiting paternity challenges to the signatories to a voluntary acknowledgment, the trial court's decision would make that status virtually unassailable. This was an inappropriate construction of § 24-7-113 as it would defeat the clear intent of the paternity statutes. Contrary to the other man's argument, the evidence showed that fraud was involved in the execution of the voluntary acknowledgement of paternity. His attempt to circumvent the adoption statutes by using the voluntary acknowledgement also violated public policy. The mother failed to raise any constitutional questions at the termination hearing; the appellate court ruled that a finding of severe child abuse against any child created an obvious presumption of parental unfitness, and the incorporation of this presumption into statutory law was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The termination of the parental rights of the mother and the biological father was affirmed. The order of the trial court in regard to the parental rights of the other man was reversed and remanded.

 

1303 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Ashworth v. Greene County


No. E2002-00500-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 106



February 10, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Greene County. No. 97000074. Thomas R. Frierson, II, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, proprietress of a bed and breakfast (innkeeper), filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of 1986 Tenn. Priv. Acts 127, a hotel/motel privilege tax. The Chancery Court for Greene County (Tennessee) granted appellee county's summary judgment as to the claim, finding that the innkeeper was not the taxpayer under the act and, consequently, did not have standing to pursue her claim. The innkeeper appealed.


OVERVIEW: The innkeeper pointed out that she was the taxpayer with respect to "business taxes," pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-701, et seq., and "sales taxes," pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6- 101, et seq. She argued that it made no sense for her to have been the taxpayer on the "breakfast" revenue but not as to the "bed" portion of her income. Under the definition of "taxpayer" in 1986 Tenn. Priv. Acts 127, it was clear that the innkeeper was not the taxpayer. The Act imposed an obligation on an innkeeper to collect and remit the tax. The Act did not designate the operator as the taxpayer. Rather, the innkeeper was merely an agent for the purpose of collecting the tax from her guests. The money damages the innkeeper sought were not hers to claim. As she was not required to pay any taxes, any reimbursement to her would be a windfall to which she was not entitled. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, at Knoxville declined to "broaden" Tennessee's definition of standing just because of a possibility that an innkeeper might be required to remit a charged, but uncollected tax. The appellate court held that the innkeeper lacked standing to have sought the relief set forth in her complaint.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed. The costs on appeal were taxed to the innkeeper.

 

1304 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Osborn v. Marr (In re Marr)


No. M2001-02890-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 45



January 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application granted by Osborn v. Marr, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 539 (Tenn., May 27, 2003)
Vacated by, Dismissed by Osborn v. Marr, 127 S.W.3d 737, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 45 (Tenn., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Reversed and Remanded. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 28066. Russ Heldman, Chancellor.
Marr v. State, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 554 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee father pled guilty to and was imprisoned for especially aggravated robbery, committed prior to the birth of the parties' son. Appellant mother subsequently filed a petition to terminate the father's parental rights. The Chancery Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) declined to do so, because the evidence that the child would have been substantially harmed if the father kept his parental rights was insufficient. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the statutory ground for terminating parental rights had been met. On appeal, the appellate court had to address the issue of whether, once grounds for termination had been established, the trial court was required to have made a separate finding of substantial harm. Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(c) did not on its face require such a separate finding; the statute required a finding by clear and convincing evidence that grounds for termination existed, and that termination of the parental rights was in the child's best interest. The issue was whether the Tennessee Constitution required an additional finding of substantial harm as it pertained to the termination of parental rights based on § 36-1-113(g)(6) regarding a parent's incarceration. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, at Nashville, concluded that, where grounds were established pursuant to § 36-1-113(g)(6), regarding incarceration of a parent, a separate finding of substantial harm was not constitutionally required. The trial court clearly required the mother to have established substantial harm, beyond meeting the requirements of the termination statute. An erroneous legal standard was applied.


OUTCOME: An erroneous legal standard had been applied, and the case was reversed and remanded for the trial court to make a determination of the child's "best interests" in light of the correct legal standard.

Simmons v. Gath Baptist Church


No. M2001-02511-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


109 S.W.3d 370; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 51


July 30, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
January 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Simmons v. Gath Baptist Church, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 442 (Tenn., May 19, 2003)
Related proceeding at State v. Simmons, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 176 (Tenn., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Warren County. No. 909. Charles D. Haston, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-employee was arrested for child sexual abuse and brought an action against appellees, the church he once worked for, as well as against the department of children's services and other governmental agencies. He claimed that his arrest was procured by illegal or unconstitutional means. The Circuit Court for Warren County (Tennessee) dismissed the action for, inter alia, failure to state a claim. The ex-employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ex-employee listed 17 issues for review, most of which had nothing to do with the grounds upon which his pleading was dismissed. However, he did state that the statute of limitations should not have applied to him, as the county jail had not provided adequate resources for prisoners to do legal research and that the governmental defendants were not immune, as they were also sued in their individual capacities and for acting under color of state law. The appellate court found neither of those arguments persuasive. Tenn. R. Civ. P. 8.01 stated that the pleading required to initiate a civil suit had to contain, inter alia, a short and plain statement of the claim showing that the pleader was entitled to relief. Neither the ex-employee's initial motion nor his subsequent filings were sufficiently coherent to satisfy the simplified requirements. Instead, they asserted a welter of allegations and grievances against a large number of people, some of whom were named as defendants and some not. Most of the allegations were so lacking in sufficient particulars that it was difficult to determine what conduct each individual was alleged to have been guilty.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed and the case was remanded. The costs on appeal were taxed to the ex-employee.

 

1306 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Fuller v. Campbell


No. M2001-01719-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


109 S.W.3d 737; 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 36


May 31, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
January 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Fuller v. Campbell, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 533 (Tenn., May 27, 2003)
Appeal denied by Fuller v. Campbell, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 564 (Tenn., June 16, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County No. 01-684-III Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision from the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted appellee State's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The inmate sought a declaratory judgment stating that because of his medical condition the Department of Corrections should be required to test him for drugs by a patch rather than by a urine sample.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that the Declaratory Judgment Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-14-101 et seq., did not permit the filing of a suit against the state to construe statutes. The chancery court lacked the jurisdiction to hear a declaratory judgment action against the Department of Correction. Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 4-5-223 and 4-5-225 did not apply to the internal management of state government if the policy did not affect the private rights, privileges, or procedures available to the public. The chancellor held that the policy fell into that category, and on appeal the court agreed. The inmate did not allege that he was presently affected by the policy. He only alleged that he feared he might become subject to discipline sometime in the future if he was unable to give a urine sample.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the chancellor, remanded the cause to chancery for any further necessary proceedings, and taxed the costs on appeal to the inmate.

 

1307 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Marceaux v. Sundquist


No. M2002-01356-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


107 S.W.3d 527; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 942



December 31, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Marceaux v. Sundquist, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 282 (Tenn., Mar. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor. No. 02-423-1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed appellant citizen's complaint against appellees, Tennessee governor and others, alleging that appellees were guilty of kidnapping, extortion, and racketeering through the application of laws calling for mandatory car insurance, and the practice of routine car stops. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen argued that the trial court erred in finding that the complaint failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, and that the trial court abused its discretion in denying his motion for production and for exigency writ. The appellate court found that the trial court did not err in denying the citizen's request for production as the discovery was unduly burdensome or expensive. Denying the citizen's request for injunctive relief was proper as there was little chance that the citizen's complaint could succeed on the merits, there was no threat of irreparable harm to the citizen, and public interest and interest-balancing considerations weighed in favor of appellees. Granting the citizen the relief he sought would bring law enforcement and all branches of state government to a halt in Tennessee. The citizen failed to demonstrate that appellees, through any of the alleged wrongs, caused the citizen a distinct and palpable injury, or that application of the Tennessee Financial Responsibility Act, which the citizen claimed was unconstitutional, had injuriously affected him. As such, the citizen lacked standing as to all claims presented.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1308 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville


No. M2001-00923-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


122 S.W.3d 148; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 927



December 31, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville County, 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 71 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 28, 2003)
Appeal denied by Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 656 (Tenn., July 7, 2003)
Appeal after remand at Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 304 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated in Part and Affirmed in Part. A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. Nos. 98-3317-III; 98-3400-II(III). The Honorable Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Vacated in Part and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trash haulers filed suit against defendant city, challenging the legality of certain fees. The suit was consolidated with the city's action against the trash haulers for collection of the unpaid fees. The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, entered summary judgment for the city. The trash haulers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The matter involved a dispute over tipping fees, which were fees on waste deliveries to a disposal facility that were assessed by the city against trash haulers. On appeal, the following issues were presented: (1) whether the tipping fee constituted double taxation; (2) whether the tipping fee violated equal protection rights; (3) whether the tipping fee was a flow control mechanism; and (4) whether the tipping fee was an unlawful restraint of trade. While the trash haulers suffered financial loss, the customers, not the haulers, bore the ultimate brunt of shouldering these costs. The tipping fees were fees, not taxes. The equal protection argument hinged on the theory that non-uniform fees were imposed in a single class. Under the circumstances, the trash haulers' equal protection rights were not violated. Moreover, there was a rational basis to justify these fees. The tipping fees also did not constitute an illegal flow control device. The tipping fees were not designed to force haulers in the area to strictly and exclusively dispose of collected waste at a certain facility. Finally, the city was authorized to impose and collect tipping fees upon the disposal of solid waste.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Tenn. Dep't of Health v. Boyle


No. M2001-01738-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 894



December 19, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 99-1343-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Tennessee Department of Health/Health Facilities Commission (HFC) filed a petition to hold defendant owners in civil contempt for operating a clinic that performed a substantial number of abortions without a certificate of need from HFC and a license from the department. The Chancery Court of Davidson County (Tennessee) held the owners in contempt and enjoined the clinic from operating without a certificate and a license. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The clinic owners asserted that Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-11-201(3) requiring a doctor's office to obtain a certificate of need and a license to operate if a "substantial number" of abortions were performed in the office did not satisfy the constitutional requirement of due process under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8. Tenn. Code Ann. § 68- 11-213(b)(2) made the operation of an ambulatory surgical treatment center (ASTC) without a license a crime. The appellate court believed that the owners had standing to challenge the statute on the vagueness ground. The appellate court found the statute was unconstitutional because it failed to give fair notice of what it required and because it encouraged arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. To the extent that there was any basis for distinguishing between a doctor who occasionally performed an abortion in his office and one whose practice was primarily devoted to such procedures, the regulations appeared to run contrary to sound health policy. The appellate court concluded that the statute adversely impacted a constitutionally protected right to privacy without a compelling State reason to justify it.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, dismissed the contempt charge, declared the statute requiring the clinic owners to obtain a certificate of need and a license unconstitutional, and remanded the case to the trial court.

Decatur County v. Vulcan Materials Co.


No. W2001-00858-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 876



December 12, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Decatur County v. Vulcan Materials Co., 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 455 (Tenn., May 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Decatur County. No. 2624. Ron E. Harmon, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mineral companies filed a lawsuit in the Chancery Court for Decatur County, Tennessee, challenging the constitutionality of a mineral severance tax increase assessed by appellee county. The trial court found the tax constitutional. The mineral companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The general assembly enacted a public act authorizing counties to collect a mineral severance tax provided the funds were deposited in the county road fund. Later, the general assembly passed another private act allowing the county to allocate the revenue from the tax to the county's general fund and to increase the tax. The mineral companies unsuccessfully opposed the tax increase, arguing the tax was unconstitutional because the funds were being deposited into the county general fund rather than into the county road fund. The county argued the mineral companies were estopped from challenging the increase because they did not make payment under protest. The appellate court initially noted in a suit to recover taxes paid after January 1, 1986, payment of the tax under protest was not a condition precedent to a claim against the governmental entity imposing the tax. The appellate court held the tax increase bore a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental interest, did not discriminate in the manner in which it was collected, and was properly applied to the general fund.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part; however, the portion of the judgment holding the mineral companies were not required to pay the tax in protest, that they did not have standing to sue, and were estopped from contesting the constitutionality of the tax was reversed.

In re R.C.V.


No. W2001-02102-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 811



November 18, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County. No. J2905. The Honorable George Blancett, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Tennessee juvenile court ordered the termination of the parents' rights to their two children. The appellate court reversed, because the trial court failed to inform the father of his right to counsel. In a second trial, the Juvenile Court of Memphis and Shelby County (Tennessee) found clear and convincing evidence justifying termination of the parents' rights and that termination was in the children's best interests. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that mother put nothing in the record as to how the special judge's appointment violated Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 11, and the State supreme court held the appointment of a juvenile court referee as special judge did not violate Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 4 requiring that judges be elected. The appellate court determined that the mother's due process rights were not violated by unfair procedures at trial, where her counsel failed to make a hearsay objection to a case worker's testimony concerning the contents of Tennessee Department of Children's Services (DCS) records. The appellate court held that the manner in which the special judge conducted the trial did not rise to the level of reversible error. The appellate court found that the mother's own testimony, along with the entire record, provided clear and convincing evidence sufficient to terminate her parental rights under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1- 113(g)(8)(B)(i). The appellate court concluded that the record adequately established that termination of parental rights was in the children's best interests. The appellate court opined that DCS made reasonable efforts for reunification of the family.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment terminating the mother's parental rights.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the State, filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of appellant, the mother. The Juvenile Court for Hickman County, Tennessee, terminated the mother's parental rights to her two children on the grounds of willful abandonment. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother married the father. At the time, the mother had one daughter, whom the father adopted. The second daughter was later born. About five years after the parents married, the mother left the father and her children. The parents were divorced two years later. The mother had not seen the children since she left the father. The mother pleaded guilty to statutory rape of two boys. The father was later found to have sexually abused the two girls. The State successfully had the mother's parental rights terminated because she abused the girls as well as abandoned them. The court of appeals held that the mother willfully abandoned her two daughters. The two girls had severe emotional problems because of the abandonment, as well as because of their father's sexual abuse. The best interests of the children rested with their aunt and uncle, who desired to adopt the two girls. The trial court did not err by finding that the mother had abandoned her children and by terminating the mother's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dyer v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2001-01446-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 635


February 22, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
September 5, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 01-885-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Aaffirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a judgment of the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), dismissing his petition for judicial review of an extension, after his release eligibility date was extended by 30 percent after he assaulted a correctional employee of appellee Tennessee Department of Correction.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of burglary and grand larceny in 1985, smuggling of contraband in 1986, and felony escape in 1990. He received separate sentences of imprisonment for each offense. He came before the prison disciplinary board for assault on a staff member, and was convicted of the violation. As a consequence, the release eligibility date on all his offenses was extended 30 percent. On appeal, the prisoner argued that the extension amounted to an unconstitutional violation of the ex post facto prohibition, double jeopardy, and separation of powers. The appellate court initially held that the prisoner was not entitled to relief, because his petition was untimely and there was nothing indicating that the prisoner first petitioned the department for a declaratory judgment. The appellate court addressed the constitutional claims and held that there was no ex post facto violation; there was no jeopardy violation, because the disciplinary proceeding was administrative in nature and did not conflict with criminal court proceedings; and the separation of powers issue was without merit, as the sentence change was within the parameters of statutory law and the executive power.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

State v. Haywood

COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, the city and the State, filed a condemnation petition. Appellant mortgage company (the company) answered. The city and the State moved to strike the answer. The Circuit Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, granted the motion to strike, denied the company's motion for a continuance, granted a writ of possession of the property, and held the company and its attorneys violated Tenn. R. Civ. P. 11.02(2). The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city and the State filed a petition for condemnation, seeking to take, by eminent domain, a portion of a tract of land located on a road. Appellants, the owners, owned the property, but appellant mortgage company (the company) possessed the mortgage on the property. The company appealed. The court of appeals held that: (1) it was error for the trial court to find the company and its attorneys violated the rule and that the attorneys violated the rule by raising certain defenses; (2) it was error for the trial court to hold that the company's objecting to the right to take the property constituted a violation of the rule; (3) it was error for the trial court to find that the company violated the rule by trying the issue of just compensation; (4) it was error for the trial court to find a violation of the rule by sending certain correspondence to the owners; and (5) the company and its attorneys did not engage in any sanctionable conduct under the rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.
