Ponchik v. Paul


No. W2002-00150-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 617



August 22, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County. No. 9367. The Honorable Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, dismissed plaintiff inmate's complaint against defendant private management company and its employees, alleging violations of prisoner's rights under the United States Constitution. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the inmate's complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The appellate court found that the inmate was a prisoner under Tennessee statutes. The inmate failed to allege all the elements of a prima facie claim of retaliation. The inmate failed to detail how his transfer to an Oklahoma prison in any way prevented or discouraged him from exercising his right to petition the court for redress of grievances. As such, the inmate could not show a casual connection between his transfer and his inability to freely access the courts. The inmate also failed to state claim that alleged he was entitled to certain procedural safeguards before the company could transfer him to another prison. The inmate failed to allege any atypical or significant hardship. Transfers to other prisons and administrative segregation did not constitute atypical or significant hardships in and of themselves. The inmate was not prejudiced by the trial court clerk's failure to insure that his response to the motion to dismiss was before the judge as the inmate did not raise the issue at the trial level, and such error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1318 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re D.L.B.


No. W2001-02245-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 575



August 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal granted: In re D.L.B., 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 633 (Tenn. Dec. 16, 2002).
Appeal granted by In re D.L.B., 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 633 (Tenn., Dec. 16, 2002)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re D.L.B., 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 983 (Tenn., Oct. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-01-0200-2; The Honorable Kenny Armstrong, Special Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A department of children's services (DCS) filed a dependency and neglect petition in juvenile court. Appellee foster parents filed a petition in the Chancery Court of Shelby County (Tennessee) to terminate appellant father's parental rights to his child. Following a hearing, the trial court entered an order terminating the father's parental rights on the basis of abandonment under Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(A)(i) (2001). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first issue was whether the trial court erred by terminating the father's parental rights on the basis of willful abandonment under § 36-1-102(1)(A)(i). The chancery court found that the father willfully abandoned his child in that he willfully failed to visit and willfully failed to support her during the four months immediately preceding the filing of the county's petition to terminate parental rights in the juvenile court. The father argued that the chancery court erred by looking to the four months immediately preceding the filing of the petition to terminate parental rights in the juvenile court rather than the four months immediately preceding the filing of the foster parent's petition to terminate parental rights in the chancery court. The appellate court held that the relevant four month period was the four months immediately preceding the filing of the county's petition to terminate parental rights in the juvenile court. The father failed to contact DCS to request visitation until six months following the filing of the county's petition. He never paid support until five months following the filing of that petition. The evidence supported the chancery court's finding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed and the case was remanded. The costs of the appeal were taxed against the father and his surety.

 

1319 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roberts


No. W2001-01702-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


106 S.W.3d 658; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 579



August 6, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Tipton County. No. 5401. Joseph H. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Juvenile Court for Tipton County (Tennessee) found that defendant, a juvenile, was guilty of disorderly conduct as a result of his actions at the school board building and guilty of assault and resisting arrest due to his actions in the juvenile court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his mother went to the school board to discuss school credits. As they were leaving, defendant made statements and gestures to the school supervisor that he considered threatening. The appellate court found that defendant's statements were not mere epithets or insults, but were threatening and made the school supervisor feel apprehensive. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of disorderly conduct pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-305(a)(1) (1997). In the courtroom, the judge ordered defendant to sit on the benches. When defendant refused to comply, the judge ordered an officer to take defendant out of the courtroom and place him into a holding cell. Defendant reacted violently and struck the officer. Eventually, five officers subdued defendant. As a result of defendant's altercation with the five officers, the jury convicted him of assault and resisting arrest. Because the juvenile court had the right to prevent disturbances in the courtroom and it did not act arbitrarily in ordering defendant to sit on the benches, the jury's decision finding defendant guilty of assault and resisting arrest for his altercation with the officers was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the jury's verdict.

 

1320 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Bennett


No. M2001-03152-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 556


June 27, 2002, Assigned on Briefs  
July 30, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 01C-766. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sued defendant state prison employees in the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) for violation of his civil rights pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. His complaint alleged the failure of certain employees to honor his doctor's direction that he was to be housed on a lower floor and assigned to a lower bunk following back surgery. The trial court granted the employees' motion for summary judgment. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner had to show that the prison employees were aware of, but chose to disregard, a substantial risk of serious harm to him. The appellate court found there were simply no facts, or reasonable inferences, suggesting that the conduct of any of the employees was tantamount to an intent to punish. While there was a dispute in the record as to who knew of the prisoner's medical restrictions and when they knew of them, the appellate court agreed with the trial court that the prisoner failed to assert facts that would support his claim for relief. The appellate court also agreed with the trial court that two of the defendants were not charged with any specific acts of misconduct; rather they were sued because of their supervisory responsibilities. The appellate court noted that liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 had to have been based on more than the right to control employees. The prisoner's claim was for negligence or, at most, gross negligence. The appellate court stated this was simply not enough to state a claim for deliberate indifference to serious medical needs to be actionable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hawkins v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2001-00473-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


127 S.W.3d 749; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 536


October 9, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
July 25, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 00C-3267.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an inmate, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition against the respondent, the Tennessee Department of Correction, for improper venue.


OVERVIEW: A state inmate filed the underlying pro se petition for writ of certiorari to challenge the result of a prison disciplinary proceeding against him. The disciplinary actions at issue were imposed after the Disciplinary Board at West Tennessee State Penitentiary in Henning found that the inmate had refused a drug screen. The trial court dismissed the suit sua sponte for improper venue. The appellate court found no error in the trial court's decision. Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-803 localized venue for actions brought by inmates to the county where the prison facility was located. Therefore, venue was proper in the county in which West Tennessee State Penitentiary was located. The appellate court directed transfer of the matter to the appropriate trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed as modified and remanded.

 

1322 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Trew v. Haggard


No. E2001-02183-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 537



July 25, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Roane County. No. 11958. Russell E. Simmons, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff towing business owner sued defendants, a sheriff and his department, for breach of contract and benefits conferred with regard to an oral contract to tow and store vehicles seized by the sheriff's department. The Circuit Court for Roane County, Tennessee, awarded damages based upon a $ 45 per vehicle towing and storage charge for 83 vehicles. The business owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into an oral contract regarding towing and storage services for vehicles seized by the department. The parties disputed many of the terms of the contract, including how much the owner's business was to be paid for towing and storage and when the department was required to hold a sale of the seized vehicles. Over a two-year period, the owner's business towed and stored about 80 vehicles for the sheriff. The department never held a sale of any of the vehicles and did not begin removing the vehicles until after the instant complaint was filed. The appeals court held the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that the parties agreed upon a fee of $ 45-$ 65 per vehicle for towing and storage until the vehicles could be sold. The sheriff's performance of his duty, under the oral contract, to sell the seized vehicles was not due until he determined he had enough vehicles to justify holding a sale. This was the procedure used by state agencies in the sale of seized vehicles. The owner was not entitled to recovery of storage fees under a quantum meruit theory since the parties had an enforceable contract which covered the same subject matter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded.

 

1323 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Redman v. Redman


No. E2001-02730-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 528



July 22, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P.3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hawkins County. No. 9578. Hon. Kindall T. Lawson, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hawkins County (Tennessee) ordered that appellee grandparents be allowed visitation with their granddaughter every two weeks as recommended by a psychologist. Both the child and appellant father had lived with the grandparents the first two year of the child's life and the grandparents had been highly involved in raising the child. The father appealed on statutory grounds and on grounds of the child's best interests.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the father first raised the issue of whether the petition for grandparent visitation should have been dismissed because it was filed under a prior version of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306 (1997) with certain language regarding the "best interest of the child" standard that had been declared unconstitutional. However, the appellate court held the doctrine of elision allowed the trial court to elide the unconstitutional portion of a statute and find the remaining provisions to be constitutional and effective. The father was against grandparent visitation because he alleged they did not support his own relationship with his daughter and because he feared a cousin posed a threat to his daughter. However, the trial court had found that the child had a significant existing relationship with the grandparents for five years, they being pretty much the child's primary parents and that there was a danger of substantial harm to the child if she was not to have visitation with her grandparents. The appellate court concluded the trial court properly evaluated all the evidence in making it's decision and found that the limited visitation ordered was sufficient to avoid substantial harm.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the case was remanded, with the cost assessed one-half to the grandparents and one-half to the father.

Tankesly v. Pugh


No. M2000-01520-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 452


January 9, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
June 27, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-135-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed petitioner inmate's petition for common-law writ of certiorari in which he sought judicial review of prison disciplinary proceedings, in favor of respondents. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the inmate's petition on the bases that it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, and that the disciplinary board chairman and the correctional facility warden were not proper parties. The appellate court found that the warden was a proper party to the suit. One of the inmate's claims was that he appealed the denial of three days credit for pre-hearing segregation to the warden, who denied him relief. The disciplinary board was a proper defendant because it was the proper board or commission whose decision was being challenged. Although the inmate alleged he was coerced into pleading guilty, he did not deny he engaged in a fight with another inmate. He willingly entered the guilty plea to the lesser offense. No particular punishment was part of the inmate's inducement to plead guilty. The inmate did not allege he was treated more harshly than others because he was a member of a suspect class. Exercise of discretion in punishment in relation to the seriousness of the offense was reasonably related to penological interests. The inmate failed to state a claim for denial of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gunter v. U.C.H.R.A.


No. M1999-01591-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 454



June 27, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Fentress County. No. 7681. Conrad A. Troutman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Fentress County (Tennessee), dismissing his claim for personal injury and property damages against appellees, a local government entity and its employee, based on the statute of limitations, after he filed his claim in general sessions court and that court transferred the cause to the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The individual was involved in an automobile accident when his car was struck by the employee, acting in the course and scope of her employment. The entity moved to dismiss the claim in the general sessions court, citing the Tennessee Governmental Tort Liability Act (GTLA). On appeal, the individual argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-1-116 should be applied to allow the transfer to circuit court, thereby saving his lawsuit from the statute of limitations; and that the Tennessee Constitution prevented dismissal of his complaint. The appellate court initially noted that the filing of the complaint in general sessions court did not toll the statute of limitations, and the "removal" was unauthorized. Additionally, the appellate court held that § 16-1-116 could not be applied retroactively, because it would impair the entity's vested right in its statute of limitations defense; the constitutional provision allowing citizens of the most populous county or counties to bring qualifying GTLA actions in general sessions courts had a rational basis; and the case was distinguished from the Flowers case, which tolled the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court dismissing the complaint, and remanded the case for any further proceedings that could become necessary.

Brown v. Tom Taylor Chevrolet-Pontiac Oldsmobile GMC Truck, Inc.


No. W2000-02890-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 427



June 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court is Affirmed. An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Obion County. No. 20,202. W. Michael Maloan, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile purchasers sued defendant automobile dealers and alleged that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-112 was unconstitutional as it allowed the dealers to pass along a business tax onto the purchasers. The Chancery Court for Obion County (Tennessee) granted the dealers' summary judgment motion. The purchasers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two separate purchasers bought cars from two separate dealers. For each sale, a business tax was imposed on the dealers under the Business Tax Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-701 et seq. The business tax expense was then passed on to the purchasers in an invoice itemizing the tax as an element of the automobile sales price. The trial court below found that the practice of permitting the dealer to pass on the business tax to its customers was neither arbitrary, capricious, nor wholly unreasonable. Accordingly, the trial court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-1-112 was constitutional. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's finding that § 67-1-112 was constitutional. It held that while the business taxes at issue were the obligation of the dealers, not the purchasers, the dealers were not prohibited from recouping that amount by charging the purchaser an increased sales price. The appellate court determined that the state's practice of allowing the dealers to pass on the tax to the purchasers was not arbitrary, capricious, nor wholly unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father requested custody of his minor child. The Juvenile Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied the father's petition for custody and awarded custody to the aunt and uncle. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: An investigator for the Tennessee Department of Children's Services (DCS) responded to a report that an older child had a bruise on the side of his face. On appeal, the father maintained that there was failure to show sufficient proof establishing willful and deliberate abandonment of his minor child. The appellate court concluded the totality of the circumstances supported the determination the father abandoned the child by clear and convincing evidence. Moreover, the facts were sufficient to support a finding that the placement of the child with the father posed a risk of substantial harm to the child. The termination of the father's parental rights was in the best interests of the child.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A disciplinary board found petitioner inmate guilty of conspiracy to violate state law. The inmate filed a petition for writ of certiorari, seeking judicial review. The Chancery Court for Lauderdale County, Tennessee, granted respondent commissioner's, respondent warden's, and respondent correctional officer's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that senior correctional officers took him into custody and placed him in segregation as the result of an altercation that occurred between two prisoners. The inmate was served with a disciplinary report in which he was charged with conspiracy to violate state law. The report alleged that the inmate had hired one of the prisoners to assault the other prisoner. On appeal, the inmate alleged that his placement in administrative segregation for an undetermined period of time constituted an atypical and significant hardship and, therefore, implicated a liberty interest which required the protections of due process. The inmate explained that, while he was being held in administrative segregation, he was classified a maximum custody inmate. The appellate court did not agree that this inability to obtain certification for a parole hearing constitutes a liberty interest which requires due process protections. Since Tennessee recognized no constitutional right to early release, the inmate could not show that he suffered a deprivation of a liberty interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order of the trial court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee children's services agency (agency) filed a petition to terminate the appellant mother's rights of her child. The Juvenile Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) granted the petition. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: In August 1999, the mother left her child with an acquaintance before she was jailed. The acquaintance did not believe the mother wanted the child back, so the child was placed in foster care. The agency moved to terminate the mother's rights in November 2000. The appellate court held that clear and convincing evidence existed to show that the mother failed to substantially comply with the responsibilities set forth in a plan of care. There was no proof that the mother had located any appropriate and responsible providers to care for the child when she was away, and by her own testimony, she paid no monetary support during the entire time her child was in the agency's custody even though she was employed for a majority of that time. The mother's argument that she did not pay support as she was not under an order to do so did not benefit her claim.

In re Estate of Jenkins


No. M2001-01969-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


97 S.W.3d 126; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 338



May 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Jenkins v. Jenkins (In re Estate of Jenkins), 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 800 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Probate Court Reversed In Part, Affirmed in Part. A Direct Appeal from the Probate Court for Sumner County. No. 93P-30. The Honorable Tom E. Gray, Judge.
Estate of Jenkins, 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 606 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 27, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Probate Court Reversed In Part, Affirmed in Part; remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee heirs petitioned the trial court to make a determination regarding the appellant surviving spouse's elective share of the decedent's estate. On remand, the Probate Court for Sumner County (Tennessee) determined that the changing fraction method to calculate the surviving spouse's elective share of the estate did not apply. The surviving spouse appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died in June 1993. The surviving spouse filed a petition for an elective share of the decedent's estate in December 1993. A dispute subsequently arose among the parties regarding the proper calculation for the surviving spouse's elective share. The appellate court determined that the "fixed fraction" method was the proper method of calculation of the surviving spouse's elective share. After the court made that decision, the legislature amended the Uniform Principal and Income Act. In response to that amendment, the executors moved the court to determine whether the fixed fraction method or the changing fraction method should be used. The appellate court held that the plain language of the amendment indicated that it was to apply to any existing estate or trust as of July 1, 2000. As the court noted, it was not reasonable to assume that the legislature intended that the amendment operate retroactively to necessitate the recalculation of prior years distributions of income. Thus, the fixed fraction method applied to income received prior to July 1, 2000, and the changing fraction applied to income after July 1, 2000.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the application of the fixed fraction method to income received before July 1, 2000, and reversed it to income received after July 1, 2000.

C.D.C. v. C.E.D.


No. E2001-02086-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 334



May 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied September 16, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamblen County. No. 99-46. Thomas R. Frierson II, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and step-father, sought to terminate the parental rights of appellee father. The Chancery Court for Hamblen County (Tennessee) refused to terminate the father's parental rights. The mother and step-father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother and the father were divorced in 1996. The mother was granted sole custody of their two children, and the father was granted supervised visitation. The issue of child support was reserved for the future, as the father was not working at the time of the divorce. The mother married the step-father in 1997. The mother and step-father sought to terminate the father's parental rights so the step-father could adopt the children. The mother and step-father claimed the father abandoned the children by willfully failing to pay child support and by willfully failing to visit the children. The appellate court affirmed the lower court's ruling that the father had not abandoned his children. The court held that, while the father's visits were irregular, the mother did little to accommodate the father's efforts to establish visitation. The court also found that, while the father could be criticized for failing to provide support, there was no order for him to do so, and the mother clearly indicated to the father that she did not want to receive support. The mother and step-father failed to provide clear and convincing evidence that the father abandoned the children.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed.

 

1334 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Baxter v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2000-02447-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 279



April 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 417.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3, Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-1729-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was found guilty of an infraction, interfering with an officer's duties, by the prison disciplinary board. After his appeal to the prison warden was denied, the inmate filed a petition for a writ of certiorari against respondent Tennessee Department of Correction (TDOC) in the Chancery Court for Davidson County alleging numerous violations of his due process rights. The trial court dismissed the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that he was not allowed to be present for the hearing or present witnesses and other evidence in his behalf; therefore, the hearing was conducted in violation of both his due process rights as well as rights secured him under TDOC's Uniform Disciplinary Procedures. The inmate further argued that a commissioner's designee did not observe his disciplinary hearing so TDOC violated the Private Prison Contracting Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-24-101 et seq. (1997), which prohibited delegating inmate disciplinary responsibilities to a prison contractor. The appellate court found his petition failed to allege that any punitive sanctions were taken against him let alone the type of atypical and significant hardship that would have triggered due process protections. The appellate court held that the deficiencies in the disciplinary hearing alleged by the inmate were not unconstitutional or illegal. The inmate did not allege that TDOC did not approve the recommendation of the disciplinary board. The appellate court concluded that the fact that the commissioner's designee was not present at the hearing was insufficient to support the issuance of a writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1335 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Lattimer v. Tenn. Dep't of Corr.


No. M2000-03126-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 262


December 11, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
April 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 98-489-II. Carol McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sued appellees, Tennessee Department of Correction (TDOC), its commissioner, the prison warden and employees for the destruction of his photos, claiming their actions amounted to an unconstitutional deprivation of his rights. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed the suit, ruling it was a negligence claim and that the only forum available was the Tennessee Claims Commission. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commission furnished a remedy for injuries caused by the negligence of state employees who were acting in their official capacities. The only proper defendant in such an action was the State. 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 furnished a remedy for malicious or intentional actions by State employees acting under color of law, which resulted in a deprivation of constitutional rights. The only proper defendants in this type of action were the individuals. The appropriate procedure was to hold the court proceedings in abeyance until the commission could determine whether the prisoner's claim fell within its charter. If the commission determined that the destruction of the prisoner's albums was a negligent act, arising from the scope of employment of the named individuals, then the waiver provision of Tenn. Code. Ann. § 9-8-307(b) came into play, and the civil rights claim could be dismissed. Finally, the TDOC was not a "person" within the meaning of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the prisoner was not challenging the TDOC Commissioner's policy, but rather the misuse of the policy by others. Accordingly, the trial court properly dismissed the claims against those two parties.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the prisoners claims against the department and the commissioner was affirmed. The dismissal of the prisoner's claims against the prison warden, the assistant commissioner as well as two prison officials who destroyed the photos was reversed. The order dismissing the civil rights claims against the latter two prison officials, the assistant warden and assistant commissioner was reversed. The case was remanded.

 

1336 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Polk County v. Rogers


No. E2001-00004-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


85 S.W.3d 781; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 200


October 16, 2001, Session  
March 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 27, 2002.  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 16, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Polk County No. 6431 Jeri S. Bryant, Chancellor. Tenn.R.App.P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Cause Remanded.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an operator of a whitewater rafting business, contended evidence presented at trial in the Chancery Court for Polk County (Tennessee) showed that classification of whitewater rafting businesses and their customers under a private act applicable to appellee county was without reasonable basis, and that the trial court's finding to the contrary was in error.


OVERVIEW: The county classified whitewater rafting businesses and their customers under a private act (the Act), assessing a privilege tax on the business. The appellate court reversed the taxes, but remanded for the trial court's determination as to whether a reasonable basis existed for the classification of the business under the Act. On remand, the trial court found a reasonable basis existed and reinstated the tax. On appeal, the rafting company argued the Act violated the Tennessee Constitution, as it was contrary to the general law of Tennessee, without a reasonable basis. The appellate court noted that the county's resources supported a population of less than 15,000; but for 116 days each year, these resources had to be used, in cooperation with state and federal services, to oversee and control an estimated one million tourists. The tax was equally applicable to all within the class, county commercial rafting companies and their customers engaging in the sale or purchase of rafting tickets. The appellate court found the classification under the Act was rational, not arbitrary, and found a direct, natural, and acceptable relation between the classification and the Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Anderson v. Jarrett


No. W2001-00484-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 187



March 13, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Reversed in part; Affirmed in part; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Haywood County. No. 6406 & 6638 J. Roland Reid, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On review of an administrative child support decision of the Tennessee Department of Human Services, the Juvenile Court, Haywood County (Tennessee), transferred the case, but also decided it on the merits, ruling appellee state's action contravened Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-905 regarding seizure of appellant obligor's assets, and the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state petitioned to establish paternity of two children. Paternity was established. Hearings were held to determine the father's child support obligations. A retroactive child support obligation was ordered, to begin in seven days. The state sought to collect it, starting the day the judgment issued, by issuing the father's employer an administrative order for the seizure of assets, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-905. Two days later, the state notified him his pension was to be seized to satisfy the retroactive support. He appealed to the juvenile court, which ruled the seizure impermissible but disavowed jurisdiction, having erroneously concluded a conflict existed between Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-322 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-1003. The state conceded it failed to comply with the statutory guidelines in seizing the father's assets before any payment was due. The instant court concluded that, pursuant to § 36-5-1003, these administrative appeals related to child support orders issued by the department of human services and were properly before the juvenile court pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-1001.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals reversed the decision of the juvenile court regarding its lack of jurisdiction to review the department human services' administrative ruling, as well as its decision to transfer the matter to chancery court. Further, it reversed the ruling on the constitutionality of the statute. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

1338 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re K.A.Y.


No. E2001-00398-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


80 S.W.3d 19; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 163



February 28, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 145426-3. Sharon Bell, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: The judgment was affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee foster parents petitioned the Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee) to adopt two children concerning whom a petition for custody filed by appellant former foster parents was pending in the juvenile court. The chancery court allowed the former foster parents to intervene and granted the foster parents' summary judgment motion. The former foster parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subject children were placed in the home of the former foster parents, who had adopted their half-siblings. The children were then removed from the former foster parents' home and placed with the foster parents. The appellate court held that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-1-117(a)(1) and (d) listed the necessary parties to an adoption proceeding and those entitled to notice, and former foster parents were not included. Therefore, the former foster parents were not entitled to notice of the foster parents' adoption petition. When the foster parents filed their adoption petition, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-116(f)(2) suspended the former foster parents' pending custody matter, and the chancery court had exclusive jurisdiction of all matters pertaining to the children under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-116(f)(1). As a result, the chancery court was not required to decide the custody petition before it ruled on the foster parents' summary judgment motion filed in the adoption case. It was unnecessary to decide the former foster parents' challenge to the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-115(g)(1), giving the foster parents a preference to adopt the children.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1339 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Comm'rs of Roane County v. Parker


No. E2001-00146-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


88 S.W.3d 916; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 122



February 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 16, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Roane County. Nos. 13,252 & 13,223. Frank V. Williams, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Chancery Court for Roane County (Tennessee) judgment upheld defendant county board of commissioners' refusal to rezone plaintiff landowners' property from A-1 General Agricultural to a newly created A-2 zoning district intended for application in rural areas for the keeping of Class I exotic animals and enjoined the landowners from using their rural property to house exotic animals except for their pet tiger. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The principal dispositive issue decided by the appeals court was whether the county's refusal to rezone the landowners' property from A-1 to A-2 was arbitrary, capricious, and discriminatory. Soon after acquiring the property, the landowners informed the county that they intended to house a tiger thereon, a non-conforming use permitted in the A-1 zone pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-208. The county responded by adopting a resolution amending the regional zoning ordinance to create the A-2 zone. The county then rezoned another person's property, originally approved for exotic animals, from A-1 to A-2. The landowners' A-1 property was more qualified than the other person's property for A-2 designation. The amendment could not abrogate permitted A-1 uses and limit uses to a different class of animals such as dogs and cats. There was no reasonable basis for the obvious discriminatory action of the county in rezoning the likely unqualified other property, while refusing to rezone the landowners' clearly qualified property. The appeals court upheld the zoning amendment as not vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the judgment, in part, to dissolve the injunction against the landowners.

 

1340 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. Bennett


No. M2000-02448-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 83



February 1, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Franklin County. No. 8939. J. Curtis Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Franklin County (Tennessee) denied appellant father's motion to modify custody, raised his child support obligation, found him in contempt, and refused to find appellee mother in contempt. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reserved the mother's contempt for a later hearing, at which it initially refused to hear evidence on that subject. The appellate court held this error was made harmless when the trial court amended its decision and allowed such proof. If the trial court's refusal to allow the father to fire his attorney and proceed pro se was error, it was harmless because it did not affect the judgment or prejudice the judicial process. The evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that the father did not show a material change in the child's circumstances to support his motion to modify custody. The father's status as joint legal custodian had no bearing on his child support obligation, as he did not have primary physical custody, so his child support obligation was correctly raised, based on increased income. The trial court's order finding the father's failure to pay child support was willful implied that it found the father was able to pay the support ordered when due, and sufficiently supported its finding that the father was in contempt. The trial court's credibility determination that the mother was not in contempt was not disturbed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Lockheed Martin Energy Sys. v. Johnson


No. E2001-00160-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


78 S.W.3d 918; 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 81



January 31, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 7, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Anderson County. No. 99CH7799. William E. Lantrip, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer filed a complaint challenging appellant State's assessment of use tax, and seeking the amount it alleged was wrongfully assessed against it with respect to computer software. The parties filed cross motions for summary judgment. The Chancery Court for Anderson County (Tennessee) granted summary judgment to the taxpayer, holding that the subject software fell within an exemption. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer had a contract with the United States Department of Energy and carried out the fabrication of nuclear weapons components. The trial court found that the subject software fell within the ambit of the exemption of Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6-102(25)(B) (1998), which provided that the fabrication of software by a person for such person's own use or consumption was not considered a taxable "use." The facts of the case implicated several provisions of the Retailers' Sales Tax Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6-101 et seq. The question before the appellate court was whether the general assembly intended to exempt computer software made by the user, but continue taxation of its sale or use otherwise, and whether the software was fabricated for the taxpayer's own use or consumption so as to be exempt from the use tax. The appellate court held the taxpayer was both the fabricator and the user of the subject software. It did not fabricate the software for sale to another, nor did it fabricate it for the use of another, either of which events would have rendered the exemption inapplicable. Therefore, the exemption under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-6-102(25)(B) (1998) applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, the case was remanded for such further proceedings as might be required, and costs on appeal were taxed to the State.

Gallaher v. Elam


No. E2000-02719-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 94



January 29, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Gallaher v. Elam, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 337 (Tenn., May 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. No. B-3443. Carey Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Knox County, Tennessee, awarded child support in favor of appellant mother in the amount of $ 1,600, plus an additional $ 200 because appellee father did not exercise his visitation rights. The mother and State of Tennessee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1240-2-4-.03(4) violated the Equal Protection Clause contained in U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The juvenile judge found that the provision of Tennessee's child support guidelines, Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1240-2-4-.02(2)(b), violated the Equal Protection Clause, as well as the Due Process Clause and the separation of powers provision of the Tennessee Constitution. The appellate court found that there was no legitimate state purposes in requiring a parent to allocate his or her income more to one child than another. The State's attempt to do so was unconstitutional. The appellate court found it was appropriate to remand the case to hear additional proof as to the father's net income, as the figures for the father's income showed that he had considerably more income in the two preceding years. The appropriate method to determine the child's award would be to determine the appropriate amount under the guidelines for three children, deduct that amount from the father's net monthly income, and make an award to the child applying the guideline percent for one child.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the constitutionality of the child support guidelines and affirmed as to other issues.

Shaffer v. Shelby County


No. W2000-02215-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 25



January 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied July 8, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. 86335-9 T.D.; The Honorable Robert L. Childers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, decedent's survivors, sued appellee county in the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) for wrongful death and personal injuries. The jury found in favor of the survivors and awarded damages. The county then filed a motion to set liability limits in accordance with the Tennessee Governmental Tort Liability Act (GTLA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-20-101 et seq. The trial court granted the motion. The survivors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was jogging in the street by a park pushing her son in a stroller in front of her when she was hit and killed by an automobile. The amounts of the awards for both the wrongful death action and the son's personal injury action were capped by the trial court pursuant to the GTLA. On appeal, the instant court found that (1) it lacked authority to abolish the doctrine of sovereign immunity; (2) the GTLA's cap on damages did not violate the Tennessee Constitution; (3) the trial court did not err in subjecting the loss of consortium claim to the GTLA's statutory limits; (4) the trial court did not err in refusing to grant summary judgment to the county based on discretionary function immunity; (5) the evidence was sufficient to sustain the survivor son's claim for negligent infliction of emotional distress; (6) the trial court did not err by refusing to grant the county's directed verdict motion with respect to the wrongful death claim; (7) the verdicts were not excessive; (8) the trial court did not abuse its discretion concerning counsel's arguments; and (8) discretionary costs were not awardable above the statutory cap.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part as to the capping of the awards. The judgment was reversed in part as to the award of discretionary costs, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Bowman v. City of Elizabethton


No. E2001-00597-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 931



December 28, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Carter County. No. 23450. G. Richard Johnson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By means of a quo warranto proceedings pursuant, plaintiff realtors contested the right of defendant city to annex their property. The Chancery Court for Carter County, Tennessee, dismissed the original complaint, finding the realtors had no standing to contest the annexation and denied a motion brought by other individuals to intervene. The realtors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three ordinances were adopted by the city annexing property in three separate locations. Each of the realtors owned property in one of the areas annexed, and they filed suit contending the annexation of the areas violated state law. Three years after the three original ordinances were adopted by the city, and after the suit was filed, the city amended the ordinances to exclude the properties owned by the realtors from the area annexed. In response to the city's amendments, three additional landowners, whose property was within the original annexation ordinance, moved to be permitted to intervene. The realtors appealed the dismissal of their suit, insisting their right to contest the annexation was not precluded by excluding their property from the ordinances repealing the earlier ones. The appeals court disagreed, finding counsel for the realtors conceded in oral argument that had the initial ordinances not included their property they would have had no standing to contest. As to the parties seeking to intervene, they failed to perfect an appeal by not filing a notice of appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause.

Dep't of Children's Servs. v. D.G.S.L.


No. E2001-00742-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 941


November 16, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
December 28, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. No. L-3955. Carey E. Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Department of Children's Services (DCS), filed a petition to terminate appellant mother's parental rights to her two sons. The Juvenile Court for Knox County, Tennessee, granted the petition from which the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The children were removed due the mother's drug addition and a lack of suitable housing. The mother also failed to complete the terms of a plan which was developed to help her to properly care for her children. The mother argued, inter alia, that (1) the DCS did not meet its burden of proof; (2) the termination of her parental rights was not in the best interests of the children; and (3) the DCS did not provide her with the resources in order to meet the goals of the plan. The appellate court held that (1) the mother's last minute efforts to attempt to comply with the plan's requirements and remain drug free did not form the basis for a conclusion that the DCS did not meet its burden of proof; (2) the mother's willful abandonment of the children by not paying child support, and her failure to maintain regular visitation with them, established that it was in the best interest of the children to terminate the mother's parental rights; and (3) because the evidence was clear that the DCS made reasonable efforts to assist the mother in establishing a suitable home for the children, a re-evaluation of the trial court's assessment of the DCS witness was not required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Spencer v. Aydlotte


No. W2001-00995-COA-R3-CV-


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 957



December 28, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Gibson County. No. 14944. The Honorable George R. Ellis, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The natural parents of the minor child were never married, although the child was legitimated by action of a juvenile court. The mother subsequently married the appellant. They petitioned to terminate the father's parental rights. The trial court denied their petition and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court stated that while the natural father had not pursued his parental rights as aggressively as he should have, the mother and her husband had failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that the natural father had engaged in conduct that evinced a settled purpose to forego all parental duties and relinquish all parental claims to the child. Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g) provided that a termination of parental rights could be based upon the ground of abandonment pursuant to § 36-1-113(g)(1). The maternal grandmother testified that the child's mother refused the father's requests to take the child to his home for visitation. She testified that the mother eventually refused to allow the father to visit with the child and that the mother conditioned the father's visitation on the father's payment of child support.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1347 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hawks v. Greene


No. M1999-02785-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 917



December 18, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 98-1320-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-50-504(h)(1), appellant Tennessee Department of Safety ordered the forfeiture of appellee driver's van that she drove while her license was revoked. The driver sought review, and the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, reversed. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver had her license revoked for one year for driving while intoxicated (DUI). She was eligible to have her license reinstated, but had failed to do so, when she was stopped for a traffic violation. The trial court held that forfeiture of her van under § 55-50-504(h) violated the Excessive Fines Clauses of the United States and Tennessee Constitutions. The appellate court agreed. It ruled that the driver's van was subject to forfeiture under § 55-50-504(h), even though she had been eligible for reinstatement. It then conducted an "excessive fines" proportionality analysis in which it considered both the gravity of the offense and the culpability of the driver's conduct. The maximum punishment for driving when one's license had been revoked for a DUI offense was six months in jail, and a $ 1,000 fine, indicating a minimal level of culpability for this offense. The driver was neither violent nor dangerous to the public. Her failure to take the steps necessary to have her license reissued was not especially reprehensible and caused minimal harm to the department. The forfeiture was held to be an unconstitutionally excessive fine on the facts of the instant case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Coats v. Smyrna/Rutherford County Airport Auth.


No. M2000-00234-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 911



December 13, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Rutherford County. No. 99MI-1476. Robert E. Corlew, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee citizen filed an action in the Chancery Court for Rutherford County, Tennessee, to compel appellant county airport authority to disclose documents pursuant to the Tennessee Public Records Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 10-7-101 et seq. The trial court ordered disclosure. The authority appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen sought documents relating to lease negotiations between the authority and a third party and correspondence to and from the authority's privately retained attorney relating to the project. The trial court ordered disclosure of most of the documents but reserved ruling on the correspondence until a later date. The court refused to stay its order and the authority released the documents, including proposed leases. The trial court then issued a separate order directing disclosure of the correspondence. That order was stayed pending appeal. The authority argued that the leases and correspondence were exempt from disclosure. The appellate court held that the case was moot as to the leases as they had been released. As to the correspondence, while an attorney had the ethical duty to maintain the confidences and secrets of a client, the mere fact that a public record had been signed or was being held by an attorney did not necessarily exempt the record from disclosure. Disclosure would be prohibited only if the records contained something of a confidential or secret nature. The subject correspondence contained no such information and was therefore subject to disclosure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
