Johnson v. Corr. Corp. of Am.


No. W2001-00763-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 952


September 12, 2001, On-briefs  
December 11, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County. No. 9308. The Honorable Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a prisoner, sued a private prison to recover for personal injuries sustained when he was attacked by another prisoner. The Circuit Court for Hardeman County (Tennessee) granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was attacked by another prisoner, who threw boiling water in his face and struck him on the head with an electric coffee pot, causing severe personal injuries. With a date discrepancy in the record, along with the prisoner's assertion and the evidence filed therewith concerning the correct filing date, the case dismissal by virtue of the statute of limitations without an evidentiary hearing was inappropriate; a factual dispute was involved concerning the true date of the filing of the complaint. Construed in the light most favorable to the prisoner, the appellate court believed he clearly stated a claim for retaliation, both under the United States and Tennessee Constitutions. He alleged that, before he was placed in punitive segregation, prison policy provided him with certain disciplinary procedures, including issuance of a disciplinary report, and the prison failed to follow these procedures in transferring him from protective to punitive segregation.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order dismissing the prisoner's complaint was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on the issue of statute of limitations and for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

1350 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Varner v. City of Knoxville


No. E2001-00329-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 963



November 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Varner v. City of Knoxville, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 669 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 147835-3. Sharon Bell, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City of Knoxville affirmed the Knoxville-Knox County Metropolitan Planning Commission's (MPC) denial of appellant property owner's rezoning application. The Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, found no error in the city's action and dismissed the complaint. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed the application seeking to change the zoning of his vacant lot so he could expand his adjacent used car business onto that lot. He requested that the subject property's zone be changed from single family residential to highway and arterial commercial. The city denied the request on the ground that the zoning change posed a significant traffic hazard and that such a change was inconsistent with the sector plan for the property. The property owner contended that the city's decision to deny his rezoning application lacked a rational basis; that it was arbitrary, capricious, and unlawful. The appellate court found no abuse of discretion in the city's decision to deny the property owner's rezoning application. The MPC staff advanced cogent reasons for maintaining the residential zone. The MPC and the city council essentially adopted the staff's reasoning. The city's decision upheld the sector plan and its rationale in denying this rezoning request was "fairly debatable," as it was based upon rational underpinnings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1351 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Sadler v. Tenn. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


No. M2001-02341-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 831


August 2, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
November 8, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-457-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a pro se petition for writ of certiorari against defendant Board of Probation and Parole. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) granted the board's motion to dismiss. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued, inter alia, that Tenn. Code. Ann. § 40-28-115(c) was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers mandated by the United States and Tennessee constitutions. The court of appeals disagreed because the exercise of a judicial function was not the same as being the recipient of a delegated power that properly belonged to the judicial branch. The inmate argued that his parole eligibility date should not have been governed by Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-501, because that statute was enacted after his conviction and sentencing. Instead, he claimed he was entitled to have his parole eligibility date calculated in accordance with the law in effect at the time he was sentenced. The court of appeals found that that the inmate might have been correct, but there was nothing in the record to indicate how his release eligibility date was calculated, including what statute it was based upon, or what the correct date would have been if the calculations had been based upon the earlier law.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1352 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


McClain v. City of Millington


No. W2000-02254-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 801



October 23, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-00-0135-2. The Honorable Floyd Peete, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Temporary injunction was vacated and case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee tavern sought a temporary injunction against appellant city in the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) prohibiting the enforcement of the hours the tavern could sell beer on Sunday. The trial court granted the tavern relief. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: In its request of a temporary injunction, the tavern had argued the city's beer ordinance was unconstitutional and invalid because it was more restrictive in terms of hours of sale than that permitted by the state law for liquor-by-the-drink establishments. The city appealed the chancery court's grant of injunctive relief, arguing the chancery court did not have jurisdiction to enjoin pending or threatened criminal proceedings, or to enjoin the enforcement the city's ordinances as they related to beer sales. The appellate court initially noted a license to sell alcoholic beverages did not confer a property right on the licensee. The appellate court held beer ordinances were expressly prohibitory and penal in nature. The appellate court further held the chancery court lacked jurisdiction to enjoin criminal prosecutions under statute or ordinances, except where property rights were affected. The appellate court concluded the chancery court erred by imposing the injunction prohibiting enforcement of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The order of the chancery court granting the tavern's temporary injunction was vacated and the injunction against the city was dissolved.

 

1353 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


City of Labanon v. Harris


No. M1999-01025-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 758



October 10, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wilson County. No. 10543. Clara Byrd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a seller of outdoor storage facilities, was cited for violating a principal building zoning ordinance and a sign ordinance. He appealed the citations to the Circuit Court for Wilson County, Tennessee, which found that the storage buildings did not violate the principal building zoning provision, and that the seller had not violated the sign ordinance. Appellant city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The seller was fined for the violation of an ordinance which prohibited certain buildings from being placed on a lot and was also fined for the violation of an ordinance which prohibited signs of certain types in certain areas. He had placed empty storage building with advertisements on the lots. The city maintained that the placement of the storage buildings violated the first ordinance because they were neither the one primary building allowed nor a customary accessory building. Because the storage buildings were not used for storage or for any purpose by the owners of the lots or the businesses on the lots, they were not incidental to the principal uses on the lots and were, therefore, not accessory buildings. The court held that the empty storage buildings which were used for advertising fell within the definition of those buildings which were prohibited by the ordinance. The trial court did not err in concluding that the storage buildings were not portable within the meaning of the sign ordinance. Because the buildings were not accessory buildings and were not easily moveable, they were prohibited by the sign ordinance.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the citation and fine for violation of the sign ordinance was affirmed, and its holding that the principal building ordinance had not been violated was reversed.

 

1354 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


K.S.O.H. v. J.W.B. (In re T.J.B.)


No. E2001-00055-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 740


August 2, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
October 4, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County. No. K-2692. Carey E. Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the mother and stepfather, petitioned to terminate the parental rights of appellee, the biological father of the minor child, so they could adopt the child, in the Juvenile Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which dismissed their petition. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the parents never married, after the child's birth, and while they were still dating, the father frequently visited the child and provided some financial support. No court order regarding his visitation schedule and child support obligation existed before the mother's petition to terminate was filed. The mother and stepfather were married when the child was two and they had one child from their marriage. The appellate court agreed with the juvenile court's holding that they failed to establish by clear and convincing evidence that the father had abandoned the child. They failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that his failure to visit and support the child was intentional. They had the burden to prove by clear and convincing evidence that he willfully failed to support or make reasonable payments toward such child's support for four consecutive months prior to the filing of the petition to terminate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the juvenile court was affirmed and the cause was remanded to the juvenile court for such further proceedings as required.

 

1355 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Meadows v. Tennessee Bd. of Emergency Med. Servs.


No. M2001-00478-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 732



October 2, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-83-I. Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After her theft conviction on a plea of nolo contendere for passing an altered bill, the respondent Tennessee Board of Emergency Medical Services (Board) revoked the petitioner medical technician's Emergency Medical Technician (EMT) license. The medical technician sought review in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee). The trial court reversed the Board's decision. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two issues were argued: (1) whether theft was a crime of moral turpitude; and (2) the effect, if any, of the medical technician's plea of nolo contendere. The court of appeals held that there was substantial and material evidence in the record to support both the conviction of the medical technician for theft of less than five hundred dollars value and that the acts forming the basis for the conviction were acts of moral turpitude sufficient to warrant the revocation of her EMT license. The court of appeals also held that wherever there was presented material evidence of the misconduct charged and the mere knowledge alone of the additional fact that the medical technician had entered a nolo contendere plea in the criminal courts could not be used as a shield against appropriate action by administrative agencies.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

1356 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Tulis v. Greene


No. M2000-02844-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 731



October 2, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 00-792-I. The Honorable Irvin H. Kilcrease, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver objected to being required to give his social security number to renew his driver's license. The Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) affirmed appellee commissioner's decision denying the driver's application for renewal, and the driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver objected that the requirement to provide his social security number, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-50-321(c)(1) (Supp. 2000), was a violation of his free exercise of religion. The statute was a neutral law of general applicability not aimed at the promotion or restriction of religious convictions. If the "strict scrutiny" constitutional analysis was the appropriate test, the statute was the least restrictive means of achieving the compelling state interest of being able to quickly identify drivers. It was also required under 42 U.S.C.S. § 666(a)(13)(A) (Supp. 2001) that the driver place his social security number on his application. The driver could have sought an exemption from this requirement under 26 U.S.C.S. § 1402(g) (Supp. 2001), but there was no evidence he had satisfied the requirements for such an exemption. His affidavit of revocation and recission provided to the Secretary of the Department of the Treasury did not accomplish this, nor did it unilaterally revoke any sort of contract with the social security administration.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1357 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. D.R. (In re C.R.R.)


No. E2000-01381-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 726


August 3, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
September 25, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Blount County. No. 7683-31-10. William Terry Denton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Blount County (Tennessee) found that appellants, mother and father, had abandoned their three children, and terminated their parental rights. The mother and father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother's arrest for possession of a firearm and the father's arrest for public intoxication and possession of a scheduled substance caused appellee Department of Children's Services to petition for temporary custody of their children. The parents were briefly incarcerated, then mother absconded with the children but returned them, and the father attempted suicide. The department entered plans of care for the parents to attempt to regain custody. The father was incarcerated again, confessed to an alcohol problem, was suspected of drug use, but had full-time work when not incarcerated. The mother lived with various people, one whose name she could not recall; was unemployed; stopped taking her own medication; was charged with crimes; and was unaware a restraining order against her visitation with her children had been lifted. The parents threatened and harmed one another physically. One child had an untreated cataract. The appellate court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(2) termination grounds were met. At least seven of the nine Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(i) factors showed that termination of the father's parental rights was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1358 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Lecorps


No. M1999-01581-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 715



September 25, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Discretionary appeal allowed: Robinson v. LeCorps, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 50 (Tenn.Feb. 11, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 96C-3528. Mary Ashley Nichols, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient, a state prison inmate, filed a medical malpractice complaint against defendant doctor. The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, ultimately dismissed the complaint after initially granting the doctor's motion in limine to exclude the evidentiary deposition of the patient's only expert witness. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient injured his ankle when it was caught and twisted between two railroad ties. He was first treated in the prison infirmary by a nurse. He was later treated by the doctor, who was under contract with the prison system to provide health care to inmates. The patient's medical malpractice complaint alleged the doctor's treatment of his ankle was negligent. The basis for the trial court's exclusion of the testimony of the patient's sole medical expert was the failure of the expert to demonstrate knowledge of the standard of care in the community where the doctor practiced. On appeal, the patient argued the exclusion of his sole expert led to the dismissal of the complaint, as it meant he could not meet his burden of proof on the elements of medical malpractice. The appeals court found the patient's expert did not adequately testify as to support a finding that he had the requisite knowledge of the standard of care in the doctor's community and, therefore, his testimony was properly excluded. Testimony that the standard in the doctor's community was the same as the national standard of care was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case.

 

1359 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Johnson


No. M2000-00358-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 639



August 28, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County No. II-26076 Russ Heldman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee husband filed a complaint for divorce in the Chancery Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, and he sought custody of the parties' children. Appellant wife filed a counter-complaint for divorce; she also sought custody of the children. Custody was awarded to the husband, and the wife was denied visitation. Contempt petitions were also filed against both the husband and the wife.


OVERVIEW: The husband's sister and brother-in-law lived across the street from the wife. They used a police-type scanner to intercept the telephone conversations between the wife, her alleged lover, and other friends. Tapes of the conversations were admitted into evidence during cross-examination of the wife for purposes of impeachment. The wife argued that the trial court's ruling on custody and visitation was based largely on the evidence presented from the audio tapes. The appellate court disagreed; there was ample evidence in the record, independent of the tapes, to support the action of the trial judge. Even so, any error was harmless. From the testimony at trial, it was clear that it was in the best interest of the children to be in the custody of the husband, but denying the wife visitation was improper. The husband challenged the trial court's findings of criminal contempt on the grounds that the contempt petition did not provide notice. Apparently, the nature of the contempt did not become known to the parties until the trial court entered its opinion. This provided no opportunity for the contemnor to purge himself.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed that part of the trial court's order sentencing the husband to the county workhouse for criminal contempt. The judgment of the trial court awarding custody of the children to husband was affirmed. The judgment of the trial court denying visitation to the mother was reversed. The judgment of the trial court finding the wife guilty of criminal contempt was reversed.

Henderson v. State, Dep't of Children Serv. ( In re T.L.P.)


No. W1999-01940-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 638



August 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County No. C6901; The Honorable Kenneth Turner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) granted a motion to terminate appellant mother's parental rights. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother's children had been placed in foster care while the mother was incarcerated. Appellee Tennessee Department of Children's Services developed a plan of care that required the mother to, among other things, remain clean and sober, complete a parenting program, refrain from breaking the law, visit with the children regularly, and maintain a stable household. After her release from prison she attended parenting classes, but was evicted from her apartment, admitted using drugs, and was again incarcerated on drug charges. The appellate court held that abandonment under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(1) (2000) was not a proper basis for termination of the mother's parental rights; the element of intent was lacking because the mother had been incarcerated during the four months preceding the petition. However, termination under § 36-1-113(g)(2) was proper based on the mother's substantial noncompliance with the plan of care, and termination was also proper under § 36-1-113(g)(3)(A) because the mother failed to remedy the conditions that led to the children's removal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1361 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Caudill v. Foley


No. M2000-01512-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 625



August 21, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 23856. Russ Heldman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part; Reversed in part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, denied appellant mother's motion seeking recusal of the trial judge on the basis that he was biased towards her appellate counsel in a child custody action against appellee father. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the judge committed reversible error in refusing to recuse himself based upon his prior relationship with her counsel, in disqualifying counsel for the mother, and refusing to award attorney's fees for the initial trial and appeal. The judge's refusal to recuse himself was not an abuse of discretion. No objective person could reasonably question the judge's bias towards counsel for actions which took place several years before while both men were serving as opposing counsel. Counsel did not testify as a witness at an earlier hearing. He was acting merely as an advocate for his client and the only questions that he answered were inquiries of the trial court in that capacity. The trial court had no objective basis to disqualify counsel from acting as the mother's attorney. Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-5-103(c) provided the trial court with discretion in awarding attorney's fees. It did not abuse its discretion in failing to award fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the trial judge's refusal to recuse himself and the awarding of attorney's fees. The judgment was reversed as to the disqualification of appellate counsel.

 

1362 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Ragsdale v. City of Memphis


No. W2001-01652-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT MEMPHIS


70 S.W.3d 56; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 612



August 17, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] A Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-01-0780. The Honorable Walter L. Evans, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayers sued appellants city, county, and private company, in the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), seeking a declaratory judgment that acts of the city and county to facilitate the building of a sports arena were unconstitutional. The trial court found the financing arrangement to construct the arena to be unconstitutional, and the appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city and county created a sports authority, in compliance with the Sports Authorities Act of 1993, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 7-67-101 through -122 (1998 and Supp. 2000). It was proposed that the sports authority issue bonds for the construction of a multiuse arena by the private company, in an effort to attract a National Basketball Association franchise. The city and the county agreed to contribute certain revenues on hand to this effort. The taxpayers complained that this activity violated Tenn. Const. art. II, § 29, which greatly limited the ability of a county, city, or town to lend its credit to a private entity. This prohibition did not apply to instrumentalities of the city or county, such as the sports authority. Because the city and county were contributing existing revenue, they were not pledging their credit. The actions of the city and county were permissible under the "public purpose" exception to art. II, § 29, because the sports arena was a public purpose. It was not appropriate for a court to substitute its judgment on this issue for that of a governmental body. The fact that the private company would derive some benefit did not invalidate the public purpose.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that the taxpayers had standing was affirmed. Otherwise, the trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

 

1363 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Univ. of Tennessee of Chattanooga v. Farrow


No. E2000-02386-COA-R9-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 615; 86 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 910



August 16, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. Nos. 146101-3 and 144421-3. Hon. Sharon Bell, Chancellor Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 98-0619. Hon. W. Frank Brown, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Chancery Court of Knox County are reversed, and the Judgment of the Chancery Court of Hamilton County is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In each of three actions under review, the plaintiff female employee alleged discrimination under the Tennessee Human Rights Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-101 et seq., and demanded a jury trial. The Chancery Court for Knox County, Tennessee, struck the demands for a jury. However, the Chancery Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, denied defendant university's motion to strike the jury demand. The employees filed interlocutory appeals.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether the employees were entitled to a trial by jury on employment discrimination claims under the Tennessee Human Rights Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-21-101 et seq. Under the Act, administrative relief was not exclusive. The aggrieved individual, without exhausting administrative remedies, could have filed a direct action in chancery or circuit court. Indeed, the employees all filed their discrimination claims directly in the chancery court. The appeals court held that the employees had a right to a jury trial under the Act, because the Act did not expressly exempt that right when creating a civil cause of action for aggrieved persons. There was no indication in the Act that the legislature intended to exclude the right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment of the Hamilton County trial court, but reversed the judgments of the Knox County trial court.

 

1364 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re C.M. v. Phillips


No. E2001-00211-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 590



August 15, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 86063. Hon. Bill Swann, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Knox County Circuit Court, Tennessee, entered an order of protection for the minor petitioner against defendant. From that order, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged an order of protection filed against him, specifically from abusing, threatening to abuse, or committing acts of violence against the minor. On appeal, he contended that: (1) Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-3-617 was unconstitutional; (2) the circuit court lacked jurisdiction over petitions for orders of protection filed on behalf of minors; (3) the minor was required to participate in the drafting and prosecution of the petition; and, (4) evidence preponderated against the factual determinations made by the trial court. The appeals court disagreed. The statute authorized attorney's fees to be awarded to the petitioner under certain circumstances, included the instant one, and did not infringe upon to powers of the courts. The child fell under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-3-601(1) and there was no conflict with the jurisdiction of the juvenile court. Third, the rules of civil procedure provided a petition could be brought by a next friend of the minor and the parent or guardian was required to sign the same. Finally, the evidence was sufficient, as the minor's statement about the alleged abuse was a reliable excited utterance and provided proof that the same occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

1365 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Coker v. State Dep't of Corr.


No. M1999-02268-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 602


April 28, 2000, Assigned on Briefs  
August 7, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 99-820-II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a declaratory judgment action against appellee corrections department in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), asserting he was entitled to sentence reduction credits which had not been awarded to him and that his early release date had been revoked. The trial court granted the department's summary judgment motion, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, originally sentenced to death, was ineligible to earn sentence reduction credits, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-236. His death sentence was overturned, and he was sentenced to life, and was eligible to earn sentence reduction credits. The vacation of his death sentence did not entitle him to retroactive sentence reduction credits. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-1-501 et seq., early release could be granted when it was certified that a facility reached 95 percent of capacity. The governor could declare certain inmates ineligible for release under the legislation. Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-1-504(b). Once the facility population reached 90 percent or less of its capacity, release eligibility dates of all inmates automatically reverted to those established prior to their reductions due to overcrowding. The inmate had once had a "safety valve" release date under the legislation, but the governor cancelled it. This did not violate the Ex Post Facto clauses of the state or federal constitutions. This program did not grant the inmate an unconditional right to early parole and was only a temporary, conditional opportunity to be considered for early release.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1366 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Stillwell v. Stillwell


No. E2001-00245-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 562



July 30, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bradley County. No. V-99-734. John B. Hagler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part as Modified, and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Bradley County (Tennessee), found there had been no material change in circumstances regarding visitation since plaintiff mother and defendant father's divorce decree incorporating their marriage dissolution agreement had been entered. However, it ordered additional visitation on alternating Wednesdays for four hours to the father and also ordered that father lock up his guns while his son was visiting. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed for divorce, and she and the father entered into a marital dissolution agreement that provided for the care and custody of the parties' minor son. The visitation schedule in the agreement provided that the father would have minimum visitation rights of every other weekend. The trial court entered a final divorce decree and incorporated the agreement. The parties soon started to informally alter the visitation. When the mother tried to limit additional visitation, the father became hostile. She petitioned to modify and also alleged she was fearful because the father was continuously carrying a loaded gun. The appellate court modified the trial court's judgment to include a two-week visitation period included in the original dissolution agreement and affirmed the additional Wednesday visitation. However, it also vacated the firearm restriction as no finding had been made that there existed a risk of substantial harm to the son.


OUTCOME: Judgment was modified to reinstate a two-week visitation period the father was originally provided in the marriage dissolution agreement, and addition of a four-hour Wednesday visitation period not in the agreement was affirmed. That part of the trial court's order restricting father's possession of a firearm in his son's presence was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1367 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Hoover-Crawford


No. M2000-01655-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 554



July 27, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Cannon County. No. 847; The Honorable John B. Melton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Tennessee Department of Children's Services (DCS) filed a petition for termination of appellant mother's parental rights. The Juvenile Court for Cannon County, Tennessee, issued a final decree of guardianship entered nunc pro tunc. The mother challenged the decree.


OVERVIEW: The mother had three minor children. DCS received a referral that the children were being cared for by an 18-year-old half sister. Upon investigation, DCS found the children alone in a filthy house. The family was in the process of being evicted, the water and electricity had been turned off, and there was little means of support. DCS also noted that the mother had a history of drug use and prostitution. The mother received full procedural protection at the termination proceeding. The trial court did err by finding that the mother abandoned the children for failure to visit the children during the four months immediately preceding the filing of the petition to terminate parental rights. The trial court did not err, however, in finding that defendant abandoned the children for failure to pay child support while the children were in state custody. The record clearly demonstrated that the mother failed to substantially comply with a plan of care. Termination of the mother's parental rights was warranted. Furthermore, the trial court did not err by finding that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1368 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Seals v. Bowlen


No. M1999-00997-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 547


August 25, 1999, Assigned on Briefs  
July 26, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 98-3535-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed in Part, Affirmed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner was found guilty of assault by respondent correctional facility disciplinary board; respondent warden rejected the prisoner's appeal. The prisoner filed an application for a writ of certiorari in the Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee. This court granted the motion to dismiss filed by respondent Tennessee Department of Correction (TDOC), and the prisoner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was accused of assaulting his cellmate. At a disciplinary hearing conducted by the board, he was allowed to present only one witness, another inmate who testified that the prisoner was attacked first by his cellmate. The instant court found error in the lower court's dismissal of the board and the warden from the action, since both had decision- making authority regarding disciplinary proceedings, and therefore were proper parties. The prisoner's claim that the board acted arbitrarily and illegally, by depriving him of due process, was cognizable under a writ of certiorari. Depriving the prisoner of good time credits implicated an interest sufficient to invoke due process. Dismissal of the prisoner's petition, however, was proper, since he was requesting the reviewing court to reweigh the evidence presented to the board. The board did not violate the prisoner's due process rights by disallowing testimony from an inmate about the victim's prior assaults; that the prisoner failed to stop hitting the cellmate was "some evidence" sufficient to support the finding that he committed assault. His claim that board members were biased was conclusory and unsupported.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the warden and the board was reversed. The order dismissing the petition was affirmed.

 

1369 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Traughber


No. M2000-01146-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 490


January 9, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
July 13, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 99-1964-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff was convicted in 1992 of sexual battery, aggravated sexual battery and rape. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-105(d)(3) in effect at the time of conviction, he would have been granted parole. He appealed denial of mandamus relief after being denied parole, in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee).


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff was convicted in 1992, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-28-105(d)(3) required only three affirmative votes of the parole board to grant parole. In 1998, the statute was amended to require four affirmative votes for a parole grant for certain crimes, among which were plaintiff's crimes. Plaintiff was denied parole in 1999 by a vote of three affirmative, four negative. His complaint was that the 1998 statute amendment was unconstitutional as applied to him because of ex post facto considerations. As to the merits of the plaintiff's claim that he was entitled to a writ of certiorari because the board reached its decision to deny him parole in an unconstitutional and unlawful manner by violating the ex post facto clause in the Tennessee constitution, the court denied the claim. The amendment did not redefine the offense for parole eligibility nor change the substantive law annexed to the targeted offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1370 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Comm'r of Transp. v. Eagle


No. M1999-00300-COA-R10-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


63 S.W.3d 734; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 485



July 11, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. II-26212. Russ Heldman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State's Transportation Department acquired land to improve a highway and petitioned to terminate the use of the property as a cemetery. The Chancery Court for Williamson County (Tennessee), over the Department's objection, added appellees, State Indian Affairs Commission and several Native Americans, as Tenn. Code Ann. § 46-4-102 "interested persons," and appointed attorney general pro tem, outside counsel, for them. State appealed.


OVERVIEW: An area near a road was known to have Native American artifacts. Before beginning road improvements, the Department began an archeological examination, found two unmarked ancient graves, and notified the State Archeologist. The Department petitioned for the graves' relocation under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 46-4-101 to -104 (2000). The trial court granted the Commission's and Native Americans' request to join the suit, and found that the Attorney General had a conflict of interest representing both the Department and the Commission. The appellate court held that, as a matter of law and fact, the Commission lacked capacity to intervene or otherwise participate. Also the Commission had no standing because, as a statutory creature, it had no rights or interests of its own entitled to constitutional protection, neither had it alleged or demonstrated that any of its proprietary interests as a state agency were being jeopardized by the proceeding. The Native Americans did not have veto power over disinterment, nor were they, without proof of blood relationship to the buried person or interest in the realty, "interested persons." Freedom of religion was not implicated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, the appointments were vacated, and the case was remanded. On remand, the trial court was entitled to exercise its discretion to permit an amicus to appear in the proceedings to assist the court in properly resolving the issues raised by the Department's petition.

Citizens for a Better Johnson City v. City of Johnson City

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant city, the owners of the newly rezoned property in question, and defendant developer, who held an option to purchase the property. The Chancery Court for Washington County, Tennessee, dismissed plaintiffs' complaint and awarded developer discretionary costs. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: City passed an ordinance amending its zoning map so as to rezone a 4.5-acre tract of undeveloped land located at the northwest corner of a busy intersection from medium density residential to planned business. Plaintiffs filed a declaratory judgment action, seeking a declaration that the zoning constituted "spot zoning" and as such was an illegal, arbitrary, and unreasonable exercise of city's zoning authority. The trial court concluded the challenged action was "fairly debatable" and, consequently, dismissed plaintiffs' complaint. The appeals court agreed, finding that the massive commercial developments on both sides of the south side of the subject intersection served as a legitimate reason for the classification. There was a fairly debatable issue.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case.

Lee v. Lee


No. W2000-01918-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


66 S.W.3d 837; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 465



June 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 2001.
Application denied by, Sub nomine at De Los Rios v. Lee, 2003 Tenn. LEXIS 456 (Tenn., May 19, 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Lee v. Lee, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 892 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County No. D27933-3. The Honorable D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, granted the parties a divorce. Appellant husband challenged the trial court's judgment granting appellee wife custody of the parties' child, dividing the marital property, and denying his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-101(a)(1) was facially unconstitutional. Because the harm to a child was implicit in a divorce proceeding, parents involved in such a proceeding automatically submitted the issue of custody of a minor child to the court. Accordingly, the husband's argument that § 36-6-101(a)(1) was facially unconstitutional was without merit, and therefore the appellate court declined to address the issue because it was not raised in the trial court. The appellate court found no abuse of discretion (1) in the trial court's suspension of the consent order regarding visitation, (2) in awarding the wife temporary custody and the authority to procure needed medical treatment for the child, (3) in the trial court's division of the marital property, and (4) in awarding the wife's attorney's fees. However, because the child's school schedule changed, on remand the trial court was required to make a determination about the husband's future visitation rights.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but remanded for it to further proceedings regarding the husband's visitation rights.

State ex rel. Armstrong v. Coleman


No. W2000-01122-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 382



May 24, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Gibson County. Nos. 4786 and 3756. The Honorable Robert W. Newell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Juvenile Court for Gibson County, Tennessee, entered orders setting periodic child support payments and setting child support arrearages against two fathers. Appellant State, acting on behalf of the mothers, appealed. The actions were consolidated for the purpose of appeal.


OVERVIEW: In separate actions, the State, acting on behalf of two mothers, sought to enforce outstanding child support orders against their children's fathers. Each father was also the subject of at least one other outstanding support order entered after the orders in the present cases. The trial court modified the amount of support and set arrearage amounts to be paid by the fathers, but allowed a credit for the amounts being paid under the later orders. When the State moved to alter or amend the judgments, the trial court made findings of fact that, sua sponte, declared provisions of the Tennessee Child Support Guidelines which prevented the consideration of later support orders in setting the amount of support to be paid to be unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in making such a ruling when the issue had not been raised by any of the parties. The guidelines were not obviously unconstitutional and the court did not consider the issue further. The trial court was directed to make new determinations as to support due and explain any deviation from the support guidelines, as required by statute.


OUTCOME: The orders of the trial court were vacated and the cases were remanded for further proceedings.

Franklin County v. Town of Monteagle


No. M2000-02453-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 379



May 23, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected June 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Grundy County. No. 4940. Jeffrey F. Stewart, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Town and county election commission defendants appealed from the decision of the Chancery Court for Grundy County, Tennessee, which granted adjoining county plaintiff's motion for injunction enjoining election commission from certifying annexation referendum election results due to a constitutional infirmity and determined the place to hold the referendum annexation election in a multi-county municipality.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found that no constitutional infirmity was alleged or proved in the referendum, that a publication of the resolution was in substantial compliance with the statutory requirement, and that there was no evidence that anyone was misled by the publication. The appellate court disagreed with the lower court that plaintiff county had standing to bring its action solely because of its ownership of public roads in the area sought to be annexed; the territory in question was populated, albeit sparsely, as evidenced by the fact that twenty votes were cast, nineteen of which favored annexation. The appellate court also found that defendant town's city hall was the proper polling place, that the area sought to be annexed should have been considered and treated in its entirety, rather than as separate tracts or tax parcels. It also held that plaintiff county had no standing to contest the annexation vote since it did not seek a declaratory judgment and that defendant town accomplished the annexation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Texas Dep't of Children's Servs. v. M.A.D.


No. E2000-02501-COA-R3-JV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 359


April 10, 2001, Assigned on Briefs  
May 17, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Greene County. No. 13574. Thomas Wright, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee received custody of three children upon their parents' incarceration and prepared a plan designed to reunite them with appellant. Appellant did not comply with this plan, and appellee petitioned the Juvenile Court for Greene County (Tennessee) to terminate her parental rights. The trial court granted that petition, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The care plan agreed to by appellant to facilitate her children's return to her custody required her to (1) see that the children were adequately supervised in the care of others; (2) maintain safe, stable, and adequate housing; (3) refrain from criminal activity; (4) not associate with criminals; (5) participate in therapy; (6) complete drug addiction counseling; (7) obtain a GED; (8) complete parenting classes; (9) maintain stable employment; and (10) receive money management training. The trial court terminated appellant's parental rights because she abandoned the children by failing to pay support for four months, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(A)(I), failed to substantially comply with the care plan, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(2), and the children were removed from her home for more than six months and the conditions leading to removal persisted, with little likelihood of being remedied at an early date, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-113(g)(3). The first ground was unconstitutional, but clear and convincing evidence supported the trial court's finding of the second and third grounds, and termination was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed because although the statute it applied to find appellant abandoned her children was found unconstitutional, it correctly found appellant's failure to comply with the care plan and persistence of the conditions leading to the children's removal from her home, as well as termination being in the children's best interests.

State ex rel. Woodall v. D & L Co.


No. W1999-00925-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 357



May 16, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] An Appeal from the Chancery Court for Madison County. No. 54682. Charles O. McPherson, Special Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Madison County, Tennessee, declared defendants' adult entertainment club a public nuisance and permanently enjoined them from engaging in conduct resulting in a continuous public nuisance. Also, the trial judge ordered the property located on the premises forfeited to the State. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants operated an adult entertainment club. Jackson, Tennessee, Ordinances ch. 3, § 8-301 prohibited nude dancing where alcohol was sold, but defendants chose to ignore the law. The trial court issued a permanent injunction and found that the club constituted a public nuisance because the defendants engaged in the unlawful sale of intoxicating liquors and numerous incidents of fighting, public drunkenness, and other breaches of the peace occurred at the club. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the club was a nuisance and that it could properly enjoin defendants from operating an adult entertainment club on the premises. However, the injunction was modified because the trial court could not enjoin defendants from utilizing the premises for a purpose unrelated to the activities which created the nuisance. Additionally, the trial court's order for the forfeiture and public sale of all of the personal property and fixtures seized on the premises was lawful under the nuisance statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court found that defendants violated the nuisance statute, that the trial court properly enjoined them from operating a business on the premises that would be a public nuisance, and that the trial court properly ordered forfeiture of the property on the premises. The trial court's judgment was reversed in part because defendants could operate a business on the premises as long as it did not constitute a public nuisance.

Tillman v. Haffey


No. M2000-02196-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


63 S.W.3d 367; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 350



May 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 2001. Discretionary Appeal Denied October 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 00C-246. The Honorable Frank G. Clement, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn.R.App.P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, which dismissed appellant's malicious prosecution and abuse of process claims as barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a private investigator and author, retained appellees to locate publishers for works of fiction appellant intended to write. Appellees later sued appellant for breach of contract and unjust enrichment, among other things. They alleged appellant stalked and threatened them, shot or killed their dogs, vandalized their cars, and burglarized their home. After a court granted partial summary judgment to appellant as to the breach of contract and unjust enrichment claims, appellees voluntarily nonsuited the remaining claims. Appellant subsequently filed a complaint alleging malicious prosecution and abuse of process. She delayed service of process until a date after which appellees could no longer refile the dismissed claims. The trial court found appellant and her attorney had improperly withheld service of process and dismissed appellant's claims as barred by the statute of limitations. Judgment was vacated. Appellees' argument that appellant had to see that the summons was issued and served contemporaneously with the filing of the complaint was not in accord with Tennessee law. For statute of limitations purposes, an action still commenced upon filing of a complaint.


OUTCOME: Judgment was vacated and remanded; the Tennessee Rules of Civil Procedure did not mandate that appellant's summons be issued to appellees at the same time she filed her complaint. Plaintiff's claim was not barred by the statute of limitations, as the filing of the complaint commenced the action.

Summers v. Town of Walnut Grove

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town challenged the order of the Sumner County Circuit Court, Tennessee, granting summary judgment to plaintiffs, judicially dissolving its existence, and enjoining it from performing municipal functions such as collection of taxes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, residents of petitioner town, sought a declaratory judgment that the enabling statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-58-108 (f)(3) was unconstitutional as it applied to the town, judicial dissolution, and an injunction against the town against collecting taxes. The appeals court had previously declared the statute unconstitutional as applied to another town. Summary judgment was granted in plaintiffs' favor. Code Ann. § 2-17-105 applied only to election contests, not to actions for declaratory judgment; and the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 6-58-108(f)(3) had already been decided in a prior litigation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Phillips v. County of Anderson


No. E2000-01204-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 308



April 30, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Anderson County. No. 99CH7630. William E. Lantrip, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sued defendants, city and county, over defendants' proposed joint venture. The Chancery Court for Anderson County (Tennessee) granted defendants summary judgment. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county board of commissioners authorized defendant county to jointly finance with defendant city a public works project, and passed resolutions authorizing defendant county to incur indebtedness for funding. The initial resolution's caption erroneously stated that defendant county would make a loan agreement with the county public building authority. This error was corrected. Plaintiff sued. Summary judgment was granted defendants. The appellate court held that plaintiff showed no material fact to indicate he had standing to sue defendant city. Plaintiff made no prior demand to defendant city, and a letter to a state official did not qualify. Defendant county's actions did not constitute an illegal "giving of public credit" under Tenn. Const. art. II, § 29. Defendants' agreement was legally sufficient under the Industrial Park Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-16-201 et seq. (1999), in that it explicitly provided defendant city with development responsibility. Documents plaintiff alleged were fraudulent were not in the record. The resolutions did not call for expenditures prohibited under the Local Government Public Obligations Act of 1986, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 9-21-102 (Supp. 2000).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case remanded for collection of costs assessed below.

Hopkins v. State Bd. of Paroles & Prob.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County No. 00-281-II Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of aggravated rape. The Davidson County Chancery Court, Tennessee, twice denied him common law certiorari challenging the Tennessee Board of Paroles' refusal to grant him release. From the second denial, he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated rape. He filed an initial petition for certiorari to the trial court, challenging denial by the Board of Paroles (Board) on the grounds that a misrepresentation was made of a psychological examination. The Board agreed to a rehearing, and the court dismissed the petition. On rehearing, parole was again denied. Appellant again sought certiorari, which the court dismissed, granting the Board's motion under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12 (b)(6). From this dismissal, appellant sought review. The appeals court upheld dismissal. The Board was within its discretion in determining that appellant was not a good candidate for release, based on the seriousness of his underlying crime and that paroling him would have a substantially adverse effect on institutional discipline. Because parole decisions are fact intensive and focus on the individual prisoner seeking parole, the court refused to inquire into the intrinsic correctness of the order.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court denying certiorari was affirmed.

State ex rel. Bissonette v. Marland


No. E2000-02089-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 287



April 26, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Knox County No. A-6518 Hon. Carey E. Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Tennessee appealed the order of the Knox County Juvenile Court dismissing a paternity action.


OVERVIEW: A paternity action was filed by the State only to be dismissed upon motion by the defendant, putative father. The trial court agreed with his position that since a previous petition was dismissed for failure to prosecute and was not re-filed within one year, the action could not be revived. The State appealed and the court reversed. The statute of limitations had not run for the filing of the action regarding this child and the trial court erroneously relied upon the saving statute under Tenn. Code. Ann. § 28-1-105 (a). Neither the child's mother nor the State would have been precluded from filing another petition, because the previous petition had no res judicata effect. The action was properly filed by the State, and there was no evidence that it would be entitled to any different relief than the mother.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

In re Sierra Cheyenne Satterwhite


No. E2000-02107-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 257



April 17, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 99 A 023. W. Frank Brown, III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, maternal grandparents, filed for termination of mother's and appellant father's parental rights to their daughter. Default was entered against mother. The Chancery Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) ordered termination of appellant's parental rights. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The mother of appellant father's child became pregnant with the child while living at home. The mother's mother forbade her from contacting appellant. The child was born out of wedlock, always lived with her maternal grandparents, and they refused offers of help from the paternal grandparents. After appellant was released from jail, he married the mother of his child, but custody proceedings granted child custody to the maternal grandparents. Visitation was ordered. Child support was neither ordered nor paid. Appellant later divorced the mother and had other children. The maternal grandparents sought to adopt the child and filed for termination of appellant's and the mother's parental rights, which was granted. The appellate court affirmed. Seven factors clearly showed appellant's abandonment: (1) he earned some money; but (2) paid no support; (3) appellant only made Tenn. Code. Ann. § 36-1-102(1)(C) token visitation; (4) gave sporadic gifts; (5) appellant never had custody, never tried to legitimate his child; (6) she was separated from him all of her six and a half years; and (7) from the time of birth to the adoption petition, appellant had criminal problems and did drugs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the matter remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Zimmerman v. City of Memphis


No. W2000-01369-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


67 S.W.3d 798; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 241



April 5, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. Nos. 110024-3 & 98-0795-2; The Honorable D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) granting defendants summary judgment in their lawsuit challenging the validity a central business improvement district, arguing it was not a valid special assessment, but rather an unlawful tax.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city council established a Central Business Improvement District (CBID) to improve and assist development of a downtown area. Defendants held a meeting to debate the CBID creation, rate of assessment, method of apportionment, delegation of powers, and stated purposes of defendant center city commission as the district management corporation. The ordinance was approved and assessments were collected. Plaintiffs challenged the validity of the CBID, asserting multifarious error, including it was not a valid special assessment, but rather an unlawful tax. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment and plaintiffs appealed. The court held defendant city had the powers pursuant to the Central Business Improvement District Act of 1990 (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-84-501 et seq. to levy special assessments on all of the property owners in the CBID for the costs and expenses for all improvements within the CBID. The court affirmed, holding the special assessment levied had none of the characteristics of an unlawful tax and was established and valuations calculated within the Act.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because by its annual review of the proposed budget, defendant city council determined the costs and expenses to be paid by the special assessments and thereby complied with local taxing statutes. Further, defendants used a proper assessed value to determine benefits conferred upon each property in the district.

 

1384 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Lovelace v. Knoxville


No. E2000-01609-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 198



March 27, 2001, Decided  
March 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied September 17, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 673.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. Nos. 141142-3 and 141160-3. Hon. Sharon Bell, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owners of nightclubs, appealed an order of the Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee) affirming the constitutionality of an "anti-brown-bagging" ordinance prohibiting customers from bringing and consuming their own alcoholic beverages to a public establishment during certain hours, arguing the ordinance was void for vagueness and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city passed an ordinance prohibiting "brown-bagging," or allowing patrons to consume their own alcoholic beverages in a public establishment. Plaintiffs, nightclub owners, filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance, arguing it was void for vagueness and overbroad. The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendant. On appeal, the court extensively reviewed the ordinance and noted the test for vagueness was whether a statute was so vague that men of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning and differ as to its application. Moreover, the court held the overbreadth doctrine not only prohibited a statute from criminalizing constitutionally protected activity, but could also render a statute unconstitutional, if its sweep had a chilling effect upon constitutionally protected conduct. The court reversed in part, holding the notice provisions imposed on bar owners to notify patrons of when it was unlawful to possess an open container, and requiring that they enforce open displays of alcohol during certain hours failed to consider the bar owner's knowledge or intent and were unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part, because the notice provisions of the law imposed on bar owners to notify patrons of when it was unlawful to possess an open container was unconstitutionally vague, as well as the term "open display," which failed to consider the bar owner's knowledge or intent.

 

1385 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Valentine


No. W1999-01293-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 191



March 19, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] An Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County. No. G9269. George E. Blancett, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and mother, sought review of the orders of the Juvenile Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, that granted the petition of appellee Department of Children's Services to terminate their parental rights concerning their son.


OVERVIEW: Because he was abused by his mother, the child was placed in the custody of the Department of Children's Services, which drafted permanency plans to be met before he could be restored to his mother and father. Alleging that the plans were not complied with, the department filed a petition to terminate mother's and father's parental rights. The petition was granted, and mother and father appealed. The appellate court affirmed. While the elected judge of the county was not an attorney, the person appointed to hear the case was, so mother's and father's rights to have the termination case heard by a licensed attorney were not violated. Neither the Tennessee Constitution nor due process forbade having a nonelected juvenile court referee hear the termination case. Trial testimony showing that neither father nor mother complied with the permanency plan requirements or contributed to the child's support, that father repeatedly abused mother and took no steps to control this behavior, and that mother nonetheless maintained her relationship with father, constituted clear and convincing evidence to support the termination of their parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1386 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re Davis


No. W1999-01662-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 130



March 1, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County. No. 11439. The Honorable A. V. McDowell, Special Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn.R.App.P. 3; Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents sought review of a decision from the Juvenile Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) which terminated their parental rights due to abandonment as defined in Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-102(A).


OVERVIEW: Respondents' minor child had been removed from their home by the Department of Children's Services. Respondent father was in and out of jail and respondent mother had bipolar disorder. At a hearing, the juvenile court found that the minor child was dependent and neglected. The child's court appointed special advocate filed a petition for the termination of parental rights pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-1-113(g), 37-2-403(2). These rights were terminated, and the respondents appealed the decision. The decision of the lower court was affirmed. There was clear and convincing evidence to support the decision. The respondents had failed to visit with the minor child once during the four months prior to the hearing and had failed to supply any support to the child. In addition, there was proof that the respondents were unable to cooperate to the degree necessary to raise the minor child. The child's need for a safe and permanent home was more important than the respondents' interests in retaining parental rights.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed. There was clear and convincing evidence that terminating respondents' parental rights would be in the best interest of the minor child. The respondents had been unable to meet the requirements of the permanency plan to make it safe and in the minor child's best interest to return to her home.
