Fiser v. Town of Farragut


No. E1999-00425-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 118



February 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied July 2, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 548.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 127706-2. Daryl R. Fansler, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision made by the Chancery Court for Knox County (Tennessee) which upheld one of appellee's zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: When appellants bought the property in question, it was outside the city limits. It was zoned for commercial use. The only things on the undeveloped property were two billboards. When the property was annexed, the billboards were nonconforming, but grandfathered. Amendments were made to the city zoning ordinance which provided appellants with only three options: they could (1) keep the billboards and not develop the land, (2) develop the property and remove the billboards, or (3) develop the property and keep the billboards as long as they were on minimum one-acre sites. Appellants had sought a declaratory judgment that the new ordinance was invalid as to their property. The lower court determined the statute was valid as to their property. This judgment was reversed. In regards to the instant property, the ordinance amounted to an attempt to take appellants' land without just compensation. The court disagreed with appellee's reading of the state's grandfather statute, finding instead, that the billboards were protected by state law and could not be overturned by a city ordinance. It was arbitrary, capricious and unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed. The ordinance as applied in the instant case was unconstitutional. It constituted an attempt by appellees to appropriate appellants' land without just compensation.

 

1388 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Tennessee Dep't of Correction


No. M1999-02519-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 111



February 23, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Application for Permission to Appeal Denied June 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 98-2964-CH-00401. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant was convicted and sentenced to 30 years as a Class X felon for aggravated rape in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), he challenged appellee Tennessee Department of Correction's calculation of his sentence reduction credits. The trial court denied appellant's claim. Appellant challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of a Class X felony. He earned credits toward sentence reduction, but waived those credits with the enactment of the Class X Felony Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-101 et seq. Appellant argued the repeal of the Act made him eligible for honor time and good conduct credits under revived Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 41-332 (subsequently codified as Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-212 ) and 41-21-229. The appellate court found the earlier sentence credits statutes were not revived because previous statutes on sentence reduction were never found to be unconstitutional. Further, as a Class X felon, appellant was not eligible for the sentence reduction credits established in any statutes except Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-230, under which he received 10 credits and remained eligible until he signed the waiver, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 41-21-236, under which he had been earning credits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the cause remanded as appellant was not eligible for credits towards his sentence under the sentence reduction statutes.

 

1389 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Terry v. Botts


No. E2000-01288-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 103



February 22, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Scott County. No. 8642, Michael A. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Juvenile Court Dismissed; Cause Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees filed a petition in the Juvenile Court for Scott County (Tennessee) seeking grandparent visitation with the children of their deceased daughter under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306. The trial court granted the petition, over appellant's objection, and he sought review, arguing, inter alia, that the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: When appellant and his children's mother divorced, she received custody of the marital child they were aware of. She discovered she was pregnant, gave birth to twins, and died. Appellant's legitimation petition in juvenile court, seeking custody of the twins, was granted. He also received custody of the child previously born. The juvenile court's jurisdiction was limited by Tenn. Code Ann. 37-1-103 (Supp. 1998) to 10 types of proceedings, including delinquency, dependency and neglect, and paternity, which all involved the minor person directly. Grandparent visitation petitions were a lawsuit involving the grandparents and the parents of the children. While children were at the heart of that suit, it was the constitutional rights of the parent potentially being affected, rather than those of the children, so § 37-1-103 did not explicitly or by implication give the juvenile court jurisdiction over a grandparent visitation petition independent of its statutory jurisdiction. Once appellant's legitimation petition was finally adjudicated, it was illogical for the juvenile court to maintain jurisdiction over the children who were the subject of that petition.


OUTCOME: The trial court was reversed because it did not have jurisdiction over appellees' grandparent visitation petition. The trial court had limited, statutory jurisdiction which did not include appellees' petition explicitly or by implication. Appellees' petition involved a dispute between adults, rather than a case involving the minor person directly.

Vaccarella v. Vaccarella


No. M1999-01937-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


49 S.W.3d 307; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 81



February 9, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Applications for Permission to Appeal Denied July 2, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Chancery Court for Williamson County. No. 24634. Russ Heldman, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review from the judgment of the Chancery Court for Williamson County (Tennessee), which granted appellee wife's Tenn. R. Civ. P. 59 motion to vacate and set aside the parties' final decree of divorce, re-granted a divorce to the parties on the grounds of inappropriate marital conduct, and granted custody of the children to appellee.


OVERVIEW: After appellant husband and appellee wife reached a marital dissolution agreement, they were granted a divorce. Appellee wife filed a Tenn. R. Civ. P. 59 motion for relief, and the trial court vacated the original divorce decree and re-granted the parties' divorce, awarding custody of the children to appellee, along with child support. Appellant sought review and judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The trial court erred with regard to its interpretation and application of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-4-103 (1996) and its procedural requirements for granting a divorce on the grounds of irreconcilable differences. The original divorce decree substantially complied with § 36-4-103 and the parties were both represented by counsel and participated in mediation with a licensed and trained mediator. Consequently, it was an error to vacate the original divorce decree because there was no relevant change of law and no new evidence to indicate any injustice. However, a substantial change of circumstances warranted a modification of child custody and support, and the trial court's determination of child support was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. It was error to grant appellee's motion to alter or amend as a matter of law because there was no relevant change of law and no new evidence had become available. Therefore, there was no error of law or fact, nor any injustice, in the original decree. However, it was not error to modify child support based on the Tennessee Child Support Guidelines.

Trusty v. Robinson


No. M2000-01590-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 75



February 6, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Smith County. No. 4364B. Clara Byrd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Smith County Circuit Court (Tennessee) entered judgment for appellee lessor in an action for damages against appellant lessee and denied appellant's motion for a new trial. Appellant challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: When appellant moved out of the house leased from appellee, appellee was unhappy with its condition and sued appellant for damages. On appeal of the judgment for appellee, appellant lacked the financial resources to obtain a verbatim trial transcript, and failed to file a Tenn. R. App. P. 24(C) statement of evidence or proceedings. Neither of appellant's contentions, that it would have been futile to prepare a statement because the trial court would not have approved it or that the trial court should have prepared an order setting forth the necessary information, warranted excusing appellant from supplying an appellate record. Because none of appellant's alleged errors by the trial court or appellee's counsel were reflected in the technical record, the court affirmed the judgment. Because there was no adequate appellate record, there was never a reasonable chance that the appeal could succeed, and the court held that the appeal was frivolous.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because appellant failed to supply an appellate record and the technical record did not contain the errors appellant alleged. Case remanded to award appellee damages because without an appellate record, appellant's challenge to the trial court's judgment was frivolous.

Brown v. Rogers


No. M2000-01277-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 73



February 5, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. 33086. Don R. Ash, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee), which terminated his parental rights based on a finding that appellant had abandoned the children.


OVERVIEW: After mother died, appellant filed a petition asking for the immediate return of his children, and appellee stepfather filed a petition to terminate appellant's parental rights so the appellee could adopt the children. The trial court found that appellant had abandoned the children. Appellant sought review, and judgment was vacated and remanded because new information, with direct bearing, had surfaced after the trial proceeding. Appellant was willfully underemployed, not financially disabled, and by his own testimony confirmed that he had failed to support the children. Furthermore, the court was unpersuaded by appellant's attempts to convince the court that he was entitled to nurture his second family at the expense of his first. However, recent evidence of an order of the juvenile court found the subject children to be dependent and neglected and the children were placed in the custody of the deceased's father and stepmother. Appellee was only allowed supervised visitation. Consequently, the appellate court was unable to conclude that clear and convincing evidence established that it was in the children's best interest to terminate appellant's parental rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment was vacated and remanded for a determination of whether the evidence currently showed, by a clear and convincing standard, that termination of appellant father's parental rights was in the best interest of the two subject children. The children were now dependent and neglected and under the exclusive jurisdiction of the juvenile court.

Reid v. Lutche


No. M1997-00229-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 46



January 24, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 97-121-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged dismissal of his pro se petition for declaratory judgment and request for certiorari from the Davidson County Chancery Court (Tennessee), upon order that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction and appellant failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was disciplined for larceny by the prison disciplinary board. Appellant then filed a pro se action for declaratory judgment in the Chancery Court, alleging that the prison's internal grievance procedure was ineffective. He also requested judicial review of the board's action by either declaratory judgment or writ of certiorari. Appellee attorney general responded with a motion to dismiss, asserting that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction and that appellant failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, which was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed, reasoning that appellant had not alleged how any of his presently existing rights were affected by the operation of the inmate grievance procedure. Further, appellant had not demonstrated how he was harmed by a statute, rule, or order. Thus, dismissal for failure to state a claim was appropriate. The request for certiorari was further dismissed, since it was not timely filed within the statutory 60-day period.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed. Complaint failed to articulate viable declaratory judgment claim. The existence of the grievance process created no substantive rights for any particular prisoner. Further, his request for certiorari was untimely, as it was not filed within the statutory 60-day period.

 

1394 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Hines v. Tilimon


No. E2000-00912-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 35



January 19, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Knox County. No. 82554. Bill Swann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded with Instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the default judgment order of the Circuit Court for Knox County (Tennessee), (1) finding Tennessee to be his child's home state, (2) finding California lacked jurisdiction to adjudicate the child's custody, (3) domesticating foreign judgments from Ohio and Oklahoma, (4) limiting his visitation, and (5) awarding appellee attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Under the Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction Act (UCCJA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-201 et seq. (1996, repealed 1999, replaced by 1999 Tenn. Pub. Acts ch. 389), and 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738A(c)(2)(B) of the Parental Kidnapping Prevention Act, child custody was to be determined in a child's home state. A custody order not from the child's home state was not entitled to full faith and credit. The child's UCCJA home state had personal jurisdiction over the child's parents, without minimum contacts. Venue was proper in the trial court, and appellant was properly served with process. Appellant's argument Tenn. R. Civ. P. 4.05(5), allowing valid process service by registered mail where the addressee refuses delivery, was unconstitutional was not raised below, or was the attorney general notified. The trial court did not abuse discretion by denying appellant's continuance motion, his request to appear telephonically, his motion to set aside the default judgment, or by modifying visitation. Appellant's previous legal action in the state on the same subject matter subjected him to the trial court's personal jurisdiction, allowing it to order him to pay attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed because its jurisdiction was proper under the UCCJA, it was not required to give full faith and credit to the order of a court which did not have UCCJA jurisdiction, it did not abuse discretion, and it had personal jurisdiction over appellant sufficient to require him to pay attorney's fees.

 

1395 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mayhew v. Wilder


No. M2000-01948-COA-R10-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


46 S.W.3d 760; 2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 17; 29 Media L. Rep. 1225



January 11, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Applications for Permission to Appeal Denied March 19, 2001. Application for Permission to Appeal Denied April 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 00C1833. Hamilton V. Gayden, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state legislature appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) which overruled defendants' motion to dismiss an action brought by plaintiffs alleging defendants violated Tenn. Const. art. II, § 22, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8- 44-101, et seq., and the due process provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court granted defendants' Tenn. R. App. P. 10 application for permission to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant state legislature alleging that in deliberating budget and revenue bills toward passage, defendants held sessions that were closed to the public and to the press. Plaintiffs claimed that such secret meetings violated Tenn. Const. art. II, § 22, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8- 44-101, et seq., and the due process provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The trial court overruled defendants' motion to dismiss. The court reversed the judgment and entered an order dismissing the complaint. The court reasoned that the Tennessee Open Meetings Act did not apply to defendants, and even if it did, it would not, in the court's opinion, bind a subsequent Tennessee General Assembly. In addition, the decision to hold closed sessions was non-reviewable by the courts because it was a purely political question. Further, a legislator's immunity from suit when performing legislative duties prevented the courts from making defendants justify the decision to hold closed sessions. Finally, the court determined plaintiffs were not deprived of their liberty or property by defendants' actions; therefore, there could be no claim for a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, entered an order dismissing the complaint, and remanded the case for further proceedings because the Tennessee Open Meetings Act did not apply to defendant state legislature. Additionally, the right to liberty did not include the right to attend meetings of governmental bodies; thus, defendants' acts did not deprive plaintiffs of that right.

 

1396 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Stanley v. Hooper


No. M2000-00916-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2001 Tenn. App. LEXIS 20



January 11, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Juvenile Court for Dickson County. No. 04-99-009-M. A. Andrew Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Juvenile Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of the Juvenile Court for Dickson County (Tennessee), which found that appellant was the legal and biological father of appellee's minor child, in a suit to determine whether the juvenile court erred in denying appellant's demand for a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sued appellant to obtain a judgment of paternity and support payments for her minor child. A DNA paternity test established a 99.71 percent probability of paternity. The juvenile court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 24-7-112(b)(2)(B) entitled appellee to a conclusive presumption of paternity. On appeal, that statutory presumption was found to be unconstitutional and the case was remanded to allow appellant an opportunity to rebut the presumption. Appellee subsequently voluntarily non-suited the original paternity action. Several months later, appellee refiled the action. The juvenile court denied appellant's request for a jury trial and found that he was the legal and biological father of appellee's child. Appellant filed an appeal. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that, by virtue of Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-106(a) (Supp. 1990) (repealed 1997), appellant had at most an accrued statutory right to a jury in the original action, but that statutory right was not a vested right that would survive appellee's non-suit. Therefore, when appellee refiled the action, after § 36-2-106(a) had been repealed, appellant no longer had the right to demand a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's statutory right to a jury trial was not a vested right; thus, it did not survive appellee's non-suit of the original paternity action and her subsequent refiling of the action after the statute allowing for a jury trial had been repealed. The case was remanded, and costs on appeal were taxed to appellant.

 

1397 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


City of Chattanooga v. Davis


No. E2000-00664-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2000 Tenn. App. LEXIS 722



October 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected November 2, 2000. Rehearing Granted March 5, 2001. Application for Permission to Appeal Granted March 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 203.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 225103. Douglas A. Meyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed a judgment of the Hamilton County Criminal Court (Tennessee), which found three statutory provisions and city ordinance unconstitutional and/or invalid and fined appellee $ 50 for violation of a municipal ordinance against reckless driving.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, who was cited for reckless driving in violation of an ordinance, appeared in city court, where he pled guilty and was fined $ 300. He appealed to the county trial court, arguing that imposition of a fine exceeding $ 50 violated Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14. Trial court reduced the fine to $ 50, but it also declared the $ 300 fine violated Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 14. Trial court found that Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 6-54-306, 6-54-308, and 55-10-307 were unconstitutional, and it also found Chattanooga, Tenn., Code § 1-8 was invalid. The court upheld the $ 50 fine assessed against appellee, but it also concluded that the trial court erred in finding the statutes and the ordinance unconstitutional and/or invalid. The ordinance was not invalid merely because of the use of the term "punished," as the penalty imposed by the ordinance was a civil penalty; use of the term "punished" did not alter the civil nature of the penalty imposed. As to the ruling that Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-307 denied equal protection, the court concluded that a rational basis existed for the delegation of authority to enforce certain driving offenses.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment assessing a $ 50 fine was affirmed. That portion of the judgment declaring the statutory provisions and the city ordinance unconstitutional was reversed, and the case was remanded for entry of an order consistent with the opinion. Use of the term "punished" in ordinance did not render ordinance invalid, as the penalty imposed by the ordinance was a civil penalty.

Yother v. Yother


No. E2000-01046-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, EASTERN SECTION, AT KNOXVILLE


2000 Tenn. App. LEXIS 723


September 20, 2000, Assigned on Briefs  
October 31, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 95DR2802. Jacqueline E. Schulten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) which determined it was in the best interest of the parties' child for custody to be awarded to appellee and found that primary residential custody of the child should be changed to appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed a petition to modify seeking the custody of the parties' minor child. The trial court determined that it was in the best interest of the child for custody to be awarded to appellee. On appeal, appellant argued the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to modify the custodial arrangement. The court reversed the judgment, reasoning that while appellant waived any objection to a lack of personal jurisdiction over her by availing herself of the forum, her conduct did not confer subject matter jurisdiction upon the trial court to modify the custody award. Further, the court determined that under both Tennessee and Georgia law, Georgia was the home state of the child when appellee filed his petition seeking custody. Furthermore, there was no indication that the courts of Georgia declined to exercise jurisdiction in deference to Tennessee as the more appropriate forum. Accordingly, the court concluded the trial court did not have jurisdiction to modify the custody award pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-203(a)(2) or (3) (repealed 1999).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment because the trial court did not have jurisdiction to modify the custodial arrangement. Additionally, the court remanded the case to the trial court for entry of an order dismissing appellee's petition seeking custody of the parties' minor child.

 

1399 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Cunningham v. Cunningham


No. W1999-02054-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


2000 Tenn. App. LEXIS 713



October 20, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Cunningham v. Cunningham, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 13 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Madison County. No. 53334. Joe C. Morris, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the judgment of the Madison County Chancery Court (Tennessee) awarding appellee wife a divorce, distributing marital property, and awarding appellee alimony and child support.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment of divorce, contending that it erred in valuing property, distributing property, and determining his alimony and child support obligations. The court reversed the trial court's valuation of appellant's business on the ground that the trial court improperly included the business' goodwill in determining its value. Because the trial court incorrectly valued the business, the court reversed the alimony and marital property awards as they were partially based on the incorrect value of appellant's business. Appellant was entitled to a downward deviation from the guidelines for his child support obligation because evidence showed that appellant exercised 160 days of visitation with his daughter, rather than the 80 days relied upon by the guidelines. The trial court did not err by ordering a portion of appellant's monthly child support obligation be put into a college trust fund because appellant requested that the trial court establish such a fund.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed insofar as it determined the value of appellant's business, awarded appellee alimony and marital property, and ordered appellant pay child support as established by the child support guidelines. Judgment affirmed insofar as it ordered appellant to pay a portion of his child support obligation into a college trust fund.

 

1400 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Bryant v. Bryant


No. M1999-01280-COA-R3-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


2000 Tenn. App. LEXIS 664



October 10, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] A Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 97A-84. The Honorable Muriel J. Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted the petition for termination and adoption, filed by petitioners, finding that the termination of the parental rights for both parents was in the best interests of the children.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners brought a petition for the termination of respondent father's parental rights, and adoption. The trial court granted the petition for termination and adoption, finding the termination of the parental rights for both parents, was in the best interests of the children. On appeal, respondent argued whether there was clear and convincing evidence that respondent abandoned his children, and whether it was in the best interests of the minor children to terminate respondent's parental rights. The court affirmed the judgment, determining that the record evidenced an intent on respondent's part to avoid his parental responsibilities. Accordingly, the court found that there was clear and convincing evidence that respondent had abandoned his minor children, thereby establishing grounds for termination of his parental rights. Finally, the court concluded the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding of clear and convincing evidence that the termination of respondent's parental rights was in the best interest of the children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings because the record evidenced an intent on respondent father's part to avoid his parental responsibilities. Additionally, the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding of clear and convincing evidence that the termination of respondent's parental rights was in the best interest of the children.
